Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
The Quranic-Sunnah Foundation of Hanafi Qawaid for Iftaa
Introduction to the qawaid of iftaa rooted in Quranic principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic and Prophetic roots of the Hanafi qawaid for iftaa and apply the principle of istihsan in a fatwa scenario.

Core Idea
Hanafi qawaid for iftaa are rooted in Quranic ease and Prophetic practice, not mere reasoning.

Before diving into specific legal rulings, this lesson establishes the bedrock of the Hanafi mufti's methodology. The qawaid (maxims) that guide derivation, preference, and fatwa are not later inventions; they are drawn directly from the Quran and Sunnah. Understanding this foundation is essential for appreciating how the Hanafi school remains faithful to revelation while responding to changing circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary sources cited
Locate the Quranic verses and Prophetic hadith mentioned in the passage. Note how each supports the themes of ease and hardship removal.
The passage cites Quran 2:185 and 22:78, along with hadith on the cat's leftover water and 'Make things easy'.
2
Extract the key legal maxims
From the cited sources, identify the overarching principles: yusr (ease), raf‘ al-haraj (removal of hardship), and the sub-principles like necessity, custom, public interest, etc.
These form the qawaid kubra (major maxims) and wusta (intermediate principles) used in iftaa.
3
Understand istihsan as the mechanism
Recognize that the Hanafi school operationalizes these maxims through istihsan (juristic preference), which allows departing from strict qiyas when ease or other grounds demand.
Istihsan is not arbitrary; it is guided by the same Quranic and Sunnah values.
4
Recognize the role of qawaid in takhrij, tarjih, and ifta
See how these principles serve as the 'usul' for a mujtahid within the school, analogous to the absolute mujtahid's use of Quran, Sunnah, ijma, and qiyas.
The qawaid are the tools for deriving new rulings, preferring among existing ones, and issuing fatwas.

(۱) في سنن الترمذي ١ : ١٥٣ ، وقال: حسن صحيح، وسنن أبي داود ١: ٦٧، وموطأ مالك ۲۲:۱ (۲) في صحيح البخاري ٥: ٢٢٦٩ ، وصحيح مسلم ٣: ١٣٥٩، وغيرها. (۳) في صحيح البخاري ۱ : ۲۳ ( ٤ ) في صحيح البخاري ٧: ١٠١ ، وصحيح مسلم ٤ : ١٨١٣ ، وغيرها.
وهذه القواعد لرسم المفتي هي الأصول التي يرجع إليها المجتهد في المذهب في التخريج والترجيح والإفتاء، فهي تمثل قواعده التي يُعتمد عليها في التعامل مع الأحكام كما يتعامل المجتهد المطلق مع قواعد الأصول من القرآن والسنة والإجماع والقياس. وما بين أيدينا من هذا هو عبارة عن شذرات متفرقة وفوائد مذكورة هنا وهناك في كتب علماء الطبقات السابقة، وأوسعها عند المتقدمين كلام قاضي خان في مقدمة «فتاواه» المشهورة، وهي في أسطر معدودة. واهتم علماء هذه الطبقة بتقييد هذه الفوائد، بسبب توسّع العلوم، وكثرة الاختلاف مقارنة بما عند المتقدمين، وصاروا يصرحون بها كثيراً في مؤلفاتهم، مثل: الكادوري (ت ۸۳۲هـ) في مقدمة «جامع المضمرات شرح القدوري»، وابن قُطلُوبُغا (٨٧٩هـ) في مقدمة «التصحيح»، (۸۷۹هـ) وابن نجيم (ت۹۷۰ هـ) في «الأشباه» و«البحر الرائق»، والشرنبلالي (١٠٦٩هـ) في «المراقي» و «الشرنبلالية»، ولكن بقيت فوائد متفرّقة يخبر عنها عند الحاجة.
And ease: 'Allah intends for you ease and does not intend for you hardship' [Al-Baqarah 2:185], and removal of hardship: 'And He has not placed upon you in the religion any hardship' [Al-Hajj 22:78]. And the Prophetic Sunnah abounds with its applications, such as the hadith of the purity of the leftover water of a cat: 'It is not impure; it is from those who go around among you,' and his saying: 'Make things easy, do not make things difficult,' and his saying: 'Religion is ease,' and the saying of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her): 'The Messenger of Allah never chose between two matters except he chose the easier of them as long as it was not sin,' and others. And the speech of our imams regarding giving weight to the mufta bihi (the relied-upon opinion) often refers to consideration of its known principles: necessity, custom, public interest, change of times, need, and general prevalence. But they usually express them by istihsan (juristic preference), leaving analogy (qiyas) for these reasons which are the principles of this science; because fiqh cannot be applied without observing these principles, and the terminology of the scholars differs in expressing them. (1) Sunan al-Tirmidhi 1:153, said hasan sahih; Sunan Abi Dawud 1:67; Muwatta Malik 22:1. (2) Sahih al-Bukhari 5:2269; Sahih Muslim 3:1359, etc. (3) Sahih al-Bukhari 1:23. (4) Sahih al-Bukhari 7:101; Sahih Muslim 4:1813, etc.
And these rules of rasm al-mufti (the chart of the mufti) are the fundamentals to which the mujtahid within the school refers in takhrij (derivation), tarjih (preference), and ifta (issuing fatwas). They represent his principles relied upon in dealing with rulings just as the absolute mujtahid deals with the principles of usul from the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, and analogy. What is before us consists of scattered fragments and benefits mentioned here and there in the books of earlier generations of scholars, and the most extensive among the earlier scholars is the speech of Qadi Khan in the introduction to his famous 'Fatawa', which is in a few lines. And the scholars of this generation took care to record these benefits due to the expansion of sciences and the abundance of differences compared to the earlier ones, and they became frequent in stating them in their works, such as: al-Kaduri (d. 832 AH) in the introduction to 'Jami' al-Mudmarat Sharh al-Quduri', and Ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH) in the introduction to 'al-Tashih', and Ibn Nujaym (d. 970 AH) in 'al-Ashbah' and 'al-Bahr al-Raiq', and al-Shurunbulali (d. 1069 AH) in 'al-Maraqi' and 'al-Shurunbulaliyya', but scattered benefits remained that are reported when needed.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage, from the introduction of the editor Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, serves as a philosophical and methodological foundation for the study of 'Rasm al-Mufti'. The author first establishes that the legal maxims (qawaid) used in iftaa are not arbitrary but are deeply rooted in the primary sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunnah, and the practice of the early community. He cites key Quranic verses on ease (yusr) and removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj), which are two of the five major legal maxims (al-qawa'id al-kubra). He then supports this with Prophetic hadith, such as the purity of a cat's leftover water and the command 'Make things easy', as well as the general principle that religion is ease. The passage emphasizes that the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan (juristic preference) and the consideration of custom, necessity, public interest, change of times, and prevalent need is the practical manifestation of these Quranic and Sunnah principles. Istihsan is the mechanism by which the Hanafi jurists sometimes depart from strict qiyas (analogy) in favor of a ruling that better fulfills the objectives of the Law. The author notes that the terminology for these principles varies among scholars. He then defines the subject matter: the qawaid of rasm al-mufti are the principles that a mujtahid within the Hanafi school uses for derivation (takhrij), preference (tarjih), and fatwa. These principles are analogous to the usul al-fiqh (Quran, Sunnah, ijma, qiyas) used by an absolute mujtahid. The passage then gives a historical overview of how these qawaid were recorded, starting with scattered fragments in earlier works, then more systematically by later scholars like Qadi Khan, al-Kaduri, Ibn Qutlubugha, Ibn Nujaym, and al-Shurunbulali. This shows the development of the field of 'usul al-ifta' as a distinct discipline within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قواعد رسم المفتي (qawa'id rasm al-mufti): The fundamental principles that a Hanafi mujtahid relies upon when deriving rulings, giving preference among opinions, and issuing fatwas.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict qiyas in favor of a ruling that better serves the goals of the Shariah, based on considerations like ease, custom, necessity, or public interest.
التخريج والترجيح والإفتاء (al-takhrij wa al-tarjih wa al-ifta'): The three main tasks of a Hanafi mujtahid: deriving rulings from the madhhab's usul, preferring one opinion over others when the school has multiple views, and issuing the final fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary basis for the Hanafi legal maxims used in iftaa?
A) The rulings of the four rightly guided caliphs
B) The Quranic principles of ease and removal of hardship
C) The consensus of the later Hanafi scholars
D) The strict application of qiyas without exception

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawaid for iftaa are not arbitrary; they are grounded in the Quranic principles of ease and removal of hardship and the Prophetic practice, operationalized through istihsan.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Foundations of Rasm al-Mufti: Applying Fiqh to Reality
Introduces the subject and principles of Rasm al-Mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the foundational principles of Rasm al-Mufti and explain how they enable fiqh to adapt to changing times and customs.

Core Idea
Fiqh rulings adapt through custom, necessity, and change of time — Rasm al-Mufti codifies this dynamic adaptation.

This lesson introduces Rasm al-Mufti, the Hanafi science of fatwa-giving. It is not a static set of rules but a methodology that applies fiqh to reality, using principles like custom (urf), necessity (darura), and public interest (maslaha) to ensure justice and ease. The source passage explains how these foundations cause rulings to vary across eras and environments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of Rasm al-Mufti
Read the opening: 'What is meant by the rules of Rasm al-Mufti are the rules of issuing fatwas. It is a science that investigates how to apply fiqh to reality.' Recognize that Rasm al-Mufti is the methodology of ifta, not a set of substantive fiqh rules.
Contrast with fiqh itself: fiqh provides substantive rulings; Rasm al-Mufti guides how to apply them in changing contexts.
2
List the foundational principles
From the text: necessity (al-darura), need (al-haja), removal of hardship (raf al-haraj), facilitation (al-taysir), change of time (taghayyur al-zaman), custom (al-urf), and public interest (al-maslaha). These are the tools a mufti uses to adjust rulings.
These principles are derived from the Shari'ah's overarching goals (maqasid).
3
Explain why rulings vary across mujtahids and eras
The text states: 'All fiqh rulings are related to these matters, and they had a profound impact on their variation from one mujtahid to another, due to the differing environments and eras of jurists.' Understand that even a single mujtahid may change his opinion when encountering a new custom or necessity.
Ibn Abidin's quote supports this: '...if he were in a time of a new custom, he would say contrary to what he said initially.'
4
Recognize the mufti's need to know custom
The text explicitly mentions that knowledge of people's customs is a condition for ijtihad. A mufti must be aware of the social, economic, and moral realities of his time to apply fiqh correctly.
This is the key takeaway: Rasm al-Mufti demands contextual awareness, not blind adherence to old fatwas.

قال ابن عابدين : وكثير منها ما يُبَيِّنُه المجتهد على ما كان في عرفِ زمانه، بحيث لو كان في زمان العرف الحادث لقال بخلاف ما قاله أوّلاً ؛ ولهذا قالوا في شروط الاجتهاد : أنه لا بد فيه من معرفة عادات الناس. فكثير من الأحكام تختلفُ باختلافِ الزَّمان؛ لتغيّر عرف أهله، أو لحدوثِ ضرورة، أو فساد أهل الزمان، بحيث لو بقي الحكم على ما كان عليه أوّلاً للزم منه المشقة والضرر بالناس، ولخالف الشريعة المبنية على التخفيف والتيسير ودفع الضرر والفساد؛ لبقاء العالم على أتم نظام وأحسن إحكام
ومثاله :(٧٩) التزكية في العدالة إنَّ الحكم أنه لا تقبل إلا شهادة العدل، كما شهد القرآن قال : ممن ترضون من الشهداء} البقرة: ٢٨٢ ، والعرف يُساعدنا في معرفة العدل، ففي زمن أبي حنيفة : لم يحتج للتزكية في العدالة؛ لأنَّ النّاس عدول، أما في زمن الصاحبين فقد تغيّرت أحوال الناس، فنحتاج لتحقق علّة الحكم من العدالة بالتزكية، فمن لم يكن عدلاً لا تُقبل شهادته هذا هو الحكم، ولكن كيف نتعرّف على العدالة، حيث أمكن ذلك بالعرف.

For Professor Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj
Section Two: Study of the Poem
It contains the following requirements:
First Requirement: The Subject of the Poem 'Rasm al-Mufti':
What is meant by the rules of Rasm al-Mufti are the rules of issuing fatwas. It is a science that investigates how to apply fiqh to reality, and its foundations are necessity, need, removal of hardship, facilitation, change of time, custom, and public interest. All fiqh rulings are related to these matters, and they had a profound impact on their variation from one mujtahid to another, due to the differing environments and eras of jurists. This had a great effect on their differences in many rulings and branches, such that even a single jurist would retract many of his opinions and adopt others when exposed to a new environment different from the one he was in.
Ibn Abidin said: Many of them are explained by the mujtahid according to the custom of his time, such that if he were in a time of a new custom, he would say contrary to what he said initially. For this reason, they said regarding the conditions of ijtihad: It is necessary to know the customs of the people. Many rulings differ with the change of time due to the change of the custom of its people, or the occurrence of a necessity, or the corruption of the people of the time, such that if the ruling remained as it was initially, it would entail hardship and harm for the people, and it would contradict the Shari'ah based on alleviation, facilitation, and repelling harm and corruption, so that the world remains in the most complete order and best system.
An example of it (79): Tazkiyah (verification of integrity) regarding 'adalah (justice). The ruling is that only the testimony of a just person is accepted, as the Qur'an states: 'from those you approve as witnesses' (al-Baqarah 2:282). Custom assists us in knowing who is just. In the time of Abu Hanifah, tazkiyah was not needed for 'adalah because people were just. But in the time of the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the conditions of people changed, so we need to verify the 'illah of the ruling of 'adalah through tazkiyah. So whoever is not just, his testimony is not accepted—that is the ruling, but how do we identify 'adalah? That is possible through custom.
Another example (80): Fulfillment of the intended purpose of the sold item regarding khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection). The option of inspection is established for one who has not seen the intended purpose of the sold item until full satisfaction is achieved. So in
(1) In Nashr al-'Urf 2:123.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is part of a modern study on Ibn Abidin's poem 'Rasm al-Mufti'. It introduces the discipline of fatwa rules (usul al-ifta), clarifying that it is the science of applying fiqh to real-world situations. The author, Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, states that the foundations of this science include necessity, need, removal of hardship, facilitation, change of time, custom, and public interest. These principles cause variations in rulings among mujtahids due to differing environments. Even a single mujtahid may change his opinion when encountering a new custom. Ibn Abidin is quoted supporting this: rulings change with custom, necessity, or corruption of people; otherwise, hardship would result, contradicting the Shari'ah's aim of ease. Two examples are given. First, tazkiyah (verification of justice) for testimony: In Abu Hanifah's time, people were presumed just, so tazkiyah was unnecessary. But when society changed in the time of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), tazkiyah became necessary. Custom determines how justice is verified. Second, khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection): This option is granted to a buyer who has not seen the item to ensure full satisfaction, with custom defining when the option applies. The footnote references a standard Hanafi work on custom.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): The rules and methodology of issuing fatwas, focused on applying fiqh to changing realities.
العدالة (al-'Adalah): Justice or uprightness of a witness, a condition for testimony acceptance.
خيار الرؤية (Khiyar al-Ru'ya): Option of inspection: the buyer's right to rescind a sale after seeing the item if it does not meet expectations.
العرف (al-Urf): Custom or common practice; a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-ifta that influences the application of rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT listed as a foundational principle of Rasm al-Mufti in the passage?
A) Necessity (al-darura)
B) Facilitation (al-taysir)
C) Ijma (consensus)
D) Custom (al-urf)

Key Takeaway
Rasm al-Mufti is the dynamic methodology that allows Hanafi fiqh to remain relevant through time by incorporating custom, necessity, and change, ensuring rulings facilitate rather than burden.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Custom’s Impact on Ijtihad: The Tazkiyah Example
Example illustrating how custom changes the application of a fixed ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of custom-based ijtihad to evaluate why Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn differed on the requirement of tazkiyah for testimony.

Core Idea
Custom determines how a fixed Shar'i condition is verified—when society changes, the method of verification changes.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf over whether witnesses need formal verification of integrity (tazkiyah) before testimony is accepted. The disagreement did not arise from a different reading of the Quranic text but from a change in societal moral standards. This case brilliantly illustrates how custom (urf) acts as a dynamic factor in Hanafi ijtihad, a key principle of Rasm al-Mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fixed Shar'i ruling
The Quran (2:282) requires that witnesses be 'just' (mman tardawna min al-shuhada). This is a fixed condition: only the testimony of a just person is accepted.
The text itself is clear; the point of difference is not the condition but its verification.
2
Understand how custom assists in applying the ruling
Custom (urf) helps in identifying who is just. In Abu Hanifah's time, society was generally upright, so people were presumed just. No further verification (tazkiyah) was needed.
This reflects the maxim 'al-asl fi al-muslim al-adalah' (the default for a Muslim is integrity).
3
Recognize the change in custom
In the time of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), societal conditions deteriorated. People could no longer be presumed just, so tazkiyah became necessary to verify integrity.
The same Quranic condition remained, but the practical method of fulfilling it changed.
4
Analyze the ijtihadi difference
The difference is not a disagreement on the hukm (ruling) itself, but on the wasila (means) to implement it. Both positions are valid ijtihads based on the custom of their respective eras.
This shows that ikhtilaf can arise from changing external circumstances, not just textual interpretation.
5
Generalize to the mufti's responsibility
A mufti today must assess the moral and social context of his time when applying such rulings. He cannot blindly follow the older opinion if the custom has changed.
This is the core of Rasm al-Mufti: contextual application of fiqh.

وتتضمن المطالب الآتية:
المطلب الأول: موضوع المنظومة «رسم المفتي»:
والمقصود بقواعد رسم المفتي هو قواعد الإفتاء، فهو علم يبحث في كيفية تطبيق الفقه في الواقع، وأصوله هي الضرورة، والحاجة، ورفع : الحرج، والتيسير، وتغيّر الزمان، والعرف، والمصلحة، وعامة الأحكام الفقهية متعلقة بهذه الأمور، فكان لها تأثيرها البالغ في اختلافها من مجتهد إلى مجتهد، بسبب اختلاف بيئات الفقهاء وعصورهم، فقد كان لذلك أثر كبير في اختلافهم في كثير من الأحكام والفروع، حتى إنَّ الفقيه الواحد كان يرجع عن كثير من أقواله إلى أقوال أُخرى إذا تعرّض لبيئة جديدة تُخالف البيئة التي كان فيها.
قال ابن عابدين : وكثير منها ما يُبَيِّنُه المجتهد على ما كان في عرفِ زمانه، بحيث لو كان في زمان العرف الحادث لقال بخلاف ما قاله أوّلاً ؛ ولهذا قالوا في شروط الاجتهاد : أنه لا بد فيه من معرفة عادات الناس. فكثير من الأحكام تختلفُ باختلافِ الزَّمان؛ لتغيّر عرف أهله، أو لحدوثِ ضرورة، أو فساد أهل الزمان، بحيث لو بقي الحكم على ما كان عليه أوّلاً للزم منه المشقة والضرر بالناس، ولخالف الشريعة المبنية على التخفيف والتيسير ودفع الضرر والفساد؛ لبقاء العالم على أتم نظام وأحسن إحكام
ومثاله :(٧٩) التزكية في العدالة إنَّ الحكم أنه لا تقبل إلا شهادة العدل، كما شهد القرآن قال : ممن ترضون من الشهداء} البقرة: ٢٨٢ ، والعرف يُساعدنا في معرفة العدل، ففي زمن أبي حنيفة : لم يحتج للتزكية في العدالة؛ لأنَّ النّاس عدول، أما في زمن الصاحبين فقد تغيّرت أحوال الناس، فنحتاج لتحقق علّة الحكم من العدالة بالتزكية، فمن لم يكن عدلاً لا تُقبل شهادته هذا هو الحكم، ولكن كيف نتعرّف على العدالة، حيث أمكن ذلك بالعرف.
ومثال آخر :(٨٠) : تحقق المقصود من المبيع في خيار الرؤية: إنَّه يثبت خيار الرؤية لمن لم ير المقصود من المبيع حتى يتحقق تمام الرّضا، ففي

For Professor Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj
Section Two: Study of the Poem
It contains the following requirements:
First Requirement: The Subject of the Poem 'Rasm al-Mufti':
What is meant by the rules of Rasm al-Mufti are the rules of issuing fatwas. It is a science that investigates how to apply fiqh to reality, and its foundations are necessity, need, removal of hardship, facilitation, change of time, custom, and public interest. All fiqh rulings are related to these matters, and they had a profound impact on their variation from one mujtahid to another, due to the differing environments and eras of jurists. This had a great effect on their differences in many rulings and branches, such that even a single jurist would retract many of his opinions and adopt others when exposed to a new environment different from the one he was in.
Ibn Abidin said: Many of them are explained by the mujtahid according to the custom of his time, such that if he were in a time of a new custom, he would say contrary to what he said initially. For this reason, they said regarding the conditions of ijtihad: It is necessary to know the customs of the people. Many rulings differ with the change of time due to the change of the custom of its people, or the occurrence of a necessity, or the corruption of the people of the time, such that if the ruling remained as it was initially, it would entail hardship and harm for the people, and it would contradict the Shari'ah based on alleviation, facilitation, and repelling harm and corruption, so that the world remains in the most complete order and best system.
An example of it (79): Tazkiyah (verification of integrity) regarding 'adalah (justice). The ruling is that only the testimony of a just person is accepted, as the Qur'an states: 'from those you approve as witnesses' (al-Baqarah 2:282). Custom assists us in knowing who is just. In the time of Abu Hanifah, tazkiyah was not needed for 'adalah because people were just. But in the time of the Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the conditions of people changed, so we need to verify the 'illah of the ruling of 'adalah through tazkiyah. So whoever is not just, his testimony is not accepted—that is the ruling, but how do we identify 'adalah? That is possible through custom.
Another example (80): Fulfillment of the intended purpose of the sold item regarding khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection). The option of inspection is established for one who has not seen the intended purpose of the sold item until full satisfaction is achieved. So in
(1) In Nashr al-'Urf 2:123.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is part of a modern study on Ibn Abidin's poem 'Rasm al-Mufti'. It introduces the discipline of fatwa rules (usul al-ifta), clarifying that it is the science of applying fiqh to real-world situations. The author, Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, states that the foundations of this science include necessity, need, removal of hardship, facilitation, change of time, custom, and public interest. These principles cause variations in rulings among mujtahids due to differing environments. Even a single mujtahid may change his opinion when encountering a new custom. Ibn Abidin is quoted supporting this: rulings change with custom, necessity, or corruption of people; otherwise, hardship would result, contradicting the Shari'ah's aim of ease. Two examples are given. First, tazkiyah (verification of justice) for testimony: In Abu Hanifah's time, people were presumed just, so tazkiyah was unnecessary. But when society changed in the time of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), tazkiyah became necessary. Custom determines how justice is verified. Second, khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection): This option is granted to a buyer who has not seen the item to ensure full satisfaction, with custom defining when the option applies. The footnote references a standard Hanafi work on custom.

Key Terms
التزكية (al-Tazkiyah): Verification of the integrity ('adalah) of a witness, often through inquiry or certification.
العدالة (al-'Adalah): Justice or uprightness of a witness, a condition for testimony acceptance.
الصاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two Companions of Abu Hanifah: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major Hanafi jurists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Sahibayn require tazkiyah for witnesses, according to the passage?
A) They disagreed with Abu Hanifah on the Quranic verse.
B) Because people's moral condition had deteriorated.
C) Because tazkiyah is mandatory in all times.
D) Because the Quran explicitly requires tazkiyah.

Key Takeaway
A fixed Shari'i condition can be implemented differently when custom changes, and a mufti must consider current societal context to apply the ruling correctly.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
12 min
Fatwa Changes with Custom and Time – The Dynamic Application of Rulings
Explaining that fatwa changes with custom to prevent hardship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule that fatwa adapts to changing custom ('urf) to prevent hardship, and apply this rule to analyze the practical differences among Hanafi jurists in the examples of tazkiyah and khiyar al-ru'yah.

Core Idea
A fatwa is not static; its application changes with custom to avoid hardship.

This passage from Ibn 'Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti lays a foundational principle for the practice of ifta': the mujtahid must consider the custom of his time when issuing fatwas. Ibn 'Abidin illustrates this with two classic Hanafi examples showing how the same ruling is applied differently due to changing social conditions. Understanding this principle is essential for any mufti to keep fiqh alive and relevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central principle
Ibn 'Abidin states that rulings differ with time due to change in custom, necessity, or corruption. The ruling itself remains constant, but its practical application adapts.
The ruling (hukm) is fixed; the method of implementation changes.
2
Examine the first example (tazkiyah)
The ruling is that only a just witness is accepted. In Abu Hanifah's time, people were assumed just, so no formal verification. In the Sahibayn's time, due to moral decline, verification became necessary.
The 'illah (cause) is knowing the witness's justice; custom determines how to realize it.
3
Examine the second example (khiyar al-ru'yah)
The buyer has the option to return an unseen item. In Abu Hanifah's time, viewing the courtyard sufficed; in Zufar's time, entering rooms was required.
The 'illah is knowing the intended benefit; custom defines what counts as 'seeing'.
4
Understand the role of 'urf as a means to ascertain the 'illah
Custom does not change the ruling but helps identify how to fulfill the cause (e.g., verifying 'adalah or seeing the item).
Al-'urf is a tool for application, not a source of new rulings.
5
Apply the principle to a new case
Use the same method: identify the fixed ruling, identify the changing custom, and determine how the application should adapt.
This skill is crucial for modern nawazil (new incidents).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابن عابدين : وكثير منها ما يُبَيِّنُه المجتهد على ما كان في عرفِ زمانه، بحيث لو كان في زمان العرف الحادث لقال بخلاف ما قاله أوّلاً ؛ ولهذا قالوا في شروط الاجتهاد : أنه لا بد فيه من معرفة عادات الناس. فكثير من الأحكام تختلفُ باختلافِ الزَّمان؛ لتغيّر عرف أهله، أو لحدوثِ ضرورة، أو فساد أهل الزمان، بحيث لو بقي الحكم على ما كان عليه أوّلاً للزم منه المشقة والضرر بالناس، ولخالف الشريعة المبنية على التخفيف والتيسير ودفع الضرر والفساد؛ لبقاء العالم على أتم نظام وأحسن إحكام. ومثاله :(۷۹) التزكية في العدالة إنَّ الحكم أنه لا تقبل إلا شهادة العدل، كما شهد القرآن قال : ممن ترضون من الشهداء} البقرة: ۲۸۲ ، والعرف يُساعدنا في معرفة العدل، ففي زمن أبي حنيفة : لم يحتج للتزكية في العدالة؛ لأنَّ النّاس عدول، أما في زمن الصاحبين فقد تغيّرت أحوال الناس، فنحتاج لتحقق علّة الحكم من العدالة بالتزكية، فمن لم يكن عدلاً لا تُقبل شهادته هذا هو الحكم، ولكن كيف نتعرّف على العدالة، حيث أمكن ذلك بالعرف. ومثال آخر :(۸۰) : تحقق المقصود من المبيع في خيار الرؤية: إنَّه يثبت خيار الرؤية لمن لم ير المقصود من المبيع حتى يتحقق تمام الرّضا، ففي عرف أبي حنيفة : يُمكن معرفة الدَّار بالنَّظر إليها من ساحتِها بدون الدخول في غرفها؛ لأنَّ الدُّورَ في زمنه متشابهة، وفي زمن زُفر : لم تعد الدُّور متشابهة، فلا يُمكن الوقوف على المقصودِ منها إلا بالدخول في غرفِ الدَّار ، فالحكمُ ثابت - وهو ثبوتُ الخيار - حتى يقف على المقصودِ من المبيع، والعلة هي التحقق من المقصود من المبيع، والعرف عرَّفنا أنَّ العلة في زمن أبي حنيفة تتحقق بالنَّظر من الساحة، وفي زمن زُفر : بدخول الغرف. وهذا العلم ينبغي أن ينال اهتماماً كبيراً من المشتغلين في الفقه، فلا سبيل لنا للترجيح بين الأقوال الفقهيّة إلا به، ولا فهم الخلاف الحاصل بين علماء المذهب إلا من خلاله، ولا إعمال الفقه في الواقع بدونه، فهو أقرب ما يكون بالرّوح للفقه؛ إذ بدونه لا حياة له. وفي ظنِّي أنّ هذا التراجعَ الذي حَصَلَ لعلم الفقه في هذا الزمان حتى أصبح علماً نظرياً في حياتنا الاقتصادية والاجتماعية والسياسية والعسكرية والقضائية لهو عائد لأمرين: ١ . ترك الدراسة المتعمقة المتمكنة في الفقه. ٢.إهمال علم رسم المفتي، فمن لم يضبطه ويُدركه لن يتمكّن من تطبيق الفقه واختيار الأنسب للواقع وفهم كيفية التعامل معه.
Ibn 'Abidin said: Many of them (rulings) are clarified by the mujtahid according to the custom of his time, such that if he were in a time of new custom, he would rule contrary to what he said initially. Hence they said regarding the conditions of ijtihad: it is necessary to know the customs of people. For many rulings differ with the difference of time, due to change in custom of its people, or occurrence of necessity, or corruption of the people of the time, such that if the ruling remained as it was initially, hardship and harm would befall the people, and it would contradict the Shari'ah which is built on alleviation, facilitation, and repelling harm and corruption, to keep the world in the most perfect system and best order. Example (79): Tazkiyah in 'adalah: The ruling is that only the testimony of a just person is accepted, as the Quran said: 'from those you are pleased with as witnesses' (2:282). Custom helps us in knowing the just person. In the time of Abu Hanifah: there was no need for tazkiyah (formal verification of justice) because people were just. In the time of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the conditions of people changed, so we need to verify the cause of the ruling of 'adalah through tazkiyah. So whoever is not just, his testimony is not accepted. This is the ruling, but how do we ascertain 'adalah? That is possible through custom. Another example (80): Realizing the intended benefit of the sold item in the option of inspection: The option of inspection is established for one who did not see the intended benefit of the sold item until complete satisfaction is realized. In the custom of Abu Hanifah: one can know the house by looking at its courtyard without entering its rooms, because houses in his time were similar. In the time of Zufar: houses were no longer similar, so one cannot ascertain the intended benefit except by entering the rooms. So the ruling is constant – the establishment of the option – until one ascertains the intended benefit of the sold item, and the cause is the verification of the intended benefit. Custom has informed us that the cause in the time of Abu Hanifah is realized by looking from the courtyard, and in the time of Zufar by entering the rooms. This knowledge should receive great attention from those engaged in fiqh, for there is no way for us to give preference among juristic opinions except through it, nor understanding of the disagreement among scholars of the madhhab except through it, nor application of fiqh to reality without it. It is most like the soul of fiqh; without it there is no life. In my opinion, this decline that has befallen the science of fiqh in this time, until it became a theoretical science in our economic, social, political, military, and judicial lives, is due to two things: 1. Abandoning deep, firm study of fiqh. 2. Neglecting the science of Rasm al-Mufti. Whoever does not master and comprehend it will not be able to apply fiqh and choose what is suitable for reality and understand how to deal with it.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage from Ibn 'Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti establishes a foundational rule for issuing fatwas: rulings are not static but adapt to changing customs, necessities, and times. The mujtahid must be aware of the 'urf (custom) of his era; if customs change, the application of the ruling may change to avoid hardship and contradict the Shari'ah's principles of ease and harm prevention. Two concrete examples illustrate this. First, tazkiyah (verification of a witness's probity): the ruling that only a just witness is accepted remains constant, but the method of verifying justice changed from Abu Hanifah's time (where people were assumed upright) to later times (where formal inquiry became necessary). Second, the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah): the buyer's right to return an unseen item is fixed, but what constitutes 'seeing' the item depends on custom—in Abu Hanifah's time, viewing a house's courtyard sufficed, while in Zufar's time, entering rooms was required. Ibn 'Abidin then stresses that understanding this dynamic is essential for preferring between juristic opinions, grasping intra-madhab disagreements, and applying fiqh to reality. He laments that contemporary decline in practical fiqh stems from abandoning deep study and neglecting the science of Rasm al-Mufti.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Custom or prevalent practice of a particular time and place that affects the application of legal rulings.
التزكية (al-tazkiyah): Formal verification of a witness's moral probity ('adalah) through inquiry or declaration.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The buyer's option to rescind a contract upon seeing the item if it was not seen before sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Abidin, why did the application of tazkiyah change from the time of Abu Hanifah to the time of his students?
A) A new Quranic verse was revealed.
B) People's moral state changed, requiring formal verification.
C) The students disagreed with the Imam on principle.
D) The ruling of accepting only just witnesses was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa must adapt to changing custom and time to fulfill the Shari'ah's goal of preventing hardship, while the underlying ruling remains constant.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Custom and the Evolution of Legal Causes: The Science of Rasm al-Mufti
Explaining how custom changes legal causes and the importance of rasm al-mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept that custom ('urf) can change the application of a legal cause (illah) without altering the cause itself, and explain the importance of rasm al-mufti in bridging fiqh and reality.

Core Idea
Custom changes how a fixed cause is fulfilled, so the mufti must know his time.

This passage uses the example of khiyar al-ru'yah to show that while the legal cause (illah) remains constant (verifying the intended object of sale), the method of fulfilling it changes with custom. It then emphasizes that the science of rasm al-mufti—understanding the rules of issuing fatwas—is essential for applying fiqh to changing realities and for weighing between differing opinions within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal cause (illah)
Determine the constant legal cause that both Abu Hanifa and Zufar agree upon. In the example, it is verifying the intended object of sale (al-tahaqquq min al-maqsud min al-mabi').
The illah is derived from the purpose of khiyar al-ru'yah.
2
Observe how custom affects fulfillment of the cause
See how Abu Hanifa and Zufar differed in applying the cause: Abu Hanifa held that looking from the courtyard suffices because houses were uniform; Zufar required entering rooms because houses became varied. Custom changed the method of fulfilling the same illah.
Custom does not change the illah; it changes how the illah is realized.
3
Analyze the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Zufar
Note that the dispute is not over the ruling itself but over its application. Both used the same cause. The difference arose from differing customs in their times.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf based on time and custom.
4
Recognize that the illah remains constant
The author stresses that the ruling is established (thabit) until the cause is fulfilled. The cause is always verifying the intended object; only the means change.
This is a key principle in rasm al-mufti.
5
Appreciate the role of rasm al-mufti
Understand that rasm al-mufti is the science that enables a mufti to weigh opinions, understand ikhtilaf, and apply fiqh to contemporary reality. Without it, fiqh becomes theoretical.
The author calls for it to be an independent discipline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عرف أبي حنيفة : يُمكن معرفة الدَّار بالنَّظر إليها من ساحتِها بدون الدخول في غرفها؛ لأنَّ الدُّورَ في زمنه متشابهة، وفي زمن زُفر : لم تعد الدُّور متشابهة، فلا يُمكن الوقوف على المقصودِ منها إلا بالدخول في غرفِ الدَّار ، فالحكمُ ثابت - وهو ثبوتُ الخيار - حتى يقف على المقصودِ من المبيع، والعلة هي التحقق من المقصود من المبيع، والعرف عرَّفنا أنَّ العلة في زمن أبي حنيفة تتحقق بالنَّظر من الساحة، وفي زمن زُفر : بدخول الغرف. وهذا العلم ينبغي أن ينال اهتماماً كبيراً من المشتغلين في الفقه، فلا سبيل لنا للترجيح بين الأقوال الفقهيّة إلا به، ولا فهم الخلاف الحاصل بين علماء المذهب إلا من خلاله، ولا إعمال الفقه في الواقع بدونه، فهو أقرب ما يكون بالرّوح للفقه؛ إذ بدونه لا حياة له. وفي ظنِّي أنّ هذا التراجعَ الذي حَصَلَ لعلم الفقه في هذا الزمان حتى أصبح علماً نظرياً في حياتنا الاقتصادية والاجتماعية والسياسية والعسكرية والقضائية لهو عائد لأمرين: ١ . ترك الدراسة المتعمقة المتمكنة في الفقه. ٢.إهمال علم رسم المفتي، فمن لم يضبطه ويُدركه لن يتمكّن تطبيق الفقه واختيار الأنسب للواقع وفهم كيفية التعامل معه. من لذلك أقول: إنَّ دراسة الفروع كما مَرَّ تُكوّن (٥٠) من علم الفقيه، و (٥٠) هي قواعد رسم الإفتاء، وهي على قسمين: جانب نظري لقواعد الإفتاء يمثل (٢٥) من علم الفقه كما هو في المنظومة التي بين أيدينا، وجانب عمليّ: وهو المعرفة الحقيقية المتبصرة بالواقع الذي يريد الإفتاء به وتنظيمه وترتيبه على أجمل طريقة وأحسن سلوك تمثل (۲٥) من علم الفقه؛ لذلك كَثُرَ قوهم: «مَن لم يكن عالماً بأهل زمانه فهو جاهل». دو وهذا العلم يُمثل الحلقة ما بين المسائل الفقهية المدوّنة في الكتب وما بين الواقع المعاش للنّاس في كافة مناحي الحياة، فمن فقده فهو فاقد للعلم حكماً؛ إذ لا خير في علم بلا عمل، وفاقده فاقد للعمل به لنفسه ولغيره. وأحوج ما نحتاج إليه في هذه الأيام هو إظهار رسم المفتي في علم مستقل له قواعده وأسسه ومبادئه، متيسّر الدراسة لكل المتفقهة، ويكون أحد البرامج المقرّرة في المدارس الشرعيّة وكليات الشريعة، وبدون ذلك سنبقى في دراستنا الشرعيّة أقرب إلى النظرية من التطبيق. وهذا العلم هو الأصول التي يعتمد عليها المجتهد في المذهب في الترجيح والتفريع والتطبيق والإفتاء، كما يعتمد المجتهد المستقل على (1) ينظر : رد المحتار ٢ : ٤٧ .
Abu Hanifa's custom: The house can be known by looking at it from its courtyard without entering its rooms, because houses in his time were similar. In Zufar's time: houses were no longer similar, so it is not possible to ascertain the intended object except by entering the rooms of the house. So the ruling is established—which is the establishment of the option—until one ascertains the intended object of the sale. The cause (illah) is verifying the intended object of the sale. Custom informed us that the cause in Abu Hanifa's time is fulfilled by looking from the courtyard, and in Zufar's time by entering the rooms. This science should receive great attention from those engaged in fiqh. There is no way for us to weigh between fiqh opinions except through it, nor to understand the disagreement among scholars of the madhhab except through it, nor to apply fiqh in reality without it. It is the closest thing to the spirit of fiqh; without it, fiqh has no life. In my opinion, this decline that happened to the science of fiqh in this time, such that it became a theoretical science in our economic, social, political, military and judicial life, is due to two things: 1. Abandoning deep, thorough study of fiqh. 2. Neglecting the science of rasm al-mufti. Whoever does not master and comprehend it will not be able to apply fiqh, choose what is most suitable for reality, and understand how to deal with it. Therefore I say: The study of branches (furu'), as mentioned, constitutes 50% of the jurist's knowledge, and 50% are the rules of rasm al-ifta'. They are of two types: a theoretical aspect of the rules of ifta', representing 25% of fiqh knowledge as in the poem (manzumah) before us, and a practical aspect: true insightful knowledge of the reality for which one intends to issue fatwas, organizing and arranging it in the best way and finest conduct, representing 25% of fiqh knowledge. Hence their statement became abundant: 'Whoever is not knowledgeable about the people of his time is ignorant.' This science represents the link between the fiqh issues recorded in books and the living reality of people in all spheres of life. Whoever lacks it is effectively lacking knowledge, for there is no good in knowledge without action, and one who lacks it lacks acting upon it for himself and others. What we need most in these days is to present rasm al-mufti as an independent science with its own rules, foundations, and principles, accessible to all students of fiqh, and to make it one of the prescribed programs in religious schools and colleges of shari'ah. Without that, we will remain in our religious studies closer to theory than application. This science is the principles upon which the mujtahid within the madhhab relies for tarjih (preference), tafri' (derivation), application, and ifta', just as the independent mujtahid relies on (1) See: Radd al-Muhtar 2:47.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a modern commentary on the importance of the science of rasm al-mufti, using the example of the option of inspection (khiyar al-ru'yah) to illustrate how custom (‘urf) affects the application of legal rulings. The author, Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj, explains that Abu Hanifa ruled that merely looking at a house from its courtyard sufficed to exercise the option of inspection, because houses in his time were uniform. Later, Zufar ruled that one must enter the rooms because houses became differentiated. Both rulings share the same cause (illah): ascertaining the intended object of sale. The change in ruling came from the change in custom, not from a change in the illah itself. The author then emphasizes that rasm al-mufti—the science of issuing fatwas—is crucial for correctly weighing between opinions, understanding intra-madhhab differences, and applying fiqh to reality. He identifies two causes of the decline of applied fiqh: superficial study and neglect of rasm al-mufti. He further breaks down the jurist's knowledge into 50% furu' (substantive law) and 50% rules of ifta', subdivided into theoretical (25%) and practical (25%) components. The practical part requires deep understanding of the contemporary context. The passage ends by calling for rasm al-mufti to be taught as an independent discipline in Islamic schools and colleges.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The science of issuing fatwas, covering the rules, principles, and methods by which a mufti derives and delivers legal rulings appropriate to time and place.
العلة (al-illah): The legal cause or effective reason that grounds a ruling; here, it is verifying the intended object of sale.
العرف (al-urf): Custom or common practice of the people, which can change the application of a ruling without changing the underlying cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did Zufar rule that one must enter the rooms of a house when exercising the option of inspection, while Abu Hanifa ruled that looking from the courtyard suffices?
A) Zufar disagreed with the underlying cause (illah) of the ruling.
B) Custom changed: houses in Zufar's time were no longer uniform, so entering rooms became necessary to ascertain the intended object.
C) Abu Hanifa's ruling was abrogated by later consensus.
D) Zufar required a stricter standard for all sales.

Key Takeaway
The legal cause (illah) remains constant, but its practical fulfillment changes with custom; thus a mufti must know his time.

Rasm al-Mufti: The Mufti's Methodology
Explains Rasm al-Mufti's role analogous to Usul al-Fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three major axes of Rasm al-Mufti and explain how they function analogously to Usul al-Fiqh for the absolute mujtahid.

Core Idea
Just as Usul al-Fiqh empowers the absolute mujtahid, Rasm al-Mufti equips the mufti with darurah, 'urf, and taysir.

This lesson introduces the foundational philosophy of Rasm al-Mufti as articulated by Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj. You will see how the mufti's methodology mirrors that of an absolute mujtahid, but with its own unique axes that enable the application of fiqh to new realities, resolution of disagreements, and meeting community needs within the Hanafi madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Analogy
Recognize that the passage draws a direct parallel between Usul al-Fiqh for the absolute mujtahid and Rasm al-Mufti for the mufti within the madhhab. Both are sets of rules that enable their respective practitioners to perform their work.
Usul al-Fiqh uses Book, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas. Rasm al-Mufti uses darurah, 'urf, taysir.
2
Extract the Purpose of Rasm al-Mufti
From the passage, list the four functions: applying fiqh to reality, exiting from the circle of disagreement (khuruj min da'irat al-khilaf), and meeting the needs of the community.
Rasm al-Mufti is a tool for the mufti to do his work, just as Usul is a tool for the mujtahid.
3
List the Three Major Axes
The passage explicitly names them: al-darurah (necessity), al-'urf (custom), and al-taysir (ease). These are the 'major principles' (al-usul al-kubra) of Rasm al-Mufti.
Memorize these three axes.
4
Understand Each Axis
Darurah permits deviation from standard rulings to prevent harm; 'urf allows custom to influence rulings when no text contradicts; taysir seeks facilitation, rooted in Qur'anic ease.
These axes are not arbitrary but correspond to key Hanafi principles.
5
Recognize the Framework
The passage emphasizes that Rasm al-Mufti is a distinct discipline with its own rules, not mere repetition. The mufti must exert effort (badhl al-juhd) using these axes.
This refutes the misconception that a madhhab-bound mufti needs no methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للأستاذ الدكتور صلاح أبو الحاج
أصول الفقه لاستخراج الأحكام من الكتاب والسنة والآثار والترجيح بينها، فكما لا غنى للمجتهد المطلق عن أصول الفقه ـ فهي القواعد التي تمكنه من القيام بعلمه واستفراغ جهده في استنباط الأحكام، وهي آلته في ذلك ـ فكذلك العالم في المذهب، فإن رسم المفتي هي الأداة التي يتمكن بها من القيام بعمله، وبذل جهده في إنزال الفقه على الواقع، والخروج من دائرة الخلاف، وتلبية حاجات مجتمعه، فهي الوسيلة لذلك.
وكما أنَّ أُصول المجتهد المطلق تدور في محاور رئيسية فيها العديد من القواعد الأصولية وهي: الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والقياس، فكذلك فإنَّ أصول المجتهد في المذهب لها محاور رئيسية مليئة بقواعدِ الإفتاء، وهذه المحاور هي الضرورة والعرف والتيسير، فهذه هي الأصول الكبرى في رسم المفتي التي يرتكز عليها المفتي في فهمه وضبطِهِ وتطبيقه للفقه.
For Professor Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj. Usul al-Fiqh is to derive rulings from the Book, the Sunnah, the Athar, and to weigh between them. Just as the absolute mujtahid cannot do without Usul al-Fiqh – for they are the rules that enable him to perform his knowledge and exert his effort in deriving rulings, and they are his tool for that – likewise the scholar within the madhhab: indeed, Rasm al-Mufti is the tool by which he is able to perform his work, exert his effort in applying fiqh to reality, exit from the circle of disagreement, and meet the needs of his community. It is the means for that. And just as the Usul of the absolute mujtahid revolve around major axes containing many usuli rules, namely: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, likewise the Usul of the mujtahid within the madhhab have major axes filled with rules of ifta. These axes are: necessity (ḍarūrah), custom (ʿurf), and ease (taysīr). These are the major principles in Rasm al-Mufti upon which the mufti relies in his understanding, his control, and his application of fiqh.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage establishes the foundational philosophy of Rasm al-Mufti. The author draws a precise analogy: just as Usul al-Fiqh provides the absolute mujtahid (al-mujtahid al-muṭlaq) with the rules (qawāʿid) to extract rulings from primary sources (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), Rasm al-Mufti provides the mufti within the Hanafi madhhab with the rules to apply the established fiqh to new situations, resolve apparent conflicts, and meet community needs while remaining within the madhhab. The three 'major axes' (al-uṣūl al-kubrā) of Rasm al-Mufti are: darurah (necessity), 'urf (custom), and taysir (ease). These are not arbitrary but correspond to the three major principles that allow the mufti to adapt rulings without abandoning the madhhab framework. The passage emphasizes that the mufti's work is not mere repetition but a disciplined effort (badhl al-juhd) requiring a distinct methodology.

Key Terms
رسم المفتي (rasm al-muftī): The set of rules and principles that enable a mufti within the Hanafi madhhab to issue fatwas, apply fiqh to reality, and navigate differences.
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid muṭlaq): An independent jurist capable of deriving rulings directly from primary sources without adherence to a particular madhhab.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): A jurist who operates within the Hanafi madhhab, relying on its principles and precedents to derive rulings for new cases.
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): Necessity that permits deviation from a standard ruling to prevent harm; one of the three major axes of Rasm al-Mufti.
عرف (ʿurf): Custom or prevalent practice that can influence legal rulings when no textual evidence contradicts it; a major axis of Rasm al-Mufti.
تيسير (taysīr): Ease or facilitation; the principle that the law aims to ease hardship, a major axis guiding muftis in issuing fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The Book, the Sunnah, Ijma
B) Necessity (ḍarūrah), custom (ʿurf), ease (taysīr)
C) Qiyas, istihsan, maslahah
D) Ijtihad, taqlid, talfiq

Key Takeaway
Rasm al-Mufti equips the mufti with darurah, 'urf, and taysir to apply fiqh to new realities while staying within the madhhab.

The Mufti's First Duty: Following Zahir al-Riwayah
Initial ruling on the mufti's duty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufti's primary obligation to follow Zahir al-Riwayah and identify its sources, distinguishing it from other levels of Hanafi authority.

Core Idea
The mufti must base his fatwa on the well-known narrations, not on rare views.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle of Hanafi ifta: the mufti is obliged to issue fatwas based on Zahir al-Riwayah, the established transmissions from the school's founding Imams recorded in six core books. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the obligation
Identify that the passage states an obligation (wajib) upon the mufti to follow a specific source.
The term 'wajib' indicates a binding duty, not merely recommended.
2
Define Zahir al-Riwayah
Explain that Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the well-known, widely transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
These are recorded in six books authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Identify the six books
List the six core books: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
These form the primary source for Hanafi fatwa.
4
Distinguish from other sources
Contrast Zahir al-Riwayah with nawadir (rare transmissions) and later fatawa, which are secondary.
The mufti may only depart from Zahir al-Riwayah for a preponderant reason.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation to Follow the Preponderant Opinion (Rajih) in Fatwa
Opening rule of fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a mufti must follow the rajih opinion, identify the exceptions for the marjuh, and apply the principle to avoid arbitrary fatwa selection.

Core Idea
The mufti must follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion; the marjuh (weaker) opinion is practically non-existent in fatwa.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule of Hanafi fatwa methodology: the mufti is obligated to follow the preponderant opinion (rajih) within the madhhab. The opening verses of Ibn 'Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti declare this as wajib (obligatory), supported by scholarly consensus and a hadith. Understanding this principle is essential for any mufti or student to issue correct and reliable fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Recognize that the first substantive line of the poem states 'اعلم بأنَّ الواجب اتباع ما ترجيحه' — know that it is obligatory to follow what has been preponderated. This establishes a clear ruling: it is wajib for a mufti to follow the rajih opinion.
The ruling is taken from the matn (text) itself.
2
Understand Key Terms: Rajih and Marjuh
Define rajih as the preponderant opinion based on evidence and transmission strength, and marjuh as the outweighed opinion. The commentary stresses that the marjuh has no consideration ('لا عبرة به') and is like non-existence.
These terms are central to the hierarchy of Hanafi rulings.
3
Examine the Evidence (Dalil)
The passage cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn al-'As about the judge's reward, which supports that truth is one and that ijtihad, even when mistaken, is rewarded. This underscores the need to adhere to the preponderant view, as it is most likely the truth.
The dalil is used to justify the obligation, not to prove the specific ruling directly.
4
Note the Exception for Marjuh
Ibn 'Abidin's commentary adds 'except in some places' (إلا في بعض المواضع). This indicates that the marjuh can only be used in exceptional circumstances, such as extreme necessity or where later preponderance changes.
These exceptions are rare and must be carefully verified.
5
Apply the Principle
As a mufti, when multiple opinions exist in the madhhab, you must identify the rajih through the works of tarjih (e.g., the works of later Hanafi masters) and issue fatwa accordingly. Avoiding tatabbu' al-rukhas (following concessions) is critical.
This prevents inconsistency and preserves madhhab integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ثمّ الصَّلاة والسَّلامُ سَرمداً
على نبي قد أتانا بالهدى

(۱) أي: العلامة التي تدل المفتي على ما يفتي به، ينظر: رد المحتار ١ : ٦٩ . (۲) ومعناه: لا يجوز العمل بغير الراجح في المذهب، والمرجوح في مقابل الراجح لا عبرة به ولا يعتمد عليه إجمالاً، قال ابن عابدين في الشرح ص ٢٤٩: «الواجب على من أراد أن يعمل لنفسِهِ، أو يُفتي غيرَه، أن يُتَّبَعَ القول الذي ربَّحُه علماء مذهبه، فلا يجوز له العمل أو الإفتاء بالمرجوح، إلا في بعض المواضع، وقال ابن الصلاح في أدب المفتي والمستفتي ص واعلم من يكتفي بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة ويعمل بما شاء مِنَ الأقوال أو الوجوه مِنْ غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع»، وقال ابن قطلوبغا في التصحيح ق ١ أ : اتباع الهوى حرام، والمرجوح في مقابلة الرّاجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجّح في المتقابلات ممنوع». ودليل هذه المسألة : أنَّ الحقّ عند الله الله واحد ، وهو قول أهل السنة؛ فعن عمرو بن العاص قال : إذا حكم الحاكم فاجتهد ثم أصاب فله أجران، وإذا حكم فاجتهد ثم أخطأ فله أجر
In the name of God, the Lawgiver of rulings. Then blessings and peace perpetually upon the Prophet who brought us guidance, and upon his Family and noble Companions. After this, the poor sinful servant Muhammad ibn 'Abidin seeks the success of his generous, One Lord and acceptance in his aims. A radiant unique poem and a jeweled system I have named 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' needed by the practitioner or the one who gives fatwa. And now I begin the objective, seeking aid from the overflow of the sea of generosity. Know that it is obligatory to follow that whose preponderance is known from its people, or that which is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) and they did not prefer its contrary, so know. (1) i.e., the sign that indicates to the mufti what he should give fatwa upon. See: Radd al-Muhtar 1:69. (2) Its meaning: It is not permissible to act upon other than the preponderant (rajih) in the madhhab, and the outweighed (marjuh) in comparison to the rajih has no consideration and is not relied upon in general. Ibn 'Abidin said in the commentary p.249: 'It is obligatory upon whoever wants to act for himself or give fatwa to others to follow the saying that the scholars of his madhhab have preponderated. It is not permissible for him to act or give fatwa by the marjuh except in some places.' Ibn al-Salah said in Adab al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti: 'Know that whoever is content that his fatwa or action agrees with a saying or a viewpoint in the issue and acts upon whatever sayings or viewpoints he wishes without considering preponderance, has indeed been ignorant and violated consensus.' Ibn Qutlubugha said in al-Tashih folio 1a: 'Following whim is forbidden, and the marjuh in comparison to the rajih is like non-existence, and preponderance without a preponderating factor in opposites is prohibited.' The evidence for this issue: that the truth with Allah is one, and it is the statement of Ahl al-Sunnah; for from 'Amr ibn al-'As: 'When a judge makes a ruling, exerts his effort and then is correct, he has two rewards; and when he makes a ruling, exerts his effort and then errs, he has one reward.'
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage opens the poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' with an invocation and then states the foundational rule of fatwa methodology: the mufti must follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion within the Hanafi madhhab. The term 'zahir al-riwaya' refers to the well-known transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani as collected in the six authoritative works. The commentary by Ibn 'Abidin and others emphasizes the absolute necessity of adhering to the rajih; the marjuh (weaker opinion) is considered negligible unless in exceptional cases. The evidence cited includes the hadith of 'Amr ibn al-'As about the judge's reward, which supports that the truth is singular and that ijtihad is rewarded even if mistaken, but only the correct view is the truth. However, in fiqh, the mufti must follow the view that is preponderant in his school, not any opinion. This rule prevents arbitrary choice ('tatabbu' al-rukhas') and ensures consistency.

Key Terms
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion in the madhhab, determined by scholars through evidence and strength of transmission.
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The outweighed or weaker opinion that is not to be relied upon for fatwa or action except in rare exceptions.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known, transmitted rulings from the founding imams, forming the core of Hanafi fiqh (the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is always permissible as long as it is an opinion of a Hanafi scholar.
B) It is forbidden unless there is a specific necessity (darurah) or exceptional circumstance.
C) It is recommended if the marjuh opinion is easier for the questioner.
D) It is allowed only if the mufti also mentions the rajih opinion.

Key Takeaway
The mufti must adhere to the rajih; the marjuh is not to be used except in exceptional cases.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Obligation to Follow the Preponderant Opinion and Two Methods to Identify It
Explaining obligation to follow rajih and methods to identify it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two methods for determining the rājiḥ (preponderant) opinion in the Hanafi school and apply them to evaluate which opinion is muftā bihi.

Core Idea
Only the rājiḥ may be followed; the marjūḥ is void except in exceptional cases.

This passage establishes a foundational rule for muftīs: one must follow the preponderant opinion within the Hanafi school. It refutes the notion that any opinion can be chosen arbitrarily and explains how to identify the rājiḥ through two clear methods. Understanding this rule is essential for anyone issuing fatwa or teaching within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Read the opening lines: it is wājib to follow the rājiḥ. Note the proof from the hadith of ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ and the refutation of the Muʿtazilī position.
Focus on the phrase 'الحق عند الله واحد' – truth with Allah is one.
2
Distinguish the two methods
The passage explicitly lists two methods: (1) tarjīḥ from a qualified mujtahid in the school, and (2) inclusion in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless later scholars have overridden it.
Method two is not absolute; later scholars like al-Hidāyah may change the preference.
3
Understand the authority of later scholars
Ibn ʿĀbidīn explains that later scholars are more knowledgeable of the school, so their tarjīḥ is binding. This overrides even Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah when they differ.
Examples: author of al-Hidāyah, Qāḍī Khān.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a scenario
Given a fatwa request, identify which opinion is rājiḥ by applying the two methods. Then determine if any later scholar has given a different preference.
Practice with the sample scenario in the application bridge.
5
Evaluate the Muʿtazilī comparison
Contrast the Hanafi position with the Muʿtazilī taṣwīb view. Understand why the Hanafi position is necessary to maintain discipline in iftā.
The passage warns that disregarding tarjīḥ leads to chaos.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم بأنَّ الواجب اتباع ما ترجيحه عن أهله قد عُلما
أو كان ظاهر الرواية ولم يرجحوا خلاف ذاك فاعلم
(۱) أي: العلامة التي تدل المفتي على ما يفتي به، ينظر: رد المحتار ١ : ٦٩ . (۲) ومعناه: لا يجوز العمل بغير الراجح في المذهب، والمرجوح في مقابل الراجح لا عبرة به ولا يعتمد عليه إجمالاً، قال ابن عابدين في الشرح ص ٢٤٩: «الواجب على من أراد أن يعمل لنفسِهِ، أو يُفتي غيرَه، أن يُتَّبَعَ القول الذي رجحه علماء مذهبه، فلا يجوز له العمل أو الإفتاء بالمرجوح، إلا في بعض المواضع، وقال ابن الصلاح في أدب المفتي والمستفتي ص واعلم من يكتفي بأن تكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة ويعمل بما شاء مِنَ الأقوال أو الوجوه مِنْ غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع»، وقال ابن قطلوبغا في التصحيح ق ١ أ : اتباع الهوى حرام، والمرجوح في مقابلة الرّاجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجّح في المتقابلات ممنوع». ودليل هذه المسألة : أنَّ الحقّ عند الله واحد ، وهو قول أهل السنة؛ فعن عمرو بن العاص قال : إذا حكم الحاكم فاجتهد ثم أصاب فله أجران، وإذا حكم فاجتهد ثم أخطأ فله أجر» في صحيح مسلم ١ : ١٣٤ ، فالقائلون بعدم الأخذ بالقول الراجح والاختيار كما يريدون واقعون في مذهب المعتزلة في تعدد الحق، وهذا مهلكة.
وَذُكِرَ طريقان لمعرفة الرَّاجح، وهما:
١ . أن يكون الترجيح صادراً مِنْ أهل الاجتهاد في المذهب، فلا يعتد بترجيح من ليس من أهل الترجيح، وهذا صريح بيَّنْ مِنْ خاتمة المحققين ابنِ عابدين بأنَّه لا يجوز الخوض في الترجيح بين الأقوال في المذهب الواحدِ إلا لمن له أهلية النظر في ذلك، بأن بلغ مرتبةً مِنَ الاجتهادِ تمكنه منه؛ لأنَّه ضرب اجتهاد، فكيف بمَن يُرجِّحُ بين المذاهب وهو ليس من أهلها، قال ابنُ الهمام: «والتحقيقُ أنَّ المفتي في الوقائع لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس»، ينظر رد المحتار ۲ : ۳۹۸ وهذا يوقعنا في قول المعتزلة : أنَّ الحقِّ عند الله متعدد، وهو ما يغفل عنه، حيث يختار من الأقوال ما يشاء من غير ترجيح، فالله المستعان.
٢ . أن يكون مذكوراً في كتب ظاهر الرواية، فهذا ترجيح له من محمد بن الحسن بذكر القول في ظاهر الرواية، إلا إذا وجدناهم رجّحوا غير ما في ظاهر الرواية، فإننا نعمل بترجيحهم؛ لأنهم لم يعدلوا عنه إلا لأسباب: كتغيّر العرف والحرج والضرورة، واللازم في حق المفتي والمدرّس قول المجتهد في المذهب لا قول المجتهد المطلق. قال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار ۱ : ۱۹۲ : ولا يخفى أنّ المتأخرين ... كصاحب «الهداية» وقاضي خان وغيرهما مِنْ أهل الترجيح هم أعلمُ بالمذهب منّا، فعلينا اتباع ما رجّحوه وما صححوه كما لو أفتونا في حياتهم».
Know that the obligatory is to follow what is preponderant according to its people, or what is in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless they have given preponderance to something else. (1) i.e., the sign that indicates to the mufti what he gives fatwa upon. (2) Its meaning: It is not permitted to act upon other than the preponderant in the school, and the preponderated in comparison to the preponderant has no consideration nor is it relied upon in general. Ibn ʿĀbidīn said in the commentary: “It is obligatory upon whoever wants to act for himself or give fatwa to others to follow the saying that the scholars of his school have given preponderance, and it is not permissible for him to act or give fatwa by the preponderated, except in some places.” And Ibn al-Ṣalāḥ said in Adab al-Muftī: “Whoever is content that his fatwa or action agrees with a saying or a wajh in the issue and acts with what he wishes of sayings or wujūh without consideration of preponderance, then he is ignorant and has breached consensus.” And Ibn Qutlūbughā said: “Following desires is forbidden, and the preponderated in comparison to the preponderant is like non-existence, and preponderance without a preponderating factor among opposites is prohibited.” The proof of this issue is that the truth with Allah is one, and it is the statement of Ahl al-Sunnah; from ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ: “When a judge makes a ruling and strives and is correct, he has two rewards; and when he strives and errs, he has one reward.” [Ṣaḥīḥ Muslim 1:134]. So those who do not take the preponderant opinion and choose as they wish fall into the school of the Muʿtazila regarding the multiplicity of truth, and this is destructive. And two methods were mentioned for knowing the preponderant: 1. That the preponderance comes from those qualified for ijtihād within the school, so the preponderance of one who is not from the people of tarjīḥ is not considered. This is clearly evident from the seal of the muḥaqqiqīn Ibn ʿĀbidīn: it is not permitted to engage in tarjīḥ between sayings within a single school except for one who has the capacity for that, by reaching a level of ijtihād that enables him to do so, because it is a form of ijtihād. How then can one who is not from its people give preponderance between schools? Ibn al-Humām said: “The reality is that the mufti in events must have a form of ijtihād and knowledge of people’s conditions.” [See: Radd al-Muḥtār 2:398]. And this lands us in the statement of the Muʿtazila that truth with Allah is multiple, which is something he neglects, as he chooses from sayings what he wishes without preponderance. So Allah is the One sought for help. 2. That it is mentioned in the books of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, so this is a preponderance given to it by Muḥammad ibn al-Ḥasan by mentioning the saying in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, unless we find that they gave preponderance to something other than what is in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, then we act by their preponderance; because they did not turn away from it except for reasons: like change of custom, difficulty, and necessity. And what is required for the mufti and teacher is the saying of the mujtahid within the school, not that of the absolute mujtahid. Ibn ʿĀbidīn said in Radd al-Muḥtār 1:192: “It is not hidden that the later scholars... like the author of al-Hidāyah, and Qāḍī Khān, and others among the people of tarjīḥ are more knowledgeable of the school than us, so we must follow what they have given preponderance and what they have deemed correct, just as if they had given us fatwa during their lives.”
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a foundational rasm al-mufti rule establishing the obligation to follow the preponderant (rājiḥ) opinion within the Hanafi school. The author opens by declaring that it is obligatory to follow what has been given preponderance by the school's authorities, or what appears in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless the later scholars have preferred otherwise. He then cites Ibn ʿĀbidīn, Ibn al-Ṣalāḥ, and Ibn Qutlūbughā to emphasize that acting upon the marjūḥ (preponderated) opinion is generally prohibited, with only limited exceptions. The proof is the hadith of ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ that a judge is rewarded even if he errs, but the key point is that truth in God's view is one—contrary to the Muʿtazilī position that every mujtahid is correct. Therefore, arbitrarily choosing from many opinions without tarjīḥ is impermissible. The passage then explains two methods to identify the rājiḥ: (1) it must come from a qualified mujtahid within the school (not a mere layman), and (2) it may be indicated by its inclusion in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, the six books of Muḥammad al-Shaybānī. However, if later authoritative scholars like the author of al-Hidāyah have changed the preference, we follow them—due to changes in custom, hardship, or necessity. The passage concludes that the mufti and teacher must follow the opinion of a mujtahid within the school, not an absolute mujtahid, and that later scholars like the authors of al-Hidāyah and Qāḍī Khān are the authorities to follow.

Key Terms
الراجح (al-rājiḥ): The preponderant opinion within the Hanafi school, determined by qualified scholars or by inclusion in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah when later scholars have not overridden it.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muḥammad al-Shaybānī (al-Mabsūṭ, al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr, al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr, al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr, al-Siyar al-Kabīr, al-Ziyādāt) which contain the primary transmitted rulings of the school.
الاجتهاد في المذهب (al-ijtihād fī al-madhhab): The ability to derive rulings within the Hanafi school by weighing evidence from its canonical texts and principles, short of absolute ijtihād.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two methods to identify the rājiḥ (preponderant) opinion?
A) Personal preference and following the majority of later scholars
B) The ruling must be from a qualified mujtahid within the school, or it must be found in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah unless later scholars gave preference to another
C) The ruling must be from the Quran and Sunnah directly, or from the consensus of the Companions
D) The mufti may choose any opinion as long as it is attributed to a Hanafi scholar

Key Takeaway
The mufti must follow the rājiḥ opinion, identified either by qualified tarjīḥ or by inclusion in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah subject to later override.
