Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Two Ways to Determine the Preferred Opinion
Explains the two methods for identifying the preponderant opinion within the Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two methods for determining the preponderant opinion in the Hanafi madhhab and apply the rules for when later scholars may override Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Tarjih in the Hanafi school requires qualified ijtihad; Zahir al-Riwayah carries initial weight but later scholars may adjust for custom and necessity.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti outlines the two fundamental ways to identify which opinion is preponderant (rajih) within the Hanafi school. As a mufti or teacher, knowing these methods is essential for issuing correct fatwas. The first method emphasizes that only qualified mujtahids can perform tarjih, while the second points to the authority of Zahir al-Riwayah books. Let's explore these rules and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two methods
Identify that the passage presents two distinct ways to recognize the rajih: (1) via the tarjih of a qualified mujtahid within the school, and (2) via mention in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah.
The passage uses 'وذُكِرَ طريقان' to explicitly introduce the two methods.
2
Examine the first method: qualification for tarjih
Analyze the condition that tarjih must come from a mujtahid fil-madhhab. Note Ibn Abidin's emphasis that this requires 'a degree of ijtihad' and that tarjih is a form of ijtihad itself.
Contrast this with absolute ijtihad; the passage quotes Ibn al-Humam on the mufti's need for a 'type of ijtihad'.
3
Examine the second method: Zahir al-Riwayah
Understand that an opinion recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad is considered to have his tarjih. However, note the exception for later scholars (mutakhkhirin) who may prefer another opinion.
The reasons for deviation are 'change of custom, hardship, necessity'.
4
Understand the authority hierarchy
Synthesize that the later scholars' tarjih overrides Zahir al-Riwayah because they are 'more knowledgeable of the madhhab'. This establishes a dynamic hierarchy where Zahir al-Riwayah is primary but not final.
Ibn Abidin's quote at the end solidifies this: we must follow the tarjih of the later scholars as if they gave fatwa in our time.
5
Apply to a hypothetical fatwa scenario
Consider a case where the mufti finds conflicting opinions: one in Zahir al-Riwayah and one preferred by later scholars. Apply the rule that the later tarjih is followed, provided there is a valid reason (custom, hardship, necessity).
This step reinforces the practical binding nature of the rule for muftis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذُكِرَ طريقان لمعرفة الرَّاجح، وهما: ١ . أن يكون الترجيح صادراً مِنْ أهل الاجتهاد في المذهب، فلا يعتد بترجيح من ليس من أهل الترجيح، وهذا صريح بيَّنْ مِنْ خاتمة المحققين ابنِ عابدين بأنَّه لا يجوز الخوض في الترجيح بين الأقوال في المذهب الواحدِ إلا لمن له أهلية النظر في ذلك، بأن بلغ مرتبةً مِنَ الاجتهادِ تمكنه منه ؛ لأنَّه ضرب اجتهاد، فكيف بمَن يُرجِّحُ بين المذاهب وهو ليس من أهلها، قال ابنُ الهمام: «والتحقيقُ أنَّ المفتي في الوقائع لا بد له من ضرب اجتهاد ومعرفة بأحوال الناس»، ينظر رد المحتار ۲ : ۳۹۸ وهذا يوقعنا في قول المعتزلة : أنَّ الحقِّ عند الله ،متعدد، وهو ما يغفل عنه، حيث يختار من الأقوال ما يشاء من غير ترجيح، فالله المستعان. ٢ . أن يكون مذكوراً في كتب ظاهر الرواية، فهذا ترجيح له من محمد بن الحسن بذكر القول في ظاهر الرواية، إلا إذا وجدناهم رجّحوا غير ما في ظاهر الرواية، فإننا نعمل بترجيحهم؛ لأنهم لم يعدلوا عنه إلا لأسباب: كتغيّر العرف والحرج والضرورة، واللازم في حق المفتي والمدرّس قول المجتهد في المذهب لا قول المجتهد المطلق. قال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار ۱ : ۱۹۲ : ولا يخفى أنّ المتأخرين ... كصاحب «الهداية» وقاضي خان وغيرهما مِنْ أهل الترجيح هم أعلمُ بالمذهب منّنا، فعلينا اتباع ما رجّحوه وما صححوه كما لو أفتونا في حياتهم».
Two ways were mentioned for knowing the preponderant opinion: 1. That the tarjih be issued by those who have ijtihad in the madhhab, so the tarjih of one who is not among the people of tarjih is not considered. This is explicitly clear from the seal of the investigators, Ibn Abidin, that it is not permitted to delve into tarjih between opinions in a single madhhab except for one who has the capability of examination in that, having reached a degree of ijtihad that enables him to do so, because it is a type of ijtihad. So how about one who does tarjih between different madhhabs when he is not among their people? Ibn al-Humam said: 'The reality is that the mufti in cases inevitably needs a type of ijtihad and knowledge of the conditions of the people.' (See: Radd al-Muhtar 2:398) And this leads us to the saying of the Mu'tazila that truth with Allah is multiple, which is what is being neglected, as one chooses from opinions whatever he wishes without tarjih. So Allah is the one sought for help. 2. That it be mentioned in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. This is a tarjih from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan by mentioning the opinion in Zahir al-Riwayah, unless we find that they (the later scholars) have given preponderance to something other than what is in Zahir al-Riwayah, then we act upon their tarjih because they did not deviate from it except for reasons: such as change of custom, hardship, and necessity. And what is binding upon the mufti and teacher is the saying of the mujtahid within the madhhab, not the saying of the absolute mujtahid. Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar 1:192: 'It is not hidden that the later scholars... like the author of al-Hidayah, Qadi Khan, and others among the people of tarjih are more knowledgeable of the madhhab than us, so we must follow what they have given preponderance to and what they have declared correct, just as if they had given us fatwa in their lifetime.'
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents two fundamental rules for determining the preponderant opinion (rajih) within the Hanafi madhhab, a crucial aspect of rasm al-mufti. The author begins by stating that tarjih (weighing of opinions) must be performed by qualified individuals—those who have reached a level of ijtihad within the madhhab. This is not absolute ijtihad but a specialized ability to evaluate evidence and reasoning within the Hanafi legal framework. Ibn Abidin and Ibn al-Humam emphasize that even a mufti in everyday cases needs a certain level of ijtihad and practical knowledge of people's customs and conditions. The passage warns against the practice of picking and choosing opinions without proper tarjih, likening it to the Mu'tazilite doctrine of multiple truths, which is rejected. The second rule involves the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, the core works of the Hanafi school authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani. Any opinion recorded in these books is considered to have been given tarjih by Imam Muhammad himself. However, later scholars (mutakhkhirin) like the author of al-Hidayah and Qadi Khan may prefer a different opinion if circumstances such as custom, hardship, or necessity have changed. In such cases, their preference is to be followed because they are more knowledgeable about the madhhab's methodology and real-world application. This highlights the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh, where later authorities can update rulings while staying within the school's framework.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): The process of weighing evidence or opinions to determine the preponderant (rajīḥ) view within a madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the most authoritative transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fī al-madhhab): A scholar who has reached such a level of expertise in the Hanafi school that he can weigh opinions and issue fatwas, without being an absolute mujtahid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, who is qualified to perform tarjih between opinions within the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Any qualified mufti, regardless of ijtihad level.
B) Only those who have reached a level of ijtihad within the madhhab.
C) Any layperson with basic knowledge.
D) Only absolute mujtahids.

Key Takeaway
The preponderant opinion is determined either by a qualified mujtahid within the madhhab or by its inclusion in Zahir al-Riwayah, with later scholars able to override for valid reasons like changed custom or necessity.

Definition and Books of Zahir al-Riwayah
Defines Zahir al-Riwayah and lists the six core books with a scholarly dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and state the majority view on their classification for fatwa application.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah: the six most authoritative Hanafi texts, with a dispute over one book, settled by majority in favor of six.

A mufti must know which books carry ultimate authority. This lesson introduces Zahir al-Riwayah, the core transmitter of the Hanafi fiqh, and clarifies a subtle dispute over its exact composition. Understanding these books is essential for proper fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the term and its synonyms
Identify 'Zahir al-Riwayah' as the six core books transmitted by Imam Muhammad, also called 'al-usul' or 'riwayat al-usul'.
These are not all of Muhammad's books, but the most reliably transmitted ones.
2
List the six books as per the poem
Memorise the list from the poetic summary: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat.
Some authors omit al-Ziyadat, but the majority includes it.
3
Explain the meaning of 'Zahir al-Riwayah'
Understand that these books contain rulings transmitted from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad via reliable chains, making them either mutawatir or mashhur.
This reliability gives them precedence over later books.
4
Analyze the dispute over five vs six books
Note that Ibn Abidin in one place excludes al-Ziyadat, but this is likely a slip. List authorities on each side.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf with a clear majority view.
5
Determine the operative position for fatwa
Conclude that the accepted position is six books, and fatwa must be based on these sources first.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

وكتب ظاهر ظاهر الرواية أتت ستّاً وبالأصول أيضاً سميت صنّفَها محمد محمد الشيباني الجامع الصغير والكبير والسير حَرَّرَ فيها المذهب النعماني الكبير والصغير ثُمَّ الزيادات مع المبسوط تواترت بالسند المضبوط (۱) معناه: أنَّ كتب ظاهر الرواية يطلق عليها أيضاً رواية الأصول، وظاهر المذهب: وهي مسائل رويت عن أصحاب المذهب، وهم: أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف ومحمد، وقد يلحق زفر والحسن وغيرهما ممن أخذ الفقه عن أبي حنيفة، لكن الغالب الشائع في ظاهر الرواية أن يكون قول الثلاثة أو قول بعضهم، وسُمّيت بظاهر الرواية؛ لأنها رويت عن محمد برواية الثقات، فهي ثابتة عنه إما متواترة أو مشهورة. ينظر : شرح رسم المفتي ص١٦، وغيره. وكلام محقق الأصل» الدكتور محمد بوينو كالن في مقدمة الأصل ١: ١١٣ يشير إلى عدم ذكر الحسن في ظاهر الرواية، حيث قال: «يَذكر الإمام محمد في الكتاب أراء أستاذيه أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ورأيه في مواضع كثيرة جداً من الكتاب، ويذكر نادراً آراء غيرهم مثل: زفر وابن أبي ليلى وسفيان، ويذكر نادراً قول أهل المدينة». واختلفوا في تحديد كتب ظاهر الرواية على أقوال: ١ . أنها ستة كتب: «الجامع الصغير» و «الجامع «الكبير» و «السير الصغير» و«السير الكبير» و «المبسوط» و «الزيادات»، واختاره اللكنوي في عمدة الرعاية ۱: ۲۹، والنحلاوي في الدرر المباحة ص٢٣٢، والكشميري في فيض الباري٢: ٢٦٦، وعلي حيدر في درر الحكام شرح مجلة الأحكام ٤ ٦٠٧ ، والعثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص۲۳، والمجددي في أدب المفتي ٥٧٠ ، وابن عابدين في رد المحتار ۱ : ٤٧ ، وشرح رسم المفتي ص ١٦، والعقود الدرية ١: ١٧٠ ، وفي موضع آخر ۲ : ۳۱۰ ، قال : «المراد بالمذهب ما يذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية الخمسة التي هي: المبسوط، والسير الكبير، والسير الصغير، والجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير من كتب الإمام محمد بن الحسن ، حيث جعلها خمسة وأخرج الزيادات، فلعله سبق قلم منه، التعارضه مع ما ذكره في مواضع أخرى
And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as six, and also called 'the principles' (al-usul). Muhammad al-Shaybani authored them: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar (both small and large), then al-Ziyadat, along with al-Mabsut, transmitted with verified chains. (1) Meaning: The books of Zahir al-Riwayah are also called 'the transmission of the principles' (riwayat al-usul) and 'the apparent madhhab' (zahir al-madhhab). They are issues transmitted from the founders of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Sometimes Zufar, al-Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa may be included, but the common practice in Zahir al-Riwayah is that it contains the sayings of the three or some of them. They are called 'Zahir al-Riwayah' because they were transmitted from Muhammad through reliable narrators, so they are established from him either via tawatur or istifada (widespread transmission). See: Sharh Rasm al-Mufti, p.16, etc. And the words of the editor of al-Asl, Dr. Muhammad Boyno Kalan, in the introduction to al-Asl 1:113 indicate that al-Hasan is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. He said: 'Imam Muhammad mentions in his book the opinions of his two teachers Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf and his own opinion in many places, and rarely mentions the opinions of others such as Zufar, Ibn Abi Layla, and Sufyan, and rarely the saying of the people of Madinah.' They differed on identifying the books of Zahir al-Riwayah. One opinion: They are six books: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. This was chosen by al-Lakhnawi in 'Umdat al-Ri'aya 1:29, al-Nahlawi in al-Durar al-Mubaha p.232, al-Kashmiri in Fayd al-Bari 2:266, Ali Haydar in Durar al-Hukkam 4:607, al-'Uthmani in Usul al-Ifta' p.23, al-Majdadi in Adab al-Mufti p.570, Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar 1:47, and Sharh Rasm al-Mufti p.16, and al-'Uqud al-Duriyya 1:170. In another place (2:310) he said: 'What is meant by al-madhhab is what is mentioned in the five books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir from the books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, where he made them five and excluded al-Ziyadat; perhaps it was a slip of the pen, contradicting what he mentioned elsewhere.'
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and lists the authoritative books of the Hanafi school. It begins with a poetic summary: the books came as six, also called 'al-usul' (the principles). They were authored by Muhammad al-Shaybani and include: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The commentary explains that these books are also known as 'riwayat al-usul' or 'zahir al-madhhab'. They contain rulings transmitted from the school's founders—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—and sometimes from other early Hanafis like Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, though the latter are rare. The name 'Zahir al-Riwayah' comes from their reliable transmission from Muhammad via trustworthy narrators, making them either mutawatir (massively transmitted) or mashhur (widespread). The passage then notes a scholarly dispute: are there five or six books? Most authorities, including Luknawi, Kashmiri, and Ibn Abidin (in most places), say six. However, Ibn Abidin in one place mentions five, excluding al-Ziyadat, but this is likely a slip. The majority view is that the six books constitute the primary source for fatwa. This lesson is essential for understanding the hierarchy of sources in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāya): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing the most reliably transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school, also called 'the principles' (al-usul).
رواية الأصول (Riwāyat al-Uṣūl): Synonym for Zahir al-Riwayah, emphasizing that these books contain the foundational transmitted rulings.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, a concise compilation of Hanafi rulings by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
زيادات (al-Ziyādāt): The book of additional rulings by Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered part of Zahir al-Riwayah by the majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many books are generally considered to constitute the Zahir al-Riwayah by most Hanafi scholars?
A) Five
B) Six
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are the primary authority for Hanafi fatwa; the majority view includes al-Ziyadat as the sixth.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Definition and Authority of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah
Defining Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and its synonyms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, list its component books, and explain why it is the primary authority in Hanafi fatwa.

Core Idea
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the core of the Hanafi madhhab — these books contain the relied-upon positions.

In this lesson, we delve into the foundational layer of Hanafi jurisprudence: Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah. Understanding this term is crucial for any mufti or student of fiqh, as it determines which texts carry binding authority. The passage clarifies its meaning, synonyms, and the conditions under which a ruling belongs to this category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its synonyms
Recognize that Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is also called Riwāyat al-Uṣūl and Ẓāhir al-Madhhab. Note that these are used interchangeably in later sources.
2
Understand the source of transmission
Know that these books were authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and transmitted from the founders: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad himself.
Rarely includes Zufar, Hasan, etc.
3
Examine the transmission criteria
The transmission must be via reliable narrators, either tawatur or mashhur, hence the name 'Zahir' (manifest) al-Riwayah.
This ensures high epistemic certainty.
4
List the core books
The books are: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. However, note the dispute on the count (covered in next lesson).
5
Apply the authority in ifta
A mufti must first consult these books. Rulings from these sources are binding and override other transmissions.
This is the highest level in Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

.۱۸
٢ . ذهب بعضهم : كالبابرتي في العناية ١ : ١٣٦ وابن كمال باشا، كما شرح رسم المفتي ص ١٧ - ۱۸، وطاشكبرى زاده إلى الفرق بينهما ، فقال طاشكبرى في مفتاح السعادة ۲ : ۲۳۷ : «إنَّهم يُعبّرون عن «المبسوط» و «الزيادات» و «الجامعين برواية الأصول، وعن «المبسوط» و«الجامع الصغير» و «السير الكبير» بظاهر الرواية، ومشهور الرواية». والراجح ما ذهب له الجمهور؛ لأنَّ الاستخدام الشائع في عامة الكتب استعمال رواية الأصول مرادفة لظاهر الرواية، ينظر: شرح السير الكبير ١ : ١٨٧١، والنكت للسرخسي ص ٣٦ ، والهداية ٣ : ١٨٤ ، والبدائع ١: ٦٣ ، وغيرها.
And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as six, and also called 'Usul'. They were authored by Muhammad (i.e. Muhammad al-Shaybani): al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar (al-Saghir and al-Kabir), then al-Ziyadat, along with al-Mabsut. They were transmitted with an authentic chain. (1) Its meaning: The books of Zahir al-Riwayah are also called Riwāyat al-Uṣūl and Ẓāhir al-Madhhab. They are issues transmitted from the founders of the madhhab, namely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad; sometimes Zufar, Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa are included, but the common prevailing [understanding] is that it is the statement of the three or some of them. It was named 'Zahir al-Riwayah' because it was transmitted from Muhammad via reliable narrators, so it is established from him either tawatur or mashhur. See: Sharh Rasm al-Mufti p.16, etc. The words of the editor of 'al-Asl', Dr. Muhammad Buwino Kalan, in the introduction to al-Asl 1:113 indicate that Hasan is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. He said: 'Imam Muhammad mentions in the book the opinions of his teachers Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf and his own opinion in very many places, and rarely mentions opinions of others such as Zufar, Ibn Abi Layla, Sufyan, and rarely the opinion of the people of Madinah.' They differed on determining the books of Zahir al-Riwayah in several opinions: 1. That they are six books: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. This was chosen by al-Laknawi, al-Nahlawi, al-Kashmiri, Ali Haydar, al-Uthmani, al-Mujaddidi, Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, Sharh Rasm al-Mufti, and al-Uqud al-Durriya. In another place (2:310) he said: 'What is meant by the madhhab is what is mentioned in the five books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir from the books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, making them five and excluding al-Ziyadat; perhaps it was a slip of the pen.' 2. That they are four books, omitting both parts of al-Siyar. This was chosen by al-Babarti in al-Inayah and Qadi Zadeh in Nata'ij al-Afkar, saying: 'What is meant by Zahir al-Riwayah among the fuqaha is the transmission of al-Jami'an, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat.' 3. That they are five books, omitting al-Siyar al-Saghir. This was chosen by Ibn Maza in al-Muhit al-Burhani, Tashkopruzadeh, Hajji Khalifa, and al-Hamawi. And the third opinion is the rajih (preferred) because when comparing the printed al-Siyar al-Saghir with the Book of Siyar from al-Asl, we find they are completely the same; perhaps it was called 'saghir' to distinguish it from al-Siyar al-Kabir. They also differed on determining [the relationship between] Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Usul: 1. The majority held that there is no difference between them, supported by Ibn Abidin. 2. Some, like al-Babarti and Ibn Kamal Pasha, distinguished: they said 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl' refers to al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Jami'an; 'Ẓāhir al-Riwayah' refers to al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. The rajih is the majority view because common usage treats them synonymously.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines a foundational concept in Hanafi fiqh methodology: 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (the manifest transmission) and its constituent books. The opening lines are a poetic summary by Ibn Abidin stating that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are six: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar (both al-Saghir and al-Kabir), al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The commentary then explains that these books are also called 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl' (transmission of the principles) and represent the core of the madhhab. The issues in these books are transmitted from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and rarely from others like Zufar and Hasan. The passage then presents three scholarly opinions on the exact count of these books: the six-book opinion (preferred by many later scholars), the four-book opinion (excluding al-Siyar), and the five-book opinion (excluding al-Siyar al-Saghir). The author, Ibn Abidin, indicates that the third (five-book) opinion is preponderant because al-Siyar al-Saghir is essentially the same as the section on siyar in al-Asl, making it separate but not an independent book. Finally, the passage addresses the relationship between 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl'. The majority, including Ibn Abidin, hold that they are synonymous, while a minority (al-Babarti, Ibn Kamal Pasha) distinguish them. The author declares the majority view as the correct one, citing widespread usage in later texts. This discussion is crucial for understanding which texts carry authoritative weight in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The manifest transmission; the six (or five) core books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, reliably transmitted and containing the relied-upon positions of the madhhab
رواية الأصول (Riwāyat al-Uṣūl): Transmission of the principles; synonym for Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah according to the majority, referring to the same set of books
ظاهر المذهب (Ẓāhir al-Madhhab): The manifest school; another term for the established position of the Hanafi school, synonymous with Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary condition for a ruling to be considered part of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah?
A) It must be from a book authored by Abu Hanifa.
B) It must be transmitted via a single reliable chain.
C) It must be from the books of Imam Muhammad and transmitted by reliable narrators, and it is the statement of the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) or some of them.
D) It must be practiced by the majority of Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is the highest category of authority in the Hanafi school; a mufti must give precedence to rulings found in these specific books.

Dispute on the Number of Books of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah
Presenting and resolving the dispute on the count of Zahir al-Riwayah books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the three opinions on the number of books constituting Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah and identify the preponderant (rājiḥ) view with its evidence.

Core Idea
The number of books in Zahir al-Riwayah is disputed; the five-book opinion is preponderant due to textual comparison.

While the definition of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is clear, scholars disagreed on exactly which books form its corpus. This lesson unpacks that disagreement, a crucial nuance for understanding the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy. Ibn Abidin presents three opinions and weighs the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
List the three opinions on the count: six books, four books, five books. Note which scholars support each.
The six-book opinion includes both parts of al-Siyar; the four-book excludes al-Siyar; the five-book excludes al-Siyar al-Saghir.
2
Analyze the evidence for the six-book opinion
This is supported by many later scholars like al-Laknawi, but Ibn Abidin notes an inconsistency where he himself sometimes called it five.
3
Analyze the evidence for the four-book opinion
Al-Babarti and Qadi Zadeh argue that 'al-Siyar' is not part of Zahir al-Riwayah. Their reasoning is based on the common usage among earlier fuqaha.
4
Analyze the evidence for the five-book opinion
The key evidence is textual: comparing al-Siyar al-Saghir with the siyar section of al-Asl reveals they are identical. Hence, al-Siyar al-Saghir is not an independent book.
This is the opinion Ibn Abidin declares as 'al-rajih' (preponderant).
5
Understand the difference with Riwāyat al-Uṣūl
The passage also addresses whether Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwāyat al-Uṣūl are synonymous. The majority, including Ibn Abidin, hold they are, despite some distinctions.
This affects terminology in later works.

١ . أنها ستة كتب: «الجامع الصغير» و «الجامع «الكبير» و «السير الصغير» و«السير الكبير» و «المبسوط» و «الزيادات»، واختاره اللكنوي في عمدة الرعاية ۱: ۲۹، والنحلاوي في الدرر المباحة ص٢٣٢، والكشميري في فيض الباري٢: ٢٦٦، وعلي حيدر في درر الحكام شرح مجلة الأحكام ٤ ٦٠٧ ، والعثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص۲۳، والمجددي في أدب المفتي ٥٧٠ ، وابن عابدين في رد المحتار ۱ : ٤٧ ، وشرح رسم المفتي ص ١٦، والعقود الدرية ١: ١٧٠ ، وفي موضع آخر ۲ : ۳۱۰ ، قال : «المراد بالمذهب ما يذكر في كتب ظاهر الرواية الخمسة التي هي: المبسوط، والسير الكبير، والسير الصغير، والجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير من كتب الإمام محمد بن الحسن ، حيث جعلها خمسة وأخرج الزيادات، فلعله سبق قلم منه، التعارضه مع ما ذكره في مواضع أخرى

٢ . أنّها أربعة كتب، فلم يَعدّ السير بقسميه منها، واختاره البابرتي في العناية ٨: ٣٧١ وقاضي زاده في نتائج الأفكار :۸ ۳۷۱،۹ : ۱۰۴ ، إذ قالا : المراد بظاهر الرواية عند الفقهاء: رواية «الجامعين» و «المبسوط و الزيادات»، ويعبّر عنها بظاهر الرواية، والمراد بغير ظاهر الرواية: رواية غيرها».
٣. أنها خمسة كتب، فلم يعدّ «السير الصغير منها، واختار ابن مازه في المحيط البرهاني ١ : ٢٩، و طاشكبرى زاده في مفتاح السعادة :۲ : ۲۳۷ ، وحاجي خليفة في كشف الظنون ۲: ١٢٨٣، والحموي في غمز عيون البصائر ٤ : ٣٢٢. والقول الثالث هو الراجح؛ لأننا عند مقابلة كتاب السير الصغير» المطبوع (طبعة السير الصغير بتحقيق: مجيد خدوري الدار المتحدة للنشر، بيروت، ١٩٧٥م، ط١) مع «كتاب السير من كتاب «الأصل» ١ : ٥٣٨٤٢١ ، ( طبعة قطر ) لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني نجد أنهما لا يختلفان عن بعضهما أبداً، فلعله سُمِّي بالصغير؛ تمييزاً له عن «السير الكبير» الذي ألفه محمد بن الحسن مستقلاً، وشرحه السرخسي وغيره. واختلفوا في تحديد ظاهر الرواية والأصول:
١ . ذهب الجمهور : أنَّه لا فرق بينهما، وانتصر لهم ابن عابدين في شرح رسم المفتي ص ١٦ -
.۱۸
٢ . ذهب بعضهم : كالبابرتي في العناية ١ : ١٣٦ وابن كمال باشا، كما شرح رسم المفتي ص ١٧ - ۱۸، وطاشكبرى زاده إلى الفرق بينهما ، فقال طاشكبرى في مفتاح السعادة ۲ : ۲۳۷ : «إنَّهم يُعبّرون عن «المبسوط» و «الزيادات» و «الجامعين برواية الأصول، وعن «المبسوط» و«الجامع الصغير» و «السير الكبير» بظاهر الرواية، ومشهور الرواية». والراجح ما ذهب له الجمهور؛ لأنَّ الاستخدام الشائع في عامة الكتب استعمال رواية الأصول مرادفة لظاهر الرواية، ينظر: شرح السير الكبير ١ : ١٨٧١، والنكت للسرخسي ص ٣٦ ، والهداية ٣ : ١٨٤ ، والبدائع ١: ٦٣ ، وغيرها.
And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah came as six, and also called 'Usul'. They were authored by Muhammad (i.e. Muhammad al-Shaybani): al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar (al-Saghir and al-Kabir), then al-Ziyadat, along with al-Mabsut. They were transmitted with an authentic chain. (1) Its meaning: The books of Zahir al-Riwayah are also called Riwāyat al-Uṣūl and Ẓāhir al-Madhhab. They are issues transmitted from the founders of the madhhab, namely Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad; sometimes Zufar, Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa are included, but the common prevailing [understanding] is that it is the statement of the three or some of them. It was named 'Zahir al-Riwayah' because it was transmitted from Muhammad via reliable narrators, so it is established from him either tawatur or mashhur. See: Sharh Rasm al-Mufti p.16, etc. The words of the editor of 'al-Asl', Dr. Muhammad Buwino Kalan, in the introduction to al-Asl 1:113 indicate that Hasan is not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. He said: 'Imam Muhammad mentions in the book the opinions of his teachers Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf and his own opinion in very many places, and rarely mentions opinions of others such as Zufar, Ibn Abi Layla, Sufyan, and rarely the opinion of the people of Madinah.' They differed on determining the books of Zahir al-Riwayah in several opinions: 1. That they are six books: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat. This was chosen by al-Laknawi, al-Nahlawi, al-Kashmiri, Ali Haydar, al-Uthmani, al-Mujaddidi, Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, Sharh Rasm al-Mufti, and al-Uqud al-Durriya. In another place (2:310) he said: 'What is meant by the madhhab is what is mentioned in the five books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Jami' al-Saghir from the books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, making them five and excluding al-Ziyadat; perhaps it was a slip of the pen.' 2. That they are four books, omitting both parts of al-Siyar. This was chosen by al-Babarti in al-Inayah and Qadi Zadeh in Nata'ij al-Afkar, saying: 'What is meant by Zahir al-Riwayah among the fuqaha is the transmission of al-Jami'an, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat.' 3. That they are five books, omitting al-Siyar al-Saghir. This was chosen by Ibn Maza in al-Muhit al-Burhani, Tashkopruzadeh, Hajji Khalifa, and al-Hamawi. And the third opinion is the rajih (preferred) because when comparing the printed al-Siyar al-Saghir with the Book of Siyar from al-Asl, we find they are completely the same; perhaps it was called 'saghir' to distinguish it from al-Siyar al-Kabir. They also differed on determining [the relationship between] Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Usul: 1. The majority held that there is no difference between them, supported by Ibn Abidin. 2. Some, like al-Babarti and Ibn Kamal Pasha, distinguished: they said 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl' refers to al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Jami'an; 'Ẓāhir al-Riwayah' refers to al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. The rajih is the majority view because common usage treats them synonymously.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines a foundational concept in Hanafi fiqh methodology: 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (the manifest transmission) and its constituent books. The opening lines are a poetic summary by Ibn Abidin stating that the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are six: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar (both al-Saghir and al-Kabir), al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. The commentary then explains that these books are also called 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl' (transmission of the principles) and represent the core of the madhhab. The issues in these books are transmitted from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and rarely from others like Zufar and Hasan. The passage then presents three scholarly opinions on the exact count of these books: the six-book opinion (preferred by many later scholars), the four-book opinion (excluding al-Siyar), and the five-book opinion (excluding al-Siyar al-Saghir). The author, Ibn Abidin, indicates that the third (five-book) opinion is preponderant because al-Siyar al-Saghir is essentially the same as the section on siyar in al-Asl, making it separate but not an independent book. Finally, the passage addresses the relationship between 'Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'Riwāyat al-Uṣūl'. The majority, including Ibn Abidin, hold that they are synonymous, while a minority (al-Babarti, Ibn Kamal Pasha) distinguish them. The author declares the majority view as the correct one, citing widespread usage in later texts. This discussion is crucial for understanding which texts carry authoritative weight in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The manifest transmission; the core books authored by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, reliably transmitted and containing the relied-upon positions of the madhhab
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr): A book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing concise fiqh rulings
الجامع الكبير (al-Jāmiʿ al-Kabīr): A book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on fiqh, larger in scope
المبسوط (al-Mabsūṭ): An extensive work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on fiqh, also part of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah
الزيادات (al-Ziyādāt): A book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing additional rulings beyond the other books
السير الكبير (al-Siyar al-Kabīr): A book on Islamic international law and warfare by Imam Muhammad
السير الصغير (al-Siyar al-Ṣaghīr): A book by Imam Muhammad which is actually identical to the siyar section in al-Asl

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence Ibn Abidin uses to support the five-book opinion?
A) The majority of scholars hold it.
B) Al-Siyar al-Saghir is identical to the siyar section in al-Asl.
C) Al-Siyar al-Saghir is rarely cited in fatwa.
D) Abu Hanifa only wrote five books.

Key Takeaway
The preponderant view on the number of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah books is five, excluding al-Siyar al-Saghir due to its textual duplication with al-Asl.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Classification of Non-Zahir al-Riwayah Sources in Hanafi Fatwa
Taxonomy of Hanafi sources beyond the six core books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of non-Zahir al-Riwayah sources and apply the hierarchy rule to determine which sources take precedence in fatwa.

Core Idea
Non-Zahir al-Riwayah books are authoritative but subordinate to the six core books.

In Hanafi fatwa, not all sources carry equal weight. While the six Zahir al-Riwayah books form the bedrock of the madhhab, many other works are also used. This lesson details the four categories of these additional sources and explains how a mufti ranks them to issue sound rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The passage divides non-Zahir al-Riwayah works into personal collections of Imam Muhammad, hadith-dominant books, Nawadir, and works by other scholars. List each category.
2
Rank each category
Focus on relative authority: hadith-dominant books (e.g., Muwatta' Muhammad, al-Athar) are ranked above Nawadir, and all yield to the six Zahir al-Riwayah books.
Al-'Uthmani's principle: take from these books unless they contradict the six.
3
Note the citation rule
The passage states: these books are acted upon except when they contradict the six core books. This is a key rule for fatwa.
This rule applies especially to Muhammad's hadith-dominant works.
4
Apply to fatwa scenario
Given a ruling from al-Athar and a conflicting ruling from al-Mabsut (a Zahir al-Riwayah book), determine which prevails.
The six books are mufta bihi; al-Athar is subordinate.

معناه: أنَّ كتب غير ظاهر الرواية هي المسائل التي رويت عن الأئمة، لكن في غير كتب ظاهر الرواية، وهي على أقسام:
أولاً: كتب لم تشتهر عن مُحمّد، ولم ترو عنه بطرق كطرق الكتب الأول، وهي:
١. «الكيانيات»: وهي مسائل جمعها محمد لرجل يسمى كيان، وقد يوجد في بعض الكتب «الكيسانيات»، وقالوا: جمعها كيسان وهي بلدة قال طاشكبرى في مفتاح السعادة ٢: ٢٣٧: «لكن هذا غير صحيح، والصحيح الأول»، وقال الكوثري في بلوغ الأماني ص٦٦: مسائل رواها سليمان بن شعيب عن أبيه عن محمد، ويقال لها الأمالي.
. «الرقيَّات»: وهي مسائل جمعها محمد حين كان قاضياً بالرقة، قال الكوثري في بلوغ الأماني ص٦٦: «رواها عنه محمد سماعة وكان معه طول بقاء محمد بن الحسن بها».
. «الجرجانيات»: وهي مسائل جمعها محمد بجرجان، قال الكوثري في بلوغ الأماني ص٦٦: «ويرويها علي بن صالح الجرجاني».
. «الهارونيات»: وهي مسائل جمعها محمد لرجل مسمَّى بهارون، وفي المظاهري ص٦٨: مسائل جمعها محمد في زمن هارون الرشيد.
. «الكسب» يقال: إنَّه مات قبل أن يتمه، وكانوا سألوه أن يؤلف كتاباً في الورع، فجاوبهم بأني ألفت كتاباً في البيوع، يريد أنَّ المرء إذا طاب مكسبه حسن عمله، فلما أصروا على الطلب بدأ في تأليف هذا الكتاب...
ثانياً: كتب محمد التي يغلب فيها الحديث، فبين أيدينا:
١. موطأ محمد بروايته عن مالك، وفيه ما يزيد على ألف حديث وأثر من مرفوع وموقوف مما رواه عن مالك، وفيه نحو مئة وخمسة وسبعين حديثاً عن نحو أربعين شيخاً سوى مالك...، وعليه شروح عديدة منها: شرح القاري، وشرح البيري، وشرح عثمان الكماخي، وشرح اللكنوي المسمى التعليق الممجد...
٢. «الحجة»، المعروفة بالحجج في الاحتجاج على أهل المدينة.
. «الآثار»، يروي فيه عن أبي حنيفة أحاديث مرفوعة وموقوفة ومرسلة، ويكثر جداً عن إبراهيم النخعي شيخ الطريقة العراقية، ويروي فيه قليلاً عن نحو عشرين شيخاً سوى أبي حنيفة، وهو كتاب نافع للغاية، وللمشايخ عناية خاصة بروايته في أثباتهم، وقد ألف ابن حجر «الإيثار بمعرفة رواة الآثار» في رجالة باقتراح صاحبه العلامة قاسم الحافظ، ثم ألف هو أيضاً كتاباً آخر في رجاله ينظر: بلوغ الأماني ص ٦٥-٦٦.
قال العثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص ١٣٩: (والظاهر أنَّها وإن كانت بمثابة كتب ظاهر الرواية في صحة نسبتها إلى الإمام محمد، واشتهارها فيما بين أهل العلم، ولكنها ليست موضوعة لبيان المذهب وفروعه... وكتب ظاهر الرواية فإنَّها وضعت لبيان المذهب أصلاً، فصارت هي المعتمدة لمعرفة المذهب الحنفي، ولعل من أجل هذا لم يذكر الفقهاء الحنفية هذه الكتب لا في ظاهر الرواية ولا في النّوادر؛ لأنها ليست من النوادر لشهرتها عن الإمام محمد، وليست من ظاهر الرواية؛ لأنّها لم توضع لبيان المذهب، ولكن الظاهر أن رتبتها فوق النوادر ويؤخذ بما جاء فيها إلا ما عارض الكتب الستة).
ثالثاً: الروايات المتفرقة
وهي المشهورة بالنوادر وهي عن محمد بن الحسن من غير ظاهر الرواية، وهي ثمان: «نوادر هشام»، ونوادر ابن سماعه» و «نوادر ابن رستم و نوادر داود بن رشيد»، و«نوادر المعلى»، ونوادر بشر»، و «نوادر ابن شجاع البلخي أبى نصر»، و«نوادر أبي سليمان»، ينظر: مقدمة منتهى النقاية على شرح الوقاية ص ٥٦-٥٨، وغيره.
رابعاً: كتب غير محمّد: كـ «المجرَّد للحسن بن زياد» ومنها: كتب «الأمالي»، ويقال: أنَّ الأمالي في ثلاثمئة جزء، والإملاء: أن يقعد العالم وحوله تلامذة بالمحابر والقراطيس، فيتكلّم العالم بما فتح الله عليه من العلم، وتكتب التلامذة ما تكلّم مجلساً مجلساً، ثم يجمعون ما كتبوا، فيصير كتاباً، ويسمّى بـ«الأمالي»، وكان هذا عادة المتقدمين. ينظر: شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص. ١٧
Its meaning: that the books of non-Zahir al-Riwayah are the issues that were narrated from the imams, but in other than the Zahir al-Riwayah books. And they are divided into categories:
First: Books not widely known from Muhammad, and not transmitted from him by the methods of the first books. They are:
1. 'al-Kiyaniyat': issues collected by Muhammad for a man named Kiyan; sometimes found as 'al-Kaysaniyat', and they said: collected by Kaysan which is a town. Tashkubri said in Miftah al-Sa'adah 2:237: 'but this is incorrect, the correct is the first.' al-Kawthari said in Bulugh al-Amani p.66: issues narrated by Sulayman ibn Shu'ayb from his father from Muhammad, also called al-Amali.
 'al-Raqqiyat': issues collected by Muhammad when he was judge in al-Raqqah. al-Kawthari said in Bulugh al-Amani p.66: 'narrated from him by Muhammad Sama'ah who was with him throughout Muhammad ibn al-Hasan's stay there.'
 'al-Jurjaniyat': issues collected by Muhammad in Jurjan. al-Kawthari said in Bulugh al-Amani p.66: 'Ali ibn Salih al-Jurjani narrates them.'
 'al-Haruniyat': issues collected by Muhammad for a man named Harun; and in al-Mazahiri p.68: issues collected by Muhammad in the time of Harun al-Rashid.
 'al-Kasb': it is said that he died before completing it. They had asked him to write a book on scrupulousness (wara'), so he answered: I have written a book on sales, meaning that if one's earning is good, his actions become good. When they insisted on the request, he began composing this book...
Second: Muhammad's books in which hadith predominates. Before us are:
1. Muwatta' Muhammad in his narration from Malik, containing over a thousand hadith and athar of marfu' and mawquf from his narration from Malik, and about one hundred seventy-five hadith from about forty shaykhs besides Malik... It has numerous commentaries including: Sharh al-Qari, Sharh al-Birri, Sharh 'Uthman al-Kamakhi, and Sharh al-Laknawi titled al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad...
2. 'al-Hujja', known as al-Hujaj in argumentation against the people of Madinah.
 'al-Athar': he narrates in it from Abu Hanifah marfu', mawquf, and mursal hadith, and relies heavily on Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, the shaykh of the Iraqi school, and narrates occasionally from about twenty shaykhs besides Abu Hanifah. It is a very beneficial book, and the scholars have special care for its narration in their thabats. Ibn Hajar wrote 'al-Ithar bi Ma'rifat Ruwat al-Athar' about its narrators at the suggestion of his associate 'Allamah Qasim al-Hafiz, then he also wrote another book on its narrators (see Bulugh al-Amani p.65-66).
Al-'Uthmani said in Usul al-Ifta' p.139: 'It appears that these, although they are like the Zahir al-Riwayah books in the authenticity of their attribution to Imam Muhammad and their fame among scholars, are not composed for exposition of the school and its branches... while the Zahir al-Riwayah books were composed originally to expound the school, so they became the relied-upon for knowing the Hanafi school. Perhaps for this reason the Hanafi jurists did not list these books either among Zahir al-Riwayah or among Nawadir; because they are not from Nawadir due to their fame from Imam Muhammad, and not from Zahir al-Riwayah because they were not composed to expound the school. But it appears that their rank is above Nawadir, and what is contained in them is to be taken except what contradicts the six books.'
Third: The scattered narrations
They are famous as Nawadir, and they are from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan other than Zahir al-Riwayah. They are eight: 'Nawadir Hisham', 'Nawadir Ibn Sama'ah', 'Nawadir Ibn Rustam', 'Nawadir Dawud ibn Rashid', 'Nawadir al-Mu'alla', 'Nawadir Bishr', 'Nawadir Ibn Shuja' al-Balkhi Abu Nasr', and 'Nawadir Abi Sulayman' (see: Muqaddimah Muntaha al-Niqayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah p.56-58, and others).
Fourth: Books by other than Muhammad: such as 'al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad', and among them: the books of 'al-Amali'. It is said that al-Amali is in three hundred parts. Imla' is that the scholar sits with students around him with inkwells and papers, and the scholar speaks of what Allah opens for him of knowledge, and the students write down what he says session by session, then they compile what they wrote, and it becomes a book, called al-Amali. This was the practice of the early scholars. See: Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p.17.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a detailed taxonomy of the Hanafi sources that fall outside the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.). The author classifies them into four categories: 

**First: Personal collections of Imam Muhammad** – These are books compiled by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani for specific persons or places (e.g., Kiyan, Raqqah, Jurjan, Harun). They are not widely transmitted through the same rigorous chains as the first books. Notable among them is 'al-Kasb', which he began composing but died before finishing; it was intended to address scrupulousness (wara'), but he redirected by saying he already wrote on sales, implying lawful earning leads to righteous deeds.

**Second: Muhammad's hadith-dominant works** – These include his recension of Malik's Muwatta', 'al-Hujja' (a polemical work against the Madinan school), and 'al-Athar' (a collection of narrations from Abu Hanifah and early Kufan scholars). These books are not primarily meant to expound Hanafi fiqh rulings; rather, they serve as hadith sources. However, as al-'Uthmani notes, they are as authentic as Zahir al-Riwayah in attribution but are ranked above Nawadir—they are to be followed unless they contradict the six core books.

**Third: The scattered narrations (Nawadir)** – These are eight distinct collections of rulings narrated from Muhammad but not through the main Zahir al-Riwayah channels. They are individually named after their narrators (e.g., Nawadir Hisham, Ibn Sama'ah, etc.). Their authority is lower than the first two categories.

**Fourth: Works by non-Muhammad scholars** – Such as 'al-Mujarrad' by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i (a direct student of Abu Hanifah) and the 'Amali' books, which were compiled from dictation sessions. These are not authored by Muhammad but still contribute to the Hanafi corpus.

This classification is crucial for a mufti to understand the rank and reliability of different Hanafi sources. The relian-upon position is that the books in the first two categories (especially the hadith-dominated ones by Muhammad) are to be given weight over Nawadir but yield to the unambiguous rulings of the six Zahir al-Riwayah works.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad that are the primary sources for Hanafi fatwa.
النوادر (al-Nawādir): The eight collections of scattered narrations from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, transmitted outside the standard Zahir al-Riwayah chains.
كسب (al-Kasb): An unfinished book by Muhammad on scrupulousness (wara'), focusing on lawful earning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the rank of 'al-Hujja' and 'al-Athar' relative to the six Zahir al-Riwayah books?
A) They are equal in authority to Zahir al-Riwayah.
B) They are of lower authority and are considered Nawadir.
C) They are above Nawadir but rulings are taken from them unless they contradict the six books.
D) They have no authority for fatwa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy: six Zahir al-Riwayah books are primary; Muhammad's hadith-dominant works are above Nawadir; all non-Zahir works yield to the six in case of conflict.

The Nawadir: Rare Transmissions and Their Authority
Classifying sources beyond the core six

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight Nawadir books, state their authority relative to Zahir al-Riwayah, and apply the hierarchy when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
Nawadir are secondary to Zahir al-Riwayah; a mufti must prefer the latter first.

This lesson explores the first layer of sources beyond the six core books: the Nawadir. These eight collections of rare transmissions from Imam Muhammad are authoritative but carry less weight than Zahir al-Riwayah. Understanding this hierarchy protects the mufti from issuing fatwa based on weaker narrations when stronger ones exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that Nawadir are transmissions from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan not included in the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah. They are referred to as 'al-riwayat al-mutafarriqah' (scattered narratives).
The text explicitly calls them 'al-mashhurah bi al-Nawadir'.
2
List the eight books
Memorize the eight named collections: Nawadir Hisham, Ibn Sam'ah, Ibn Rustam, Dawud ibn Rashid, al-Mu'alla, Bishr, Ibn Shuja' al-Balkhi, and Abu Sulayman. These are the primary rare transmissions.
Some lists vary slightly; the text here is authoritative.
3
Locate the authority
Understand that these books are below Zahir al-Riwayah in authority. They are used when a ruling is not found in the six books, or as supporting evidence.
Later compilers often mixed them, but a mufti should prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah.
4
Contrast with other early sources
The text also mentions books like al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and the al-Amali (dictation works). These are similar in authority to Nawadir but from different compilers.
Amali is a genre; the Hanafis have many such collections.

وأصحاب أصحابه ونحوهم فَمَن بعدهم... وأوّل كتاب جمع في النوازل مما عُلِم «النوازل» لأبي الليث السمرقندي (ت ٣٧٥هـ)، وجمع فيه فتاوى المتأخرين من المجتهدين من مشايخه، وشيوخ مشايخه كمحمد بن مقاتل ومحمد بن سلمة ونصير بن يحيى، وذكر فيها اختياراته أيضاً.
ثم جمع المشايخ فيه كتب: كـ مجموع «النوازل» و«الواقعات للناطفي والصدر الشهيد، ثم جمع من بعدهم من المشايخ الفتاوى لكنهم خلطوا فيها مسائل ظاهر الرواية والنوادر والنوازل مع بعضها كما في «جامع قاضي خان» و«الخلاصة»، وغيرها من الفتاوى، ومنهم من ميز بينها كما في «محيط رضي الدين السَّرَخُسي»، فإنَّه ذكر أوّلاً مسائل الأصول، ثمّ النوادر، ثم الفتاوى. ينظر : النافع الكبير ص١٨-١٩، وغيره.
Third: The scattered narratives—they are known as al-Nawadir, and they are from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan other than Zahir al-Riwayah. They are eight: Nawadir Hisham, Nawadir Ibn Sam'ah, Nawadir Ibn Rustam, Nawadir Dawud ibn Rashid, Nawadir al-Mu'alla, Nawadir Bishr, Nawadir Ibn Shuja' al-Balkhi Abu Nasr, and Nawadir Abu Sulayman. See: Muqaddimah Muntaha al-Niqayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah pp. 56-58, etc. Fourth: Books not by Muhammad: like al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, and among them the books of al-Amali. It is said that al-Amali was in three hundred parts. Imla' (dictation) is that the scholar sits with students around him with inkwells and papers, the scholar speaks what Allah opens for him of knowledge, and the students write what he says session by session, then they collect what they wrote, and it becomes a book called al-Amali. This was the practice of the earlier scholars. See: Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 17. And after that: Issues of Nawazil—the shaykhs extracted them with evidences. (1) Meaning: that the books of Nawazil and Waqi'at are issues deduced by the later scholars from the companions of Muhammad and the companions of his companions and so on and those after them... The first book compiled in Nawazil that is known is al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 375 AH). He collected in it the fatawa of the later mujtahids among his shaykhs and the shaykhs of his shaykhs like Muhammad ibn Muqatil, Muhammad ibn Salama, and Nasir ibn Yahya, and he also mentioned his own choices. Then the shaykhs compiled books in it: like the collections of al-Nawazil and al-Waqi'at by al-Natifi and al-Sadr al-Shahid. Then the shaykhs after them compiled fatawa, but they mixed in them issues of Zahir al-Riwayah, al-Nawadir, and al-Nawazil together, as in Jami' Qadi Khan and al-Khulasah and other fatawa. And among them are those who distinguished between them, as in Muhit Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi, for he mentioned first the issues of usul, then al-Nawadir, then the fatawa. See: al-Nafi' al-Kabir pp. 18-19, etc.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Uqud Rasm al-Mufti by Ibn Abidin, discussing the hierarchical sources for Hanafi fatwa beyond the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah. It categorizes the sources into layers: first, the Nawadir (rare transmissions) which are eight specific books transmitted from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan but not part of Zahir al-Riwayah; second, books by other early Hanafi scholars like al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and the dictation-based Amali works. The text then explains the Nawazil literature—books of legal cases deduced by later scholars based on the principles of the early masters. The first known compilation is al-Nawazil by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi (d. 375 AH), collecting fatawa of mujtahids after the disciples of Muhammad. Later compilations like Jami' Qadi Khan and al-Khulasah mixed all layers without distinction, while some works like al-Muhit by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi meticulously separated them. For the mufti, this classification is crucial: rulings from Zahir al-Riwayah are primary, Nawadir are secondary and used cautiously, and Nawazil represent later ijtihad but must be checked against the founding texts. The author emphasizes that the practice of later scholars mixing sources can cause confusion, so a mufti must be aware of the source and authority weight of each ruling.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-Nawadir): The eight books of rare transmissions from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, forming the primary corpus of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Nawadir are eight secondary sources; a mufti must always prefer Zahir al-Riwayah first.

Hierarchy of Hanafi Texts and Prioritization Rules
Explains priority among Zahir al-Riwayah books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hierarchy of Hanafi source texts and apply the rule of preferring later Zahir al-Riwayah books over earlier ones when issuing fatwas.

Core Idea
Later Zahir al-Riwayah texts override earlier ones; Sarakhsi's Mabsut is the ultimate authority.

In Hanafi fatwa, not all texts are equal. A mufti must know which sources carry more weight. This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti lays out the hierarchy: the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are primary, with later ones preferred, and the commentary of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi is so authoritative that it should never be contradicted. Understanding this hierarchy ensures that your fatwas are built on the most reliable narrations within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books
Memorize the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat. These are the foundational texts of the Hanafi school.
Al-Mabsut is the original, al-Jami' al-Saghir comes after.
2
Apply the later-over-earlier rule
When two of the six books conflict, the later one is preferred. For example, al-Ziyadat is later than al-Mabsut, so it takes precedence.
This reflects Imam Muhammad's final revisions.
3
Recognize al-Kafi's role
Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of the six, removing repetition. It is a trusted summary.
It is not a separate source but a distillation.
4
Acknowledge Sarakhsi's Mabsut as supreme
The commentary Mabsut al-Sarakhsi on al-Kafi is 'like the sun' — reliable and not to be contradicted or replaced.
Fatwas that contradict it are rejected.
5
Understand riwaya hierarchy
Not all narrations from Abu Hanifa have equal weight. Some were chosen by him, others by later scholars. Be aware of the chain of transmission.
This affects which reports are relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واشتهر المبسوط بالأصل الجامع الصغير بعده فها وذا السبقه الستة تصنيفاً كذا فيه على الأصل لذا تقدّما وقع التعارض مثلاً فيما بين المبسوط و الزيادات يختار ما في الزيادات؛ لكونه متأخراً. ويجمع الست كتاب الكافي للحاكم الشهيد فهو الكافي أقوى شروحه الذي كالشمس مبسوط شمس الأئمة السرخسى معتمد النقول ليس يُعمل عنه يُعدل يخلفه وليس. واعلم بأن عن أبي حنيفة جاءت روايات غدت منيفة اختار منها بعضها والباقي يختار منه سائر الرفاق
And al-Mabsut became famous as the original, al-Jami' al-Saghir after it, so these six books in classification such that upon the original they are advanced. If a conflict occurs, for example, between al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat, that which is in al-Ziyadat is chosen because it is later. And the six books are collected in the book al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, so it is sufficient. The strongest of its commentaries is al-Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, which is like the sun, reliable in transmissions, not working against it, not departing from it, nor replacing it. And know that from Abu Hanifa came narrations that became beneficial. Some of them he chose, and the remainder are chosen from the rest of the companions.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule for muftis regarding the hierarchy of Hanafi primary texts. The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are foundational, with al-Mabsut by Imam Muhammad considered the original, followed by al-Jami' al-Saghir. When a conflict arises between two of these six books, the later one is preferred, as exemplified by preferring al-Ziyadat over al-Mabsut. Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is a compilation of these six, removing repetition, and its most authoritative commentary is al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, which is so reliable that it should not be contradicted. Lastly, the passage reminds that not all narrations from Abu Hanifa are equal; some were selected by him, while others are chosen by later scholars, implying a hierarchy of transmissions within the school.

Key Terms
الستة (al-sitta): The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, and al-Ziyadat.
الزيادات (al-Ziyadat): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, considered later than al-Mabsut and thus preferred in case of conflict.
الكافي (al-Kafi): A compilation by al-Hakim al-Shahid that condenses the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah into a single volume.
مبسوط السرخسي (Mabsut al-Sarakhsi): The famous commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi on al-Kafi, regarded as the most authoritative explanation of the six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, later Zahir al-Riwayah texts override earlier ones, and Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is the supreme authority that cannot be contradicted.

The Authority of Al-Kafi and Al-Mabsut in Hanafi Fatwa
Establishes authoritative sources for fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the authoritative source hierarchy in Hanafi fatwa and apply the rule that Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the primary reference, not to be contradicted.

Core Idea
Al-Kafi is the core text; Al-Mabsut is the ultimate commentary — nothing contrary to it is accepted.

In the Hanafi madhhab, not all books carry equal weight. This passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' establishes a clear hierarchy: the compilation Al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid is the relied-upon source, and its foremost commentary, Al-Mabsut by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, is so authoritative that no fatwa is given against it. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any mufti to issue correct rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify Al-Kafi as the relied-upon compilation
Al-Hakim al-Shahid compiled the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah, dropping repetitions, into Al-Kafi. The passage states it is the book relied upon in the madhhab.
Zahir al-Riwayah are the six core works of Imam Muhammad.
2
Recognize Al-Mabsut as the supreme commentary
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's commentary on Al-Kafi is described as 'like the sun' and the strongest. Al-Tarsusi's statement establishes that nothing contrary to it is acted upon.
Al-Tarsusi: 'no fatwa is given except upon it'.
3
Understand the rasm rule for fatwa
The passage sets a rule: in issuing fatwa, one must rely on Al-Mabsut. This is a procedural principle (rasm al-mufti) that guides muftis to the correct source.
This rule prevents reliance on weaker or later opinions.
4
Apply the hierarchy in practice
When a question arises, the mufti should first refer to Al-Kafi, then to Al-Mabsut. Any opinion contradicting Al-Mabsut is rejected.
This hierarchy ensures consistency in the madhhab.

قال حاجي خليفة في كشف الظنون :۲ : ۱۳۷۸ : وهو كتاب معتمد في نقل المذهب». وشرحه جمع من العلماء: كالإسبيجابي (ت٤٨٠هـ) وإسماعيل بن يعقوب الأنباري
ت ۳۳۱هـ) . ينظر : كشف الظنون ۲ : ۱۳۷۸. وأبرز شراحه وأشهرهم شمس الأئمة السَّرَخُسي (ت نحو ٥٠٠هـ)، قال الطرسوسي: « مبسوط السَّرَخُسي» لا يعمل بما يخالفه، ولا يركن إلا إليه، ولا يفتى ولا يعوّل إلا عليه».
ينظر : شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٢٠، وغيره. قال الدكتور محمد بوينوكالن في مقدمة «الأصل» ص ۱۱۹ - ۱۲۰: «والذي لاحظنا مِنَ الإطلاع على كتاب «الكافي» للحاكم أنه يختصر لفظ كتاب الأصل، ويتخذه أساساً ثم يضيف إليه ما يراه مناسباً من كتب الإمام محمد الأخرى وأحياناً من كتب أبي يوسف، لكن الأساس هو كتاب «الأصل»، والعبارة هي كتاب «الأصل» في معظمها ... والحاكم قد قام بعمل مهم جداً في هذا الكتاب، وهو أنه قد قارن بين نسخ كتاب الأصل، وأثبت الفروق بينها في مواضع كثيرة من «الكافي»، وأكثر ما اعتمد عليه نسخة أبي سليمان وأبي حفص، ولكن توجد فيه إشارات إلى بعض النسخ الأخرى في مواضع قليلة...». (۳) في أوب: «جات».
فلم یکن لغیره جواب
كما عليه أقسم الأصحاب)
(۱) ومعناها وردت عن أبي حنيفة عدة أقوال واضحة بينة في المسألة، فاختار منها أبو حنيفة رواية، واختار أصحابه الروايات الباقية، فكل ما ورد من أقوال عن أصحابه هي أقوال لأبي حنيفة هم اختاروها، وهذا تفسير القسم الوارد عن أبي يوسف وغيره من أنَّ كلَّ أقوالهم هي عبارة عن أقوال لأبي حنيفة، وهذا يخالف حقق في بلوغهم درجة المجتهد المطلق، وإنَّما آثروا الانتساب لشيخهم أدباً وإجلالاً له، فقولهم بما قال إنَّما هو لموافقة رأيهم لرأيه في الاجتهاد، فإنَّ مجلس أبي حنيفة مجلس تفقيه، وَمِنَ الطبيعي أن تعرض فيه كل الوجوه للمسألة، ومَن ثَمّ يختار كل واحدٍ منهم وجهاً اعتماداً على أصوله التي قرّرها. وأيضاً هذا الكلام منهم بعدم خروجهم عن أقوال أبي حنيفة من باب الأدب والتواضع أمام من يقول لهم : لو لم تستقلوا باجتهاد في مذهب منفرد للشهرة العظيمة التي نالوها بعد الإمام فكان كلامهم ردّاً على هذا، وإن لم يكن في الواقع تماماً، والله أعلم.
قال العثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص ١٦٩: ومعناه على ما حققه العلامة الكوثري: أنَّ الإمام أبا حنيفة كان يبدي أمام تلامذته احتمالات مختلفة في مسألة واحدة، وكان أصحابه يأخذون بأحد هذه الاحتمالات بأدلتها».
ونحكي هنا كلام الكوثري في حسن التقاضي ص ٦٠ بلفظه؛ لما فيه من الفوائد: «ومنشأ الخلاف ادعاء أنَّ تلك الأقوال كلها أقوال أبي حنيفة، هو ما كان يجري عليه أبو حنيفة في تفقيه أصحابه من احتجاجه لأحد الأحكام المحتملة في مسألة وانتصاره له بأدلة، ثم كرّروه بالرد عليه بنقض أدلّته، تدريباً لأصحابه على التفقه على خطوات ومراحل إلى أن يستقرّ الحكم المتعيّن في نهاية التمحيص، ويُدوّن في الديوان في عداد المسائل الممحصة، فمنهم من ترجح عنده غير ما استقر عليه الأمر من تلك الأقوال باجتهاده الخاص، فيكون هذا المترجح عنده قوله من وجه، وقول أبي حنيفة من وجه آخر ، مِنْ حيث إنَّه هو الذي آثار هذا الاحتمال ودلل عليه أوّلاً وإن عدل عنه أخيراً....... والحاصل أنَّ أصحاب أبي حنيفة إنَّما اختاروا في كل مسألة مِنْ أحد الاحتمالات التي أثارها الإمام، ثمّ ما استقر عليه رأي الإمامصار مذهباً له، وما استقر عليه رأي أحد أصحابه نسب إليه».
And it collects the six books: Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim al-Shahid, for it is Al-Kafi. The strongest of its commentaries is that which is like the sun: the Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, relied upon for transmissions; nothing is acted upon contrary to it, nor is anything else relied upon. And know that from Abu Hanifa have come abundant narrations. He chose some of them, and the rest he chose from the rest. (1) In J: 'al-Nufus'. Al-Rifaq (2) Al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) compiled the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, dropping repetitions, in his book 'Al-Kafi', so reliance was upon it in the madhhab. Hajji Khalifa said in Kashf al-Zunun 2:1378: 'It is a relied-upon book in transmitting the madhhab.' Many scholars commented on it, such as al-Isbijabi (d. 480 AH) and Ismail ibn Ya'qub al-Anbari (d. 331 AH). See Kashf al-Zunun 2:1378. The most prominent commentator is Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (d. ca. 500 AH). Al-Tarsusi said: 'The Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is not acted upon in contradiction to it, nor is anything besides it relied upon; no fatwa is given and no reliance is placed except upon it.' See Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 20 and others. Dr. Muhammad Buynukalin said in the introduction of 'Al-Asl' pp. 119-120: 'What we observed from studying Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim is that he abridges the wording of 'Al-Asl' and takes it as a basis, then adds to it what he deems appropriate from Imam Muhammad's other works and sometimes from Abu Yusuf's works, but the basis is 'Al-Asl' and the phrasing is mostly that of 'Al-Asl'... Al-Hakim did a very important task in this book: he compared copies of 'Al-Asl' and recorded differences in many places of Al-Kafi, most relying on the copy of Abu Sulayman and Abu Hafs, but there are references to other copies in few places...' (3) In B: 'Jat'. Then he had no answer, as the companions swore. (1) Its meaning: Several clear, evident statements were reported from Abu Hanifa on the issue. Abu Hanifa chose one narration, and his companions chose the remaining narrations. So all statements reported from his companions are statements of Abu Hanifa that they chose. This is the interpretation of the oath reported from Abu Yusuf and others that all their statements are expressions of Abu Hanifa's statements. This does not contradict that they reached the level of absolute mujtahid; rather, they preferred to attribute to their teacher out of politeness and reverence. Their saying what they said is because their opinion agreed with his opinion in ijtihad. Abu Hanifa's circle was a fiqh circle, and it is natural that all aspects of an issue were presented, then each of them chose a face based on the principles he established. Also, this statement of theirs about not departing from Abu Hanifa's statements is a matter of politeness and humility in response to those who said to them: 'If you had not engaged in independent ijtihad in a separate madhhab, given the great fame they achieved after the Imam, their statement was a refutation of this, even if not entirely true in reality, and Allah knows best.' Al-Uthmani said in Usool al-Ifta' p. 169: 'Its meaning, as verified by Allama al-Kawthari, is that Imam Abu Hanifa used to present different possibilities to his students on a single issue, and his companions would adopt one of these possibilities with its proofs.' We quote al-Kawthari's words in Husn al-Taqadi p. 60 verbatim for its benefits: 'The source of the dispute is the claim that all these statements are statements of Abu Hanifa; this stems from Abu Hanifa's practice in teaching his students: he would argue for one of the possible rulings on an issue and champion it with proofs, then they would refute him by invalidating his proofs, training his students in fiqh step by step until the definitive ruling was settled after scrutiny, and it would be recorded in the diwan among the examined issues. Some of them would prefer something other than what was settled upon according to their own ijtihad, so what they preferred became their statement in one respect, and Abu Hanifa's statement in another, since he was the one who raised the possibility and proved it first, though he later retracted it... The conclusion is that the companions of Abu Hanifa chose in every issue one of the possibilities raised by the Imam; then what the Imam's opinion settled upon became his madhhab, and what one of his companions' opinion settled upon was attributed to him.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' serves a dual purpose. First, it establishes the supreme authority of Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) as the core compilation of Zahir al-Riwayah—the six foundational works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's Al-Mabsut is deemed so authoritative that nothing contrary to it is accepted. This sets a rasm rule: in fatwa, one must rely on Al-Mabsut. Second, the passage addresses the nature of the opinions of Abu Hanifa's major students—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The verse (nazm) states that many narrations came from Abu Hanifa; he chose some, and his students chose the rest. The commentary clarifies that this does not mean the students lacked independent ijtihad. Rather, Abu Hanifa would present multiple legal possibilities in his teaching circle (majlis tafqih). Each student, applying the same usul, might select a different possibility. The students attributed their choices to Abu Hanifa out of adab and humility, not because they were incapable of independent reasoning. The passage relies on the analysis of al-Kawthari and others to explain that the students' statements are in fact selections from Abu Hanifa's own raised possibilities. This is a key concept in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the positions of the students are not extraneous but are part of the Abu Hanifa's living ijtihad.

Key Terms
الكافي (Al-Kafi): A book by Al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) that compiles the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad, dropping repetitions, and serves as the relied-upon source in the Hanafi madhhab.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Al-Mabsut, Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Jami' al-Kabir, Al-Siyar al-Saghir, Al-Siyar al-Kabir, Al-Ziyadat) that contain the authoritative rulings transmitted from Abu Hanifa and his students.
مبسوط السرخسي (Mabsut al-Sarakhsi): The commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (d. ca. 500 AH) on Al-Kafi. It is considered the most relied-upon commentary in the madhhab, equivalent to Al-Kafi itself in authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of Al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi in the Hanafi school?
A) It is one of several commentaries, each equally authoritative.
B) It is not to be relied upon because it contradicts Al-Kafi.
C) It is the most authoritative commentary; nothing contrary to it is accepted, and it is the basis for fatwa.
D) It is a supplementary work not used for fatwa.

Key Takeaway
Al-Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is the ultimate authority for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab, and no ruling contradicting it is valid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
9 min
The Nature of the Companions' Opinions: Selections from Abu Hanifa's Possibilities
Clarifies the relationship between Abu Hanifa's and his students' opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats the opinions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani as part of the madhhab, and describe how they were derived from Abu Hanifa's teaching method.

Core Idea
The companions' opinions are choices from Abu Hanifa's presented possibilities, not independent rulings outside his framework.

A common question in Hanafi methodology is: how can the students of Abu Hanifa be both independent mujtahids and yet attribute their opinions to him? This passage from Ibn Abidin, quoting earlier scholars like al-Kawthari, provides the answer: Abu Hanifa would present multiple legal possibilities in his teaching circle. His companions would adopt one of these possibilities, applying the same usul. Their choices were thus rooted in his ijtihad. Understanding this concept is vital for correctly weighing the authority of opinions within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim from the verse
The verse states that from Abu Hanifa came many narrations; he chose some, and his companions chose the rest. This suggests the companions' opinions are essentially Abu Hanifa's possibilities.
This is the starting point of the discussion.
2
Examine the commentary's explanation
Ibn Abidin explains that the companions reached the level of absolute mujtahid but preferred to attribute their views to their teacher out of adab. More deeply, Abu Hanifa's teaching method involved presenting all possible aspects of an issue.
This explanation harmonizes the students' independence with their attribution.
3
Appreciate al-Kawthari's analysis
Al-Kawthari clarifies that Abu Hanifa would argue for one possibility, then allow his students to refute him, training them. Eventually, each student might settle on a different possibility based on his own ijtihad. Thus, the final opinion of a student is a selection from Abu Hanifa's raised options.
This shows the dynamic pedagogical process.
4
Apply to madhhab understanding
When a difference exists between Abu Hanifa and his students, the mufti must understand that both opinions have roots in Abu Hanifa's usul. The student's opinion is not a complete departure but a valid alternative within the madhhab.
This prevents viewing the companions as mere transmitters.
