(۱) ومعناها وردت عن أبي حنيفة عدة أقوال واضحة بينة في المسألة، فاختار منها أبو حنيفة رواية، واختار أصحابه الروايات الباقية، فكل ما ورد من أقوال عن أصحابه هي أقوال لأبي حنيفة هم اختاروها، وهذا تفسير القسم الوارد عن أبي يوسف وغيره من أنَّ كلَّ أقوالهم هي عبارة عن أقوال لأبي حنيفة، وهذا يخالف حقق في بلوغهم درجة المجتهد المطلق، وإنَّما آثروا الانتساب لشيخهم أدباً وإجلالاً له، فقولهم بما قال إنَّما هو لموافقة رأيهم لرأيه في الاجتهاد، فإنَّ مجلس أبي حنيفة مجلس تفقيه، وَمِنَ الطبيعي أن تعرض فيه كل الوجوه للمسألة، ومَن ثَمّ يختار كل واحدٍ منهم وجهاً اعتماداً على أصوله التي قرّرها. وأيضاً هذا الكلام منهم بعدم خروجهم عن أقوال أبي حنيفة من باب الأدب والتواضع أمام من يقول لهم : لو لم تستقلوا باجتهاد في مذهب منفرد للشهرة العظيمة التي نالوها بعد الإمام فكان كلامهم ردّاً على هذا، وإن لم يكن في الواقع تماماً، والله أعلم.
قال العثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص ١٦٩: ومعناه على ما حققه العلامة الكوثري: أنَّ الإمام أبا حنيفة كان يبدي أمام تلامذته احتمالات مختلفة في مسألة واحدة، وكان أصحابه يأخذون بأحد هذه الاحتمالات بأدلتها».
ونحكي هنا كلام الكوثري في حسن التقاضي ص ٦٠ بلفظه؛ لما فيه من الفوائد: «ومنشأ الخلاف ادعاء أنَّ تلك الأقوال كلها أقوال أبي حنيفة، هو ما كان يجري عليه أبو حنيفة في تفقيه أصحابه من احتجاجه لأحد الأحكام المحتملة في مسألة وانتصاره له بأدلة، ثم كرّروه بالرد عليه بنقض أدلّته، تدريباً لأصحابه على التفقه على خطوات ومراحل إلى أن يستقرّ الحكم المتعيّن في نهاية التمحيص، ويُدوّن في الديوان في عداد المسائل الممحصة، فمنهم من ترجح عنده غير ما استقر عليه الأمر من تلك الأقوال باجتهاده الخاص، فيكون هذا المترجح عنده قوله من وجه، وقول أبي حنيفة من وجه آخر ، مِنْ حيث إنَّه هو الذي آثار هذا الاحتمال ودلل عليه أوّلاً وإن عدل عنه أخيراً....... والحاصل أنَّ أصحاب أبي حنيفة إنَّما اختاروا في كل مسألة مِنْ أحد الاحتمالات التي أثارها الإمام، ثمّ ما استقر عليه رأي الإمامصار مذهباً له، وما استقر عليه رأي أحد أصحابه نسب إليه».
And it collects the six books: Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim al-Shahid, for it is Al-Kafi. The strongest of its commentaries is that which is like the sun: the Mabsut of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, relied upon for transmissions; nothing is acted upon contrary to it, nor is anything else relied upon. And know that from Abu Hanifa have come abundant narrations. He chose some of them, and the rest he chose from the rest. (1) In J: 'al-Nufus'. Al-Rifaq (2) Al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) compiled the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, dropping repetitions, in his book 'Al-Kafi', so reliance was upon it in the madhhab. Hajji Khalifa said in Kashf al-Zunun 2:1378: 'It is a relied-upon book in transmitting the madhhab.' Many scholars commented on it, such as al-Isbijabi (d. 480 AH) and Ismail ibn Ya'qub al-Anbari (d. 331 AH). See Kashf al-Zunun 2:1378. The most prominent commentator is Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (d. ca. 500 AH). Al-Tarsusi said: 'The Mabsut of al-Sarakhsi is not acted upon in contradiction to it, nor is anything besides it relied upon; no fatwa is given and no reliance is placed except upon it.' See Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 20 and others. Dr. Muhammad Buynukalin said in the introduction of 'Al-Asl' pp. 119-120: 'What we observed from studying Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim is that he abridges the wording of 'Al-Asl' and takes it as a basis, then adds to it what he deems appropriate from Imam Muhammad's other works and sometimes from Abu Yusuf's works, but the basis is 'Al-Asl' and the phrasing is mostly that of 'Al-Asl'... Al-Hakim did a very important task in this book: he compared copies of 'Al-Asl' and recorded differences in many places of Al-Kafi, most relying on the copy of Abu Sulayman and Abu Hafs, but there are references to other copies in few places...' (3) In B: 'Jat'. Then he had no answer, as the companions swore. (1) Its meaning: Several clear, evident statements were reported from Abu Hanifa on the issue. Abu Hanifa chose one narration, and his companions chose the remaining narrations. So all statements reported from his companions are statements of Abu Hanifa that they chose. This is the interpretation of the oath reported from Abu Yusuf and others that all their statements are expressions of Abu Hanifa's statements. This does not contradict that they reached the level of absolute mujtahid; rather, they preferred to attribute to their teacher out of politeness and reverence. Their saying what they said is because their opinion agreed with his opinion in ijtihad. Abu Hanifa's circle was a fiqh circle, and it is natural that all aspects of an issue were presented, then each of them chose a face based on the principles he established. Also, this statement of theirs about not departing from Abu Hanifa's statements is a matter of politeness and humility in response to those who said to them: 'If you had not engaged in independent ijtihad in a separate madhhab, given the great fame they achieved after the Imam, their statement was a refutation of this, even if not entirely true in reality, and Allah knows best.' Al-Uthmani said in Usool al-Ifta' p. 169: 'Its meaning, as verified by Allama al-Kawthari, is that Imam Abu Hanifa used to present different possibilities to his students on a single issue, and his companions would adopt one of these possibilities with its proofs.' We quote al-Kawthari's words in Husn al-Taqadi p. 60 verbatim for its benefits: 'The source of the dispute is the claim that all these statements are statements of Abu Hanifa; this stems from Abu Hanifa's practice in teaching his students: he would argue for one of the possible rulings on an issue and champion it with proofs, then they would refute him by invalidating his proofs, training his students in fiqh step by step until the definitive ruling was settled after scrutiny, and it would be recorded in the diwan among the examined issues. Some of them would prefer something other than what was settled upon according to their own ijtihad, so what they preferred became their statement in one respect, and Abu Hanifa's statement in another, since he was the one who raised the possibility and proved it first, though he later retracted it... The conclusion is that the companions of Abu Hanifa chose in every issue one of the possibilities raised by the Imam; then what the Imam's opinion settled upon became his madhhab, and what one of his companions' opinion settled upon was attributed to him.'
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' serves a dual purpose. First, it establishes the supreme authority of Al-Kafi by Al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) as the core compilation of Zahir al-Riwayah—the six foundational works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi's Al-Mabsut is deemed so authoritative that nothing contrary to it is accepted. This sets a rasm rule: in fatwa, one must rely on Al-Mabsut. Second, the passage addresses the nature of the opinions of Abu Hanifa's major students—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The verse (nazm) states that many narrations came from Abu Hanifa; he chose some, and his students chose the rest. The commentary clarifies that this does not mean the students lacked independent ijtihad. Rather, Abu Hanifa would present multiple legal possibilities in his teaching circle (majlis tafqih). Each student, applying the same usul, might select a different possibility. The students attributed their choices to Abu Hanifa out of adab and humility, not because they were incapable of independent reasoning. The passage relies on the analysis of al-Kawthari and others to explain that the students' statements are in fact selections from Abu Hanifa's own raised possibilities. This is a key concept in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the positions of the students are not extraneous but are part of the Abu Hanifa's living ijtihad.

Key Terms
أبو حنيفة (Abu Hanifa): The eponymous founder of the Hanafi school (d. 150 AH). In this passage, he is the source of multiple legal possibilities presented to his students.
أصحاب (as'hab (companions)): Abu Hanifa's major students, especially Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, who reached the level of absolute mujtahid but chose to attribute their opinions to him out of adab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the origin of the companions' opinions (such as those of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani)?
A) They invented completely new rulings independent of Abu Hanifa.
B) They selected from among the various possibilities that Abu Hanifa presented in his teaching circle.
C) They simply memorized and transmitted Abu Hanifa's exact words without any interpretation.
D) They derived rulings from the Quran and Sunnah without reference to Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The companions' opinions are authoritative selections from the legal possibilities raised by Abu Hanifa, reflecting their independent ijtihad within his methodological framework.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Rule of 'Alayhi Aqsam al-Ashab: Origin of Students' Qawls
Explaining the meaning of a key rasm rule about division of opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meaning of 'alayhi aqsam al-ashab' and identify the origin of the students' qawls in Abu Hanifa's own multiple statements.

Core Idea
Students' statements are selections from Abu Hanifa's multiple opinions, not independent ijtihad.

In Hanafi usul al-iftaa, one of the most important rules for a mufti is understanding the hierarchy of statements within the madhhab. This lesson unpacks a key rasm al-mufti term: 'alayhi aqsam al-ashab' — the division of opinions among Abu Hanifa's students. You will learn that the statements of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and others are not independent rulings; rather, they are selections from the many possibilities that Imam Abu Hanifa himself explored in his teaching sessions. This understanding is essential for properly ranking and applying different qawls in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term and its literal meaning
Begin by locating the phrase 'alayhi aqsam al-ashab' in the text. Understand that 'aqsam' means 'divided' and 'ashab' refers to Abu Hanifa's students. The phrase indicates that on a given issue, the students divided—they chose different positions from among Abu Hanifa's multiple statements.
This is not about independent ijtihad but about selecting from the Imam's own expressed possibilities.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's teaching method
The passage explains that Abu Hanifa's council was a 'majlis tafqih' where he would present different possibilities for a ruling, argue for one, then allow students to refute and refine. This process trained them and generated multiple qawls.
Al-Kawthari's quote shows this was a deliberate pedagogical method.
3
Distinguish the students' role from the Imam's final position
After the training, Abu Hanifa would settle on a definitive opinion (his madhhab). Each student might favor a different possibility he had raised earlier. That student's qawl is thus traceable to the Imam, even if it differs from the settled opinion.
This explains why students' qawls are considered part of the Hanafi madhhab but with a lower rank.
4
Apply the rule to fatwa hierarchy
As a mufti, you must know that the Imam's settled qawl is primary; a student's qawl is only followed when the Imam's is unknown or when later tarjih elevates it. This lesson forms the basis for that ranking.
Understanding this prevents incorrectly treating a student's opinion as equal to the Imam's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعناها وردت عن أبي حنيفة عدة أقوال واضحة بينة في المسألة، فاختار منها أبو حنيفة رواية، واختار أصحابه الروايات الباقية، فكل ما ورد من أقوال عن أصحابه هي أقوال لأبي حنيفة هم اختاروها، وهذا تفسير القسم الوارد عن أبي يوسف وغيره من أن كل أقوالهم هي عبارة عن أقوال لأبي حنيفة، وهذا يخالف حقق في بلوغهم درجة المجتهد المطلق، وإنما آثروا الانتساب لشيخهم أدباً وإجلالاً له، فقولهم بما قال إنما هو لموافقة رأيهم لرأيه في الاجتهاد، فإن مجلس أبي حنيفة مجلس تفقيه، ومن الطبيعي أن تعرض فيه كل الوجوه للمسألة، ومن ثم يختار كل واحد منهم وجهاً اعتماداً على أصوله التي قررها. وأيضاً هذا الكلام منهم بعدم خروجهم عن أقوال أبي حنيفة من باب الأدب والتواضع أمام من يقول لهم : لو لم تستقلوا باجتهاد في مذهب منفرد للشهرة العظيمة التي نالوها بعد الإمام فكان كلامهم رداً على هذا، وإن لم يكن في الواقع تماماً، والله أعلم.
قال العثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص ١٦٩: ومعناه على ما حققه العلامة الكوثري: أن الإمام أبا حنيفة كان يبدي أمام تلامذته احتمالات مختلفة في مسألة واحدة، وكان أصحابه يأخذون بأحد هذه الاحتمالات بأدلتها.
ونحكي هنا كلام الكوثري في حسن التقاضي ص ٦٠ بلفظه؛ لما فيه من الفوائد: «ومنشأ الخلاف ادعاء أن تلك الأقوال كلها أقوال أبي حنيفة، هو ما كان يجري عليه أبو حنيفة في تفقيه أصحابه من احتجاجه لأحد الأحكام المحتملة في مسألة وانتصاره له بأدلة، ثم كرروه بالرد عليه بنقض أدلته، تدريباً لأصحابه على التفقه على خطوات ومراحل إلى أن يستقر الحكم المتعين في نهاية التمحيص، ويدون في الديوان في عداد المسائل الممحصة، فمنهم من ترجح عنده غير ما استقر عليه الأمر من تلك الأقوال باجتهاده الخاص، فيكون هذا المترجح عنده قوله من وجه، وقول أبي حنيفة من وجه آخر، من حيث إنه هو الذي أثار هذا الاحتمال ودلل عليه أولاً وإن عدل عنه أخيراً....... والحاصل أن أصحاب أبي حنيفة إنما اختاروا في كل مسألة من أحد الاحتمالات التي أثارها الإمام، ثم ما استقر عليه رأي الإمام صار مذهباً له، وما استقر عليه رأي أحد أصحابه نسب إليه».
Its meaning: multiple clear statements from Abu Hanifa were transmitted on a single issue; among these Abu Hanifa chose one narration, and his companions chose the remaining narrations. So every statement that came from his companions is actually a statement of Abu Hanifa that they selected. This is the interpretation of the statement reported from Abu Yusuf and others that all their statements are expressions of Abu Hanifa's statements. This contradicts what is verified about them reaching the level of absolute mujtahid, but they preferred to attribute themselves to their teacher out of respect and veneration. Their statement of what they said is only because their opinion agreed with his opinion in ijtihad. For the council of Abu Hanifa was a council of fiqh study (tafqih), and it is natural that all aspects of an issue were presented there; then each one would choose a perspective based on his own principles. Also, this statement of theirs about not departing from Abu Hanifa's statements is a matter of etiquette and humility before those who might question them, and not because it was entirely true in reality, and Allah knows best. Al-Uthmani said in Usul al-Ifta' p. 169: Its meaning, as verified by al-Kawthari, is that Imam Abu Hanifa would present different possibilities to his students on a single issue, and his companions would adopt one of these possibilities with its evidence. And we will quote al-Kawthari's words from Hasan al-Taqadi p. 60 verbatim, for they contain benefits: 'The origin of the disagreement is the claim that all those statements are statements of Abu Hanifa, which is based on what Abu Hanifa used to do in teaching his companions: he would argue for one of the possible rulings on an issue and defend it with evidence, then they would respond and refute his evidence, training his companions in fiqh study step by step until the definite ruling was settled upon after examination and recorded in the collection among the settled issues. Some of them favored a different position based on their own ijtihad, so that favored position became their statement from one perspective and Abu Hanifa's statement from another perspective, in that he had raised that possibility and argued for it initially, even if he later retracted it. In summary, Abu Hanifa's companions each chose one of the possibilities raised by the Imam, and then the settled opinion of the Imam became his madhhab, and the settled opinion of one of his companions was attributed to him.'
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage explains a key rasm al-mufti rule: the division of opinions among Abu Hanifa's closest students (the sahibayn and others). The text clarifies a common misunderstanding: the students did not invent their own independent qawls; rather, they selected from among the multiple opinions that Abu Hanifa himself had expressed during his teaching sessions. Abu Hanifa would present different possibilities and argue for one, then allow his students to refute it, training them in ijtihad. Ultimately, each student chose one of those possibilities that they saw as strongest. Thus, their statements are traceable to Abu Hanifa's teaching. Al-Kawthari’s lengthy quote explains that the settled opinion of the Imam became his madhhab, while the opinion of a student — even if differing from the Imam’s final choice — is attributed to that student, yet rooted in the Imam’s initial exploration. This shows the deep organic connection between Abu Hanifa and his school.

Key Terms
عليه أقسم الأصحاب (alayhi aqsam al-ashab): The division of opinions among Abu Hanifa's students (ashab) on a given issue, where each student adopted one of the Imam's multiple statements.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The rules and principles that guide a mufti in issuing fatwas, including the hierarchy of qawls and the procedure for tarjih.
مجتهد مطلق (mujtahid mutlaq): An absolute mujtahid who can derive rulings directly from the primary sources without being bound by a specific madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the statements of Abu Hanifa's students considered part of his madhhab?
A) Because the students never disagreed with the Imam.
B) Because the students selected their statements from the multiple possibilities Abu Hanifa expressed.
C) Because the students' ijtihad always resulted in the same ruling as the Imam.
D) Because the students only transmitted the Imam's final opinions.

Key Takeaway
The rule 'alayhi aqsam al-ashab' establishes that students' qawls originate from Abu Hanifa's multiple opinions, ensuring that the mufti understands their subordinate rank in the fatwa hierarchy.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Hierarchy of Hanafi Imams for Fatwa When Abu Hanifa Has No Qawl
Rule for preferring qawls when Abu Hanifa's qawl is absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of authorities for fatwa when Abu Hanifa has no explicit qawl, and apply the rule to determine which imam's qawl is taken in a given scenario.

Core Idea
When Abu Hanifa has no qawl, the mufti follows Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar, then al-Hasan ibn Ziyad in order of descending ijtihad status.

In the Hanafi madhhab, when a mufti encounters a case that has no explicit ruling from Abu Hanifa himself, a clear hierarchy exists for whose opinion should be adopted. This hierarchy is not arbitrary but based on the relative strength of each imam's usul (methodological principles). Understanding this order is essential for correct fatwa practice, especially when the Imam's own view is absent. This lesson unpacks the sequence and its underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary hierarchy
Read the passage carefully and list the four mujtahids in the order they should be consulted when Abu Hanifa's qawl is absent.
The order is: Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, al-Hasan ibn Ziyad.
2
Understand the basis of tarjih
Recognize that preference among these mujtahids is based on their status in ijtihad, determined by the soundness of their usul, not on external evidence like hadith.
This is a key point distinguishing Hanafi tarjih from other methods.
3
Distinguish between deduction and application
Note the passage's comment that authors always prefer Abu Hanifa's statement in deduction (istinbat) but may adopt companions' statements in application (tatbiq) due to necessity.
This explains why the fatwa may follow a companion's view despite the Imam's superior derivation.
4
Identify the exception clause
Look at the phrase 'Wa qila bil-takhyir fi fatwahu in khalafa al-Imam sahibahu' and understand that when both companions oppose the Imam, the mufti may choose freely.
This is a disputed point: some say the mufti may choose, others insist on the Imam's view.
5
Apply the hierarchy to a hypothetical
Assume you find no qawl from Abu Hanifa on a new issue, but you have qawls from Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar. Which one do you take, and why?
You take Abu Yusuf's first, unless there is a reason to prefer another under the takhyir exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المختار
وحيث لم يوجد له اختيار فقول يعقوب هو محمد فقوله الحسن ثم زفر وابن زياد الحسن وقيل بالتخيير في فتواه إن خالف الإمام صاحباه )
(۱) ومعناه: إن لم نجد قولاً لأبي حنيفة في مسألة فنأخذ بقول أبي يوسف إن وجد، وإن لم يوجد نأخذ بقول محمد بن الحسن، فإن لم يوجد نأخذ بقول زفر أو الحسن بن زياد، فهذا يدل على أن الترجيح عندهم يعتمد على مكانة المجتهد، فمن ارتفعت مكانته قدم ترجيحه. وهذا الترتيب الموجود للترجيح على حسب المكانة في الاجتهاد، فمن كانت أصوله أحكم وأقوى كان ترجيحه أفضل، فالترجيح بين الاجتهادات مبني على قوة الاجتهاد المعتمد على أحكم الأصول، ولم يرجحوا بينهم بظاهر الحديث مثلاً كما يفعل الآن؛ لعدم انتباههم لهذه الفائدة الدقيقة؛ لذلك نجد المؤلفين لا يقدمون على قول أبي حنيفة قول أحد من أصحابه من جهة الاستدلال، فدائماً يرجحون قوله أبي حنيفة من جهة الاستنباط، ولكن يرجحون قول أصحابه من جهة التطبيق، فبعد أن يفصلوا في الاستدلال لقول أبي حنيفة يقولون: والفتوى على قول محمد؛ للضرورة مثلاً، وانظر إلى فعل صاحب الاختيار» و«الهداية» تجد مصداق هذا.
The chosen rule: And when there is no choice for him (Abu Hanifa) in a matter, then the statement of Ya'qub (Abu Yusuf) [is taken], then if not, the statement of Muhammad (al-Shaybani), then the statement of al-Hasan (al-Shaybani? actually Zufar), then Zufar and Ibn Ziyad al-Hasan. And it was said that he (the mufti) may choose in his fatwa if the Imam (Abu Hanifa) is opposed by his two companions. (1) Its meaning: if we do not find a statement from Abu Hanifa on an issue, we take Abu Yusuf's statement if found; if not, we take Muhammad ibn al-Hasan's statement; if not found, we take Zufar's or al-Hasan ibn Ziyad's statement. This indicates that tarjih (preference) among them depends on the status of the mujtahid: whoever has higher status, his preference is given precedence. This order of preference is according to status in ijtihad: whoever has more sound and stronger usul (principles), his preference is better. Tarjih between ijtihads is based on the strength of ijtihad relying on the soundest principles. They did not prefer among them based on the apparent (zahir) of a hadith, for example, as is done now, due to their lack of attention to this subtle benefit. Thus we find that authors do not prefer a statement of any of his companions over Abu Hanifa's statement in terms of istidlal (deduction); they always prefer Abu Hanifa's statement in terms of istinbat (derivation), but they prefer his companions' statements in terms of application. After they detail the deduction for Abu Hanifa's statement, they say: 'And the fatwa is according to Muhammad's statement, due to necessity, for example.' Look at the action of the author of al-Ikhtiyar and al-Hidayah, you will find this confirmed.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents the established order of taking qawls in the Hanafi madhhab when Abu Hanifa himself has no explicit chosen qawl. The hierarchy is: first Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar, then al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. The basis for this order is the rank of the mujtahid in ijtihad strength, determined by the soundness of his usul (methodological principles). The passage also notes that later authors do not place any companion's statement above Abu Hanifa's in terms of deduction; the Imam's position is always superior in derivation. However, in practice (application), they may adopt a companion's view due to necessity or changed circumstances, as seen in works like al-Ikhtiyar and al-Hidayah. This is a critical refinement: the hierarchy is for fatwa when Abu Hanifa's own view is absent, and the tarjih is based on the strength of ijtihad, not on external evidence like a hadith.

Key Terms
المختار (al-mukhtar): The selected/relied-upon opinion in the madhhab regarding the hierarchy of taking qawls.
ترجيح (tarjih): Preferring one mujtahid's qawl over another based on the strength of his usul and status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first authority to be consulted in fatwa when Abu Hanifa has no qawl on an issue?
A) Muhammad al-Shaybani
B) Zufar
C) Abu Yusuf
D) Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad

Key Takeaway
When Abu Hanifa's qawl is absent, the mufti follows a strict hierarchy based on the ijtihad status of the companions: Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar, then al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, unless the imam is opposed by both companions, in which case choice is allowed.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Fatwa Rules When Abu Hanifa Agrees or Disagrees with His Companions
Rules for preferring combined opinions of Imam and companions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti hierarchy to determine the mufta bihi in cases of agreement or disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his companions.

Core Idea
When Abu Hanifa and at least one companion agree on a fatwa, it is binding — deviation only for necessity.

This lesson unpacks a critical rule from Rasm al-Mufti: how a Hanafi mufti determines which opinion to give fatwa upon when the founding Imam and his two main students differ. The passage from Ibn Abidin's compilation, citing Qadi Khan, provides clear scenarios and their resolutions. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for any serious fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The passage describes four situations: (1) Imam + both companions agree, (2) Imam + one companion agree, (3) both companions oppose the Imam, (4) Imam alone vs each companion separately. List them.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For (1) and (2), the joint opinion is binding. For (3), the ruling depends on the subject matter. For (4), the Imam's opinion is preferred.
3
Apply the exceptions
Note that deviation from joint opinion is allowed only for necessity. In time-bound issues and transactions, the companions' view is taken due to changed circumstances or later consensus.
4
Synthesize the hierarchy
Combine the rules into a decision tree for the mufti: first check if Imam+companion agree; if not, check if both oppose and categorize the issue; otherwise, give preference to Imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) فالحاصل أنه إذا اتفق أبو حنيفة وصاحباه على جواب لم يجز العدول عنه إلا لضرورة، وكذا إذا وافقه أحدهما، قال قاضي خان في فتاواه ۱ : ۱ : وإن كانت المسألة مختلفاً فيها بين أصحابنا: فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه يأخذ بقولهما ـ أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه ـ؛ لوفور الشرائط، واستجماع أدلّة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر وزمان: كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال الناس، وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك، وفيما سوى ذلك يخير المفتي المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه، وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة». وأمّا إذا انفرد عنهما بجواب وخالفاه فيه، فإن انفرد كل منهما بجواب أيضاً بأن لم يتفقا على شيء واحد، فالظاهر ترجيح قوله أيضاً، ينظر : شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٢٦.
(2) In summary: if Abu Hanifa and his two companions agree on an answer, it is not permissible to deviate from it except for necessity. Likewise if one of them agrees with him. Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa 1:1: 'If the issue is disputed among our scholars: if with Abu Hanifa is one of his two companions, one takes the statement of both (i.e., the Imam and the one who agrees with him) due to the abundance of conditions and the gathering of correct evidence in it. If his two companions both oppose him: if their disagreement is one of era and time, like ruling based on apparent justice ('adala), one takes the statement of the two companions due to change in people's situations. In sharecropping (muzara'ah), mu'amalah (transaction), and the like, one chooses their statement due to the consensus of the later scholars on that. In cases other than that, the mufti who is a mujtahid may choose, and act upon what his opinion leads to. And Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: One takes the statement of Abu Hanifa.' As for when he (Abu Hanifa) is alone with his answer and both oppose him, if each gives a separate answer (do not agree on one thing), then apparently his statement is also given preference. See: Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 26.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage lays down detailed rules for determining the fatwa when Abu Hanifa and his companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are in agreement or disagreement. The ruling is: if the Imam and at least one companion agree, that joint opinion must be followed unless there is a pressing necessity. If both companions disagree with the Imam, the mufti must consider the nature of the disagreement: if it relates to time-bound issues (e.g., judging by apparent justice, which changes over time), the companions' view is taken because social circumstances have changed. Similarly, in transactions like muzara'ah, later consensus supports the companions. In other matters, a mufti who has ijtihad may choose. The passage also cites the opinion of Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, who insists on taking Abu Hanifa's view alone. When the Imam stands alone against both companions, and each companion also differs from the other, the Imam's view is still preferred. These are precise tasilat (detailed rulings) for the mufti's practice.

Key Terms
صاحباه (sahibahu): Abu Hanifa's two main students: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
العدول عنه (al-udul 'anhu): Deviation from a fatwa ruled jointly by Abu Hanifa and a companion, only allowed for necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Qadi Khan, what should the mufti do if Abu Hanifa's two companions both disagree with him in a matter of sharecropping (muzara'ah)?
A) Take Abu Hanifa's view because he is the Imam.
B) Take the companions' view due to later consensus.
C) Choose freely as a mujtahid.
D) Refer to a hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufti must prioritize the joint opinion of Imam and at least one companion; only in specific, well-defined cases may he deviate to the companions' view or his own ijtihad.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
8 min
Hierarchy of Hanafi Mujtahids and Rules of Tarjih
Rasm rule defining mufti's hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rasm al-mufti hierarchy to determine the preferred opinion for fatwa, and identify exceptions when the mujtahid mufti may choose.

Core Idea
For fatwa, follow: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then others—unless circumstances change or you are a mujtahid mufti.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti provides the essential decision tree for any Hanafi mufti. When faced with multiple positions within the school, the mufti must know the order of preference among the founding Imams. However, this hierarchy is not absolute; exceptions exist for changed customs and for muftis who themselves possess ijtihad. Let's unpack the rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default hierarchy
List the order: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, then Zufar, then Hasan ibn Ziyad. This order is based on the strength of their usul (principles).
If a ruling from a higher-rank imam exists, it should be followed first.
2
Recognize when the hierarchy is modified
When Abu Hanifa is opposed by both companions (Sahibayn) and the issue involves changing customs (e.g., qada' by apparent 'adala) or transactions (muzara'ah, mu'amalah), the companions' view is taken due to later consensus.
This exception is based on change of times and practical necessity.
3
Distinguish between a mujtahid mufti and a non-mujtahid mufti
A mujtahid mufti (one who can perform ijtihad within the madhhab) may choose based on strength of proof; a non-mujtahid mufti must follow the fixed hierarchy strictly.
The passage notes that after the fourth century, associated mujtahids (mujtahid muntasib) ceased, so most muftis today are non-mujtahid.
4
Understand the two meanings of 'tarjih by strength of proof'
Tarjih can refer to (a) principles of deduction (usul al-istinbat) for the associated mujtahid, or (b) principles of construction/application (usul al-bina') for the mujtahid in the madhhab.
This distinction clarifies that the hierarchy is not about superficial proof but about methodological rank.
5
Apply the rule to a non-mujtahid mufti today
For a non-mujtahid mufti, always start with Abu Hanifa's view; if absent, proceed down the list. Only deviate when the issue falls under the exceptions for custom or transactions.
This ensures consistency and avoids arbitrary selection.

(۲) فالحاصل أنه إذا اتفق أبو حنيفة وصاحباه على جواب لم يجز العدول عنه إلا لضرورة، وكذا إذا وافقه أحدهما، قال قاضي خان في فتاواه ۱ : ۱ : وإن كانت المسألة مختلفاً فيها بين أصحابنا: فإن كان مع أبي حنيفة أحد صاحبيه يأخذ بقولهما ـ أي بقول الإمام ومن وافقه ـ؛ لوفور الشّرائط، واستجماع أدلّة الصواب فيها. وإن خالفه صاحباه في ذلك فإن كان اختلافهم اختلاف عصر وزمان: كالقضاء بظاهر العدالة، يأخذ بقول صاحبيه؛ لتغيير أحوال النّاس، وفي المزارعة والمعاملة ونحوها يختار قولهما؛ لإجماع المتأخرين على ذلك، وفيما سوى ذلك يخيّر المفتي المجتهد، ويعمل بما أفضى إليه رأيه، وقال عبد الله بن المبارك: يأخذ بقول أبي حنيفة». وأمّا إذا انفرد عنهما بجواب وخالفاه فيه، فإن انفرد كل منهما بجواب أيضاً بأن لم يتفقا على شيء واحد، فالظاهر ترجيح قوله أيضاً ، ينظر : شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٢٦. ثم وقيل: مَن دليله أقوى رجح وذا لمفتِ ذى اجتهاد الأصح ) فالآن لا ترجيح بالدليل فليس إلا القول بالتفصيل) وهذا تأكيد على الفكرة السابقة في الترجيح بقوّة الاجتهاد، فجعل بعضُهم اجتماع اجتهاد الصاحبين مساوِ لاجتهاد أبي حنيفة بحيث يتخيّر المفتي بينهما، ولكن هذا شرط للمفتي المجتهد كما قال قاضي خان، وإن لم يكن مجتهداً يلتزم العمل بقول أبي حنيفة. (۱) ومعناه : الترجيح بينهم بقوّة الدليل، وهو على معنين: ١. إن قصدنا به أصول الاستنباط، فتكون هذه وظيفة المجتهد المنتسب، حيث لهم بعض الأصول التي خالفوا فيها، فيكون ترجيح بين قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه بالنسبة للأصول التي اختارها المجتهد المنتسب، وإلا لن يكون قول أبي حنيفة مرجوحاً بالنظر إلى أصوله، ولن يكون قول الصاحبين مرجوحاً بالنظر إلى أُصولهم؛ لأنَّ الترجيح لا يكون إلا بالأصول كما سبق. ٢. إن قصدنا به أصول البناء وأصول التطبيق، فتكون هذه وظيفة المجتهد المنتسب والمجتهد في المذهب، فهما يرجحان بين الأقوال بالنظر إلى هذين الأصلين، والله أعلم. (۲) في ج: «الترجيح». ومعناه: قد علمت أن الأصحَ تخيير المفتي المجتهد، فيفتي بما يكون دليله أقوى، ولا يلزمه المشي على التفصيل السابق من اعتبار قول أبي حنيفة أولاً ثم أبي يوسف، وهكذا. ولكن لما انقطع المجتهد المنتسب بعد القرن الرابع، ولم يبق إلا الترجيح بالاعتماد على أصول البناء وأصول التطبيق مِنْ قِبَل المجتهد في المذهب، ومن لم يقدر على الاجتهاد مِنَ المفتين، وهو حال عامة المفتين، فعليه التزام التفصيل السابق مِنَ الإفتاء أوّلاً بقول أبي حنيفة وهكذا.
Then the preferred [view]: and where there is no choice for him, then the saying of Ya'qub [Abu Yusuf], then Muhammad, then his [i.e., Muhammad's] saying al-Hasan, then Zufar and Ibn Ziyad al-Hasan. And it was said: he has a choice in his fatwa if the Imam is opposed by his two companions. Its meaning: If we do not find a saying of Abu Hanifa on an issue, we take the saying of Abu Yusuf if found; if not found, we take the saying of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan; if not found, we take the saying of Zufar or al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. This indicates that tarjih according to them depends on the rank of the mujtahid; so whoever's rank is higher, his tarjih is preferred. This existing order of tarjih is according to rank in ijtihad; so whoever's principles are more solid and stronger, his tarjih is better. Tarjih between ijtihads is based on the strength of ijtihad relying on the most solid principles. They did not give preference between them by apparent hadith as is done now, due to their inattention to this precise benefit. Therefore we find authors do not prefer any of his companions' sayings over Abu Hanifa's saying from the standpoint of inference; they always prefer Abu Hanifa's saying from the standpoint of deduction, but they prefer his companions' sayings from the standpoint of application. So after they detail the inference for Abu Hanifa's saying, they say: 'The fatwa is on the saying of Muhammad' due to necessity, for example. And look at the practice of the author of al-Ikhtiyar and al-Hidaya, you will find confirmation of this. (2) The upshot is that if Abu Hanifa and his two companions agree on an answer, it is not permissible to deviate from it except for necessity. Similarly if one of them agrees with him. Qadi Khan said in his Fatawa: 'If the issue is disputed among our companions: if Abu Hanifa has one of his two companions with him, one takes their saying — i.e., the saying of the Imam and whoever agrees with him — due to abundance of conditions and collection of proofs of correctness therein. If his two companions oppose him in that, then if their difference is a difference of era and time, like judging by apparent uprightness, one takes the saying of the two companions due to the change in people's conditions. In the case of muzara'ah and mu'amalah and the like, one chooses their saying due to the consensus of later scholars on that. In other than that, the mujtahid mufti is given a choice, and acts according to what his opinion leads to. 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak said: 'One takes the saying of Abu Hanifa.' As for when he is alone with an answer and they oppose him in it, if each of them is also alone with an answer, that is, they did not agree on one thing, then apparently his saying is also preferred. See: Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 26. Then: 'And it was said: Whoever's proof is stronger is preferred, and this is for a mufti possessing ijtihad al-asahh.' So now there is no tarjih by proof; there is only the saying with detail. This is an emphasis on the previous idea of tarjih by strength of ijtihad, so some made the combined ijtihad of the two companions equal to the ijtihad of Abu Hanifa such that the mufti is given a choice between them, but this is a condition for the mujtahid mufti as Qadi Khan said. If he is not a mujtahid, he must adhere to acting on Abu Hanifa's saying. (1) Its meaning: tarjih between them by strength of proof, and it has two meanings: 1. If we mean by it the principles of deduction, then this is the function of the associated mujtahid, as they have some principles in which they differ; so there is tarjih between the saying of Abu Hanifa and his two companions with respect to the principles chosen by the associated mujtahid. Otherwise, the saying of Abu Hanifa would not be outweighed with respect to his principles, nor would the saying of the two companions be outweighed with respect to their principles, because tarjih is only by principles as previously. 2. If we mean by it the principles of construction and the principles of application, then this is the function of the associated mujtahid and the mujtahid in the madhhab; they both give tarjih between sayings with respect to these two principles. And Allah knows best. (2) In [manuscript] J: 'al-tarjih'. Its meaning: you know that the soundest view is that the mujtahid mufti has a choice, so he gives fatwa according to whose proof is stronger, and he is not obligated to follow the previous detail of first considering Abu Hanifa's saying, then Abu Yusuf, and so on. However, since the associated mujtahid ceased after the fourth century, and only tarjih remains relying on the principles of construction and the principles of application by the mujtahid in the madhhab, and for those muftis who cannot perform ijtihad, which is the case of most muftis, they must adhere to the previous detail of giving fatwa first by Abu Hanifa's saying and so on.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage from Ibn Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti is a rasm rule: it lays down the methodological hierarchy for issuing fatwas within the Hanafi madhhab. The central principle is that when a mufti cannot find a ruling from Abu Hanifa, he proceeds in a fixed order: first Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, then Zufar, then al-Hasan ibn Ziyad. This order reflects the relative rank of these mujtahids in the Hanafi school. The text clarifies that tarjih among their opinions is based on the strength of their usul (principles of ijtihad), not on external evidence like a hadith that might appear stronger. However, there are exceptions: when Abu Hanifa is joined by one of his two companions (Abu Yusuf or Muhammad), their combined authority outweighs a lone opinion; when both companions agree against Abu Hanifa, the mufti may still choose Abu Hanifa's opinion unless the issue concerns changing customs (like qada' by apparent 'adala) or transactions (muzara'ah, mu'amalah), where later consensus supports the companions. For a mujtahid mufti, tarjih by strength of proof is permissible; but after the fourth century, when associated mujtahids (mujtahid muntasib) became extinct, the mufti must follow the strict hierarchy: first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, etc. This passage thus provides the mufti with a clear decision tree for resolving ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المجتهد المنتسب (al-mujtahid al-muntasib): A mujtahid who follows a particular madhhab (here Hanafi) and has the ability to deduce rulings within its principles, but not absolutely. He can perform tarjih between opinions of the founders.
أصول الاستنباط (usul al-istinbat): The principles of legal derivation used by the mujtahid to extract rulings from sources.
أصول البناء (usul al-bina'): The principles of construction (or application) used to weigh and choose between existing rulings in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an exception where the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) is preferred over Abu Hanifa's?
A) Any case where the Sahibayn have a stronger proof.
B) Cases concerning changes in customs (e.g., judicial testimony) and transactions (muzara'ah).
C) When the Sahibayn outnumber Abu Hanifa.
D) When the mufti is a mujtahid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa hierarchy prioritizes Abu Hanifa, but exceptions for changing customs and later consensus may shift reliance to his companions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Preference Among Founders and the Role of Ijtihad
Explains the rule for preferring opinions among the founders based on mufti's ijtihad level

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for preferring opinions among the founding imams based on the mufti's level of ijtihad, distinguishing between mujtahid and non-mujtahid muftis.

Core Idea
Only a mujtahid mufti may prefer by evidence; non-mujtahid muftis must follow the fixed ranking.

In the Hanafi tradition, the authority of a mufti to choose between the opinions of the founding imams depends on his level of ijtihad. This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti clarifies a key rule: while a mujtahid mufti may give fatwa based on the strongest evidence, a non-mujtahid mufti is bound to a strict order—first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct fatwa practice and prevents arbitrary selection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of mufti
The passage distinguishes between a mujtahid mufti (who has ijtihad) and a non-mujtahid mufti. Determine which category applies to most muftis after the fourth century.
The mujtahid mufti here includes the affiliated mujtahid (mujtahid muntasib) and the mujtahid within the madhhab (mujtahid fi al-madhhab).
2
Understand the ruling for each category
For a mujtahid mufti, preference is based on strength of evidence. For a non-mujtahid mufti, preference is a fixed ranking: Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad, etc.
The fixed ranking is the default; deviation only occurs if a later authority has explicitly preferred another opinion.
3
Parse the two meanings of 'tarjih bi al-dalil'
Preference by evidence can refer to (1) using the fundamentals of deduction (usul al-istinbat), which is the domain of the affiliated mujtahid, or (2) using the fundamentals of construction and application (usul al-bina' wa al-tatbiq), which applies to the mujtahid in the madhhab.
After the fourth century, only the second meaning remains relevant because the affiliated mujtahid no longer exists.
4
Apply the rule to a modern scenario
Given a contemporary mufti who is not a mujtahid, he must start with Abu Hanifa's opinion. Only if a later Hanafi master has explicitly preferred another opinion (e.g., via tarjih) may he follow that, but this itself is part of the madhhab's internal development.
The modern mufti's role is primarily to apply pre-existing tarjih, not to perform new ijtihad.

(۱) ومعناه : الترجيح بينهم بقوّة الدليل، وهو على معنين: ١. إن قصدنا به أصول الاستنباط، فتكون هذه وظيفة المجتهد المنتسب، حيث لهم بعض الأصول التي خالفوا فيها، فيكون ترجيح بين قول أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه بالنسبة للأصول التي اختارها المجتهد المنتسب، وإلا لن يكون قول أبي حنيفة مرجوحاً بالنظر إلى أصوله، ولن يكون قول الصاحبين مرجوحاً بالنظر إلى أُصولهم؛ لأنَّ الترجيح لا يكون إلا بالأصول كما سبق.

For Professor Dr. Salah Abu al-Hajj. And it was said: Whoever's evidence is stronger, his opinion is preferred, and this is for a mufti who has ijtihad. The correct view: Now there is no preference by evidence, so there remains only the detailed ranking. And this is a confirmation of the previous idea regarding preference by strength of ijtihad. For some made the combined ijtihad of the two companions equal to Abu Hanifa's ijtihad such that the mufti may choose between them, but this is a condition for the mujtahid mufti as Qadi Khan said. And if he is not a mujtahid, he is bound to act by the opinion of Abu Hanifa. (1) Its meaning: preference among them by strength of evidence, and it has two meanings: 1. If we intend by it the fundamentals of deduction, then this is the function of the affiliated mujtahid, because they have some fundamentals in which they differed. Thus there is preference between the opinion of Abu Hanifa and his two companions with respect to the fundamentals chosen by the affiliated mujtahid. Otherwise, Abu Hanifa's opinion would not be outweighed from the perspective of his own fundamentals, and the companions' opinion would not be outweighed from the perspective of their fundamentals, because preference is only by fundamentals as previously. 2. If we intend by it the fundamentals of construction and the fundamentals of application, then this is the function of the affiliated mujtahid and the mujtahid in the madhhab. They both prefer between opinions with respect to these two fundamentals. And Allah knows best. (2) In [text] J: 'al-tarjih'. Its meaning: You have known that the correct view is that the mujtahid mufti may choose, so he gives fatwa according to whichever has stronger evidence, and he is not obliged to follow the previous detailed ranking of considering Abu Hanifa's opinion first, then Abu Yusuf, and so on. But when the affiliated mujtahid ceased after the fourth century, and nothing remained except preference by relying on the fundamentals of construction and the fundamentals of application by the mujtahid in the madhhab, and those who cannot perform ijtihad among the muftis, which is the situation of most muftis, then he is obliged to follow the previous detailed ranking of giving fatwa first by Abu Hanifa's opinion and so on.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a rasm_rule establishing the hierarchy of preference among the founding imams of the Hanafi madhhab. The text first presents an opinion that preference is based on strength of evidence, but then clarifies that this only applies to a mujtahid mufti. For others, the rule is a fixed ranking: first Abu Hanifa, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad al-Shaybani, etc. The commentary further distinguishes two types of preference: one based on the fundamentals of deduction (usul al-istinbat), which is the domain of the affiliated mujtahid, and another based on the fundamentals of construction and application (usul al-bina' wa al-tatbiq), which applies to the mujtahid in the madhhab. After the fourth century, the affiliated mujtahid disappeared, leaving only the second type. Thus, for current muftis who are not mujtahids, they must strictly follow the established ranking.

Key Terms
مجتهد منتسب (mujtahid muntasib): A mujtahid affiliated with a madhhab, who can deduce rulings using the foundations of the imam but may differ in some subsidiary principles.
مجتهد في المذهب (mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A mujtahid within the madhhab, who can prefer among existing opinions using the fundamentals of construction and application but cannot deduce new rulings from primary sources.
أصول البناء وأصول التطبيق (usul al-bina' wa usul al-tatbiq): Fundamentals of construction and application: principles used to derive specific rulings from general maxims and to apply them to new cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the duty of a mufti who is not a mujtahid regarding the opinions of Abu Hanifa and his companions?
A) He may choose the opinion with the strongest evidence.
B) He must follow the opinion of Abu Hanifa first, then Abu Yusuf, and so on.
C) He must only follow the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
D) He may issue fatwa based on his own ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
The mufti's ability to prefer by evidence is contingent on his level of ijtihad; without it, he must follow the fixed ranking: Abu Hanifa first, then Abu Yusuf, then Muhammad.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Hierarchy of Mufti and Reliance on Preferred Opinions
Explaining the binding nature of mujtahid opinions on the mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the ranks of authority in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy and apply the rule for taking the preferred opinion (rajih) from the school's mujtahids and later scholars.

Core Idea
A Hanafi mufti is bound by the preferred opinions of the school's mujtahids; only when no clear ruling exists may he turn to the majority of later scholars.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti lays out the hierarchical chain of authority from the absolute mujtahid to the layperson. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for a mufti to know which opinions carry binding force and when to rely on later scholars' consensus. The text also illustrates how the school's mujtahids sometimes preferred the opinions of Zufr, showing the dynamic nature of tarjih within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hierarchy layers
List the five ranks mentioned: Quran/Sunnah → absolute mujtahid → mujtahid fi al-madhhab → mufti → layperson. Note that each rank's opinion is binding on the next.
The absolute mujtahid (e.g., Abu Hanifa) derives from primary sources; the mujtahid fi al-madhhab (e.g., Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) applies the school's methodology.
2
Understand binding authority
Recognize that the mufti is not free to choose any opinion; he must follow the preferred (rajih) opinion as determined by the mujtahid fi al-madhhab. This is analogous to the layperson's obligation to follow the mufti.
The ruling passes through these filters to ensure reliability.
3
Analyze the rule for preferred opinions
The mufti first looks for a clear correction (tasih) from the mujtahid fi al-madhhab. If not found, he turns to the apparent preference (zahir al-riwaya) in the books. If still uncertain, he consults the majority of later scholars (muta'akhkhirun).
This ensures consistency while allowing for adaptation.
4
Explore the role of later scholars
When early scholars (Abu Hanifa and his students) have no explicit ruling, the later scholars' single opinion is taken; if they differ, the majority opinion of recognized figures like al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs, etc. is followed.
The passage quotes al-Maqdisi's al-Hawi al-Qudsi to support this.
5
Examine the practical example
Note that the mujtahids preferred Zufr's opinion in seventeen (or twenty, per Ibn Abidin) issues. This shows tarjih is not static and can evolve with scholarly analysis.
Ibn Abidin's correction underscores the importance of verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما لم يكن خلافه المصححا فنأخذ الذي لهم قد وضحا رجحوا مقال بعض صحبه وصححوا فإننا نراهمو قد من ذاك ما قد رجحوا لزفر مقاله في سبعة وعشر علمائنا ذوى الدراية تأخروا يرجع الذي عليه الأكثر إذا لم توجد واختلف الذين قد تأخروا الرواية عن مثل الطحاوي وأبي حفص وأبي جعفر والليث الشهر. ومعناه: أننا نلتزم بما صحح المجتهدون في المذهب من أقوال، فأقوال المجتهدين في المذهب هي الحجة في حق المفتي، كما أن قول المجتهد المطلق حجة في حق المجتهد في المذهب، وقول المفتي حجة في حق العامي، فهي مراتب يسير فيها الحكم حتى يصل إلى العامي، فيبدأ بالقرآن والسنة ثم المجتهد المطلق ثم المجتهد في المذهب ثم المفتي ثم العامي، فلا يصل إلى العامي إلا بعد مروره بعدة مراحل في الفحص والتمحيص. فإن لم يجد المفتي تصحيحاً للمجتهد في المذهب يعلم أن الراجح ظاهر عبارات الكتب من ذكر ظاهر الرواية، فيلتزم العمل به. ومعناه: أننا نرى أن المجتهدين في المذهب رجحوا كثيراً من أقوال أصحاب أبي حنيفة؛ لأن المذهب ليس خاصا بأبي حنيفة، وإنما هو أكبر المجتهدين في المذهب، وفي المذهب مجتهدون كثر، ورجح المجتهدون في المذهب من بين أقوالهم ما هو الأنسب للواقع، ومن ذلك أنهم رجحوا لزفر سبعة عشرة مسألة، لكن حرر ابن عابدين في رد المحتار ٣: ٦٠٧ أنها عشرين مسألة. ومعناه: إن لم يوجد حكم في المسألة عن المجتهدين المستقلين أبي حنيفة وتلامذته، فيؤخذ بالحكم بطبقة المجتهد المنتسب، قال المقدسي في الحاوي القدسي: إذا لم يوجد في الحادثة عن واحد منهم جواب ظاهر، وتكلم فيه المشايخ المتأخرون قولا واحدا يؤخذ به، فإن اختلفوا، يؤخذ بقول الأكثرين مما اعتمد عليه الكبار المعروفون كأبي حفص، وأبي جعفر، وأبي الليث، والطحاوي وغيرهم، فيعتمد عليه.
If there is no correct alternative, we take what they have clarified. They preferred some of his companions' statements and verified them. Indeed, we see that they have from that which they preferred for Zufr seventeen issues. Our scholars of insight delayed, reverting to that which the majority holds. If the transmitted narration from like al-Tahawi and Abu Hafs and Abu Ja'far and al-Layth al-Shahr (famous) is not found and the later scholars differed, then the meaning: we abide by what the mujtahids in the madhhab corrected of statements, for the statements of the mujtahids in the madhhab are the proof for the mufti, just as the statement of the absolute mujtahid is proof for the mujtahid in the madhhab, and the mufti's statement is proof for the layman. Thus they are ranks through which the ruling passes until it reaches the layman. It begins with the Quran and Sunnah, then the absolute mujtahid, then the mujtahid in the madhhab, then the mufti, then the layman. The layman only receives it after it has passed through several stages of examination and scrutiny. If the mufti does not find a correction from the mujtahid in the madhhab, he knows that the preferred view is apparent from the expressions of the books mentioning the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), so he must act upon it. And its meaning: we see that the mujtahids in the madhhab have preferred many of the statements of Abu Hanifa's companions; because the madhhab is not exclusive to Abu Hanifa, but he is the greatest of the mujtahids in the madhhab, and there are many mujtahids in the madhhab. The mujtahids in the madhhab have preferred among their statements what is most suitable for reality. Among that is that they preferred for Zufr seventeen issues, but Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar 3:607 verified that they are twenty issues. And its meaning: If there is no ruling in the issue from the independent mujtahids Abu Hanifa and his students, then the ruling is taken from the level of the affiliated mujtahid (mujtahid muntasib). Al-Maqdisi in al-Hawi al-Qudsi said: If there is no apparent answer in the incident from any one of them, and the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) have spoken about it with a single opinion, it is taken. If they differ, then the opinion of the majority is taken, from that which the well-known great scholars like Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, Abu al-Layth, al-Tahawi, and others have relied upon, so it is relied upon.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule that defines the mufti's obligation to follow the preferred (rajih) opinions of the mujtahids in the Hanafi madhhab. The text begins by stating that the mufti must take what the mujtahids have clarified and verified. It then explains the hierarchy: the absolute mujtahid (e.g., Abu Hanifa) produces the ruling; the mujtahid in the madhhab (e.g., Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) verifies and prefers certain opinions; the mufti applies the preferred opinion; and the layman follows the mufti. If no clear preference is found from the early mujtahids, the mufti must rely on the majority opinion of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) such as al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs, Abu Ja'far, and Abu al-Layth. This ensures consistency within the madhhab while allowing for adaptation to reality. The passage also mentions that the mujtahids sometimes preferred Zufr's opinion in seventeen (or twenty according to Ibn Abidin) issues, demonstrating that the madhhab is not static. The rule is critical for muftis to know their place in the hierarchy and to avoid issuing fatwas based on weaker or unpopular opinions.

Key Terms
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A scholar who can deduce rulings within the Hanafi school based on the principles of the school, such as Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
المجتهد المطلق (al-mujtahid al-mutlaq): An independent mujtahid who derives rulings directly from primary sources, such as Abu Hanifa himself.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known transmitted narrations from the founding Imams, as collected in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later scholars who are not independent mujtahids but interpret the school's rulings; e.g., al-Tahawi, Abu Hafs, al-Karkhi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a mufti do if there is no clear ruling from the independent mujtahids (Abu Hanifa and his students) on a matter?
A) He may issue a fatwa based on his own reasoning.
B) He should refer to the opinion of the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) and take the majority view.
C) He must remain silent and not issue a fatwa.
D) He can follow the opinion of any scholar from any madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti is obligated to follow the preferred opinions of the school's mujtahids and, failing that, the majority opinion of the later scholars.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
7 min
Guidance for the Mufti: When No Text Exists and the Tarjih Rule for Ibadat
Provides instructions for mufti when no transmitted ruling is found and presents first rule of tarjih in ibadat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the procedure a Hanafi mufti must follow when no transmitted ruling exists, and apply the rule of tarjih in ibadat by identifying when the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is preponderant and when an exception applies, using the case of tayammum with nabidh.

Core Idea
When text is absent, derive by qiyas on precedents; in ibadat, prefer Imam unless a sound narration from the Sahibayn overrides.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti provides two foundational rules for the Hanafi mufti. First, it explains the careful procedure when no existing ruling from the school's authorities is at hand: the qualified mufti must exert ijtihad through qiyas on similar transmitted cases, avoiding reliance on general fiqh principles. Second, it sets forth the first controlling rule (dabt) for tarjih in ibadat: the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa is normally preferred, except where a sound narration from another authority (like the Sahibayn) clearly supports a differing outcome, as illustrated by the ruling on tayammum with date-water (nabidh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct guidelines
The passage contains two separate but related instructions: (a) what a mufti should do when no transmitted ruling exists, and (b) the general rule for preferring opinions in worship chapters.
Recognize that the first part is a procedural directive, the second is a substantive dabt.
2
Analyze the mufti's duty when no text exists
Understand that the mufti, if a mujtahid, must base his ijtihad solely on qiyas from similar transmitted cases from the imams of the school, not on general qawaid. He must also fear Allah and not be lenient.
This emphasizes the gravity of fatwa and the limits of free reasoning within the madhhab.
3
State the default tarjih rule for ibadat
The default is that the saying of Abu Hanifa is given preponderance in all chapters of ibadat—purification, prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj.
This is a strong presumption, but it is not absolute.
4
Examine the exception: the tayammum with nabidh case
The passage gives the example of tayammum with nabidh where the Sahibayn's view (tayammum allowed) was preferred over Abu Hanifa's (wudu with nabidh valid). Identify the evidence (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud) and why the later scholars (mutakhkhirun) ruled otherwise.
This shows that sound transmissions from the Sahibayn can override the default preference if explicitly stated by the school.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical scenario
Given a new ibadat issue, determine which saying is preponderant by first seeking a clear textual statement from the school, then applying the dabt: default to Abu Hanifa unless a sound narration from others is explicitly preferred in the later works.
Practice with the example: if a mufti finds both Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's opinions on a matter of prayer, which is mufta bihi? (Answer: Abu Hanifa, unless a specific text says otherwise).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم توجد لهؤلاء مقالة واحتيج للإفتاء فلينظر المفتى بجد واجتهاد ولیخش بطش ربِّه يوم المعاد فليس يجسر على الأحكام سوی شقى خاسر المرام) محوره غدت لدى أهل النهى مقرَّره وهاهنا ضوابط فى كل أبواب العبادات رجّح قول الإمام مطلقاً ما لم تصح رواية بها الغير أخذ مثل تيمم لمن تمراً نبذ عنه
(١) ومعناه: إن لم يكن في المسألة حكم عن أبي حنيفة وأصحابه ولا من جاء بعدهم مِنَ العلماء، ونحتاج للفتوى فيها، فإن كان المفتي مجتهداً فعليه بعد بحثه الشديد أن يجتهد في المسألة ويستخرج بالقياس على نظائرها من المسائل المنقولة عن أئمة المذهب، ولا يعتمد على القواعد الفقهية، وليتق الله تعالى فيما يفتي؛ لأنَّه يُبيّن حكم الله تعالى، فإن تساهل أو لم يكن أهلاً لذلك فهو جرى على الله، وهو شقي خاسر عند الله تعالى. قال المقدسي في الحاوي القدسي ق ١٨٠ / أ: «وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصاً، ينظر المفتي فيها نظر تأمل وتَدَبُّر واجتهاد؛ ليجد فيها ما يَقْرُبُ إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يَتَكَلَّمُ فيها جزافاً لمنصبه وحرمته، وليخش الله تعالى ويُراقبه، فإنَّه أَمرٌ عظيمٌ لا يَتَجاسَرُ عليه إلا كل جاهل شقي».
(٢) ومعناه : سنذكر ضوابط منقحة وثابتة عند أهل العقول، وهم العلماء، وهي: ١. الراجح قول أبي حنيفة في جميع أبواب العبادات مِنَ الطهارة والصلاة والزكاة والصيام والحج، إلا في مسائل قليلة صرحوا بترجيح قول غيره: كترجيحهم لقول الصاحبين في جواز التيمم مع وجودِ نبيذ التمر، مع أن قول أبي حنيفة التوضؤ بالنبيذ؛ لحديث ابن مسعود له في ليلة الجنّ: «سألني النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ما في إداوتك ؟ فقلت: نبيذ . فقال : تمرة طيبة وماء طهور، قال: فتوضأ منه في سنن الترمذي ١: ١٤٧، وسنن البيهقي الكبير :١: ٩، وسنن الدارقطني ١: ٧٧، وسنن أبي داود ١: ٢١ وسنن ابن ماجه ١: ١٣٥، ومصنف ابن أبي شيبة ١: ٣٢، وشرح معاني الآثار ١: ٩٥، ومسند الشاشي ٢: ٢٤٨، ومسند أحمد ١: ٤٠٢، ومسند أبي يعلى: ٢٠٣، والمعجم الكبير ١: ١٤٧، وغيرها، وحسنه في إعلاء السنن ١: ٢٨٤. إلا أنه رجع
And when no statement of these [scholars] is found and there is need for fatwa, the mufti should look with utmost effort and ijtihad, and fear the might of his Lord on the Day of Return, for none dares to give rulings except a wretched loser. Its axis has become established among people of understanding. And here are rules: in every chapter of acts of worship, the saying of the Imam [Abu Hanifa] is given preponderance absolutely, unless a sound narration from others is transmitted, such as the example of tayammum for one who has date-water from him. (1) Its meaning: If there is no ruling in the issue from Abu Hanifa and his companions nor from the scholars who came after them, and we need to give a fatwa in it, then if the mufti is a mujtahid, after thorough research he must exert ijtihad in the issue and derive by analogy on its parallels from transmitted issues of the imams of the school, and not rely on fiqh principles. And he should fear Allah in his fatwa, for he is clarifying the ruling of Allah. If he is lenient or is not qualified, then he has committed a crime against Allah, and he is a wretched loser. Al-Maqdisi said in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'If no answer from them is found at all textually, the mufti should look into it with deep reflection and ijtihad to find what is close to discharging responsibility, and should not speak carelessly due to his position and sanctity, and should fear Allah and be mindful, for it is a great matter that only every ignorant wretch dares to undertake.' (2) Its meaning: We will mention refined rules that are established among people of intellect (the scholars). They are: 1. The preponderant is the saying of Abu Hanifa in all chapters of worship—purification, prayer, zakat, fasting, pilgrimage—except in a few issues where they explicitly gave preponderance to the saying of others: such as their preponderance for the saying of the two companions [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] regarding the permissibility of tayammum in the presence of date-water, whereas Abu Hanifa's saying is wudu with date-water, based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud on the Night of Jinn: 'The Prophet asked me: What is in your water-skin? I said: Nabidh. He said: A good date and pure water. He said: Perform wudu from it.' [Citations] and he considered it hasan in I'la' al-Sunan. But he retracted.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) governing two distinct but related situations in the Hanafi fatwa tradition. The author, Ibn Abidin, first addresses the scenario where no transmitted ruling exists from any Hanafi authority (Abu Hanifa, his companions, or later scholars). In such a case, if the mufti is qualified as a mujtahid, he must exert ijtihad by deriving the ruling through qiyas on similar cases reported from the imams of the school. Importantly, he is warned not to rely on general fiqh principles but to base his derivation on transmitted precedents. The passage emphasizes the gravity of this task, quoting al-Maqdisi that one must not speak carelessly. The second part introduces the first of the 'dawabit' (controlling rules): in all chapters of 'ibadat (purification, prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj), the preponderant saying is that of Imam Abu Hanifa absolutely, except where a sound narration from the sahibayn or others clearly supports an alternative. The example given is tayammum with date-water (nabidh al-tamar). Abu Hanifa allowed wudu with nabidh based on a hadith, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed tayammum when water is absent but nabidh is present. The later scholars preferred the sahibayn's view, making this an exception to the general rule of preferring Abu Hanifa in ibadat. The author lists extensive hadith references for the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, though the passage cuts off with 'but he retracted', indicating a follow-up on the hadith's status. The key point for the mufti is to recognize that the default preponderance of Abu Hanifa in ibadat is not absolute; exceptions are explicitly identified.

Key Terms
الإمام (al-Imam): Imam Abu Hanifa, the founder of the madhhab.
الصاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
ضوابط (dawabit): Controlling rules or principles that regulate the mufti's practice, especially in tarjih (preferring one opinion over another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a Hanafi mufti do if no ruling is found from Abu Hanifa, his companions, or later scholars for a new issue?
A) Refer directly to the Quran and Sunnah without considering madhhab precedents.
B) Derive the ruling by qiyas on similar cases transmitted from the imams of the madhhab, after thorough research.
C) Issue a fatwa based on his own personal opinion (ra'y) since no ruling exists.
D) Consult the qadi for a decision and then follow that.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti must derive rulings by qiyas on madhhab precedents when no text exists, and in ibadat, the default is to follow Abu Hanifa's opinion except where a sound narration from the Sahibayn or others dictates otherwise.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
6 min
Ruling When No Text from Imams Exists
Defines the mufti's duty when no transmitted ruling exists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for deriving a fatwa when no transmitted ruling exists, using qiyas within the madhhab and avoiding reliance on general qawaid.

Core Idea
When no transmitted ruling exists, the mufti must derive by qiyas, not rely on general maxims.

What does a mufti do when a completely new question arises—one that Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani, and later Hanafi scholars never addressed? This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti gives the answer: he must exert himself in ijtihad, deriving a ruling by analogy from similar cases, and he must not fall back on general fiqh principles. This lesson unpacks that crucial procedural rule and its grave responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the gap
The first step is to confirm that no text (nass) from the Hanafi imams exists on the issue. This includes the three founding imams and later authoritative scholars. If even one transmitted opinion exists, the rule does not apply.
2
Check the mufti's qualification
The rule applies only if the mufti is a mujtahid—someone capable of independent reasoning. If he is not, he must not issue a fatwa; he should refer the questioner to someone qualified.
Ibn Abidin stresses the danger of speaking without qualification.
3
Derive by qiyas, not qawaid
The mufti must search for similar transmitted cases (nazair) and perform analogical reasoning (qiyas) to extract a ruling. He must not rely on general fiqh maxims (qawaid fiqhiyya) as the sole basis, because they are abstract principles, not binding precedents.
4
Issue with taqwa
The mufti must fear Allah and recognize that he is stating Allah's ruling. Carelessness or arrogance leads to loss in this world and the next.
Al-Maqdisi's quote reinforces the gravity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحيث لم توجد لهؤلاء مقالة واحتيج للإفتاء فلينظر المفتى بجد واجتهاد ولیخش بطش ربِّه يوم المعاد فليس يجسر على الأحكام سوی شقى خاسر المرام) محوره غدت لدى أهل النهى مقرَّره ومعناه: إن لم يكن في المسألة حكم عن أبي حنيفة وأصحابه ولا من جاء بعدهم مِنَ العلماء، ونحتاج للفتوى فيها، فإن كان المفتي مجتهداً فعليه بعد بحثه الشديد أن يجتهد في المسألة ويستخرج بالقياس على نظائرها من المسائل المنقولة عن أئمة المذهب، ولا يعتمد على القواعد الفقهية، وليتق الله تعالى فيما يفتي؛ لأنَّه يُبيّن حكم الله تعالى، فإن تساهل أو لم يكن أهلاً لذلك فهو جرى على الله، وهو شقي خاسر عند الله تعالى.
قال المقدسي في الحاوي القدسي ق ١٨٠ / أ: «وإن لم يوجد منهم جواب البتة نصاً، ينظر المفتي فيها نظر تأمل وتَدَبُّر واجتهاد؛ ليجد فيها ما يَقْرُبُ إلى الخروج عن العهدة، ولا يَتكَلَّمُ فيها جزافاً لمنصبه وحرمته، وليخش الله تعالى ويُراقبه، فإنَّه أَمرٌ عظيمٌ لا يَتَجاسُرُ عليه إلا كل جاهل شقي».
And when no statement of these [imams] exists and there is need for fatwa, then let the mufti look with seriousness and exertion, and fear the assault of his Lord on the Day of Return, for none dares to pass rulings except a wretched loser of aspiration. Its meaning: If there is no ruling in the matter from Abu Hanifa and his companions nor from those who came after them from the scholars, and we need a fatwa in it, then if the mufti is a mujtahid, he must, after thorough research, exert himself in the matter and derive [a ruling] by analogy to its parallels from the transmitted cases of the madhhab imams, and he should not rely on fiqh maxims. And let him fear Allah in what he gives as fatwa, because he is explaining the ruling of Allah. If he is negligent or not qualified for that, then he is being insolent against Allah, and he is wretched and lost in the sight of Allah. Al-Maqdisi said in al-Hawi al-Qudsi, folio 180a: 'If absolutely no answer is found from them as text, the mufti should look into the matter with reflection, deliberation, and exertion, to find something close to discharging responsibility, and he should not speak about it frivolously due to his position and honor. And let him fear Allah and watch Him, for it is a great matter that none dares to undertake except every ignorant wretched person.'
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm al-mufti rule: when the transmitted rulings of the Hanafi madhhab (from Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and later authorities) contain no explicit answer for a new issue, and a fatwa is needed, the mufti must engage in ijtihad. The author, Ibn Abidin, emphasizes that the mufti must be qualified (mujtahid) and must derive the ruling by way of qiyas (analogy) from similar cases within the madhhab. He warns against relying solely on general fiqh principles (qawaid) without textual foundation, because those principles are not a substitute for transmitted precedents. The tone is grave: the mufti faces Allah's reckoning, and only a wretched fool would dare to speak without knowledge. The quote from al-Maqdisi reinforces this: the mufti must reflect deeply and not speak lightly. The rule applies only when absolutely no textual answer exists. This lesson teaches the methodology of fatwa when faced with a novel case.

Key Terms
اجتهاد (ijtihad): The mufti's independent reasoning to extract a ruling from the madhhab's principles by analogy.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from a transmitted precedent to a new case, based on the illah (effective cause).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a mufti do when no ruling is found from Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, or later scholars for a new issue?
A) Issue a fatwa based on the nearest qawida.
B) Remain silent and refer the questioner elsewhere.
C) Derive the ruling by qiyas from similar transmitted cases.
D) Choose the opinion of any later scholar arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
When the Hanafi texts are silent, the mufti must derive a ruling by analogy from similar transmitted cases, not from general fiqh maxims, and must do so with deep fear of Allah.
