للترجيح الالتزامي؛ ويكون بمعرفة مناهج علماء مذهبه في تأليف كتبهم؛ إذ أن لكل مؤلف طريقة في الترجيح بين الأقوال، يتعرفها المفتي بكثرة مطالعة الكتب وشروحها وحواشيها، بالإضافة للنظر فيما ألف في رسم المفتي، ومن هذه الصور: ١. تقديم القول الراجح؛ قد التزم بعض المؤلفين بأنهم يقدمون القول الراجح عندهم في الذكر على الأقوال المرجوحة، ومثال ذلك: أ. قاضي خان (ت٥٩٢هـ)، إذ قال في فتاواه: وبينما كثرت فيه الأقاويل من المتأخرين اقتصرت على قول أو قولين وقدمت ما هو الأظهر، وافتتحت بما هو الأشهر؛ إجابة للطالبين، وتيسيراً على الراغبين. ب. إبراهيم الحلبي (ت٩٦١هـ) في ملتقى الأبحر ص٢ إذ قال: وصريت بذكر الخلاف بين أئمتنا، وقدمت من أقاويلهم ما هو الأرجح، وأخرت غيره. ٢. تأخير دليل القول الراجح؛ فإن عامة الكتب التي التزمت ذكر الدلائل: كالهداية والمبسوط وغيرهما، فعادتهم المعروفة أنهم يذكرون دليل القول الراجح في الأخير، ويجيبون عن دلائل أقوال أخر، فالدليل المذكور في الأخير يدل على رجحان مدلوله عند المؤلف. ٣. ذكر دليل القول الراجح؛ وهذا إذا ذكر دليل قول واحد فقط وأهمل دليل الآخر، فالراجح ما ذكر دليله. والظاهر أن الكتب التي تهتم بذكر الاستدلال لا ترجح من جهة الدليل إلا قول الإمام، وإن كانت الفتوى على خلاف قوله، فيرجحون القول الآخر من جهة أصول التطبيق من ضرورة وعرف وغيرها. قال الشلبي: الأصل أن العمل على قول أبي حنيفة؛ ولذا ترجح المشايخ دليله في الأغلب على دليل من خالفه من أصحابه، ويجيبون عما استدل به مخالفه، وهذا أمارة العمل بقوله، وإن لم يصرحوا بالفتوى عليه؛ إذ الترجيح كصريح التصحيح. ومعنى الأشبه: الأشبه بالنصوص رواية، والراجح دراية دليلاً، فيكون عليه الفتوى. ومعنى الأوجه: أي وجهاً من حيث إن دلالة الدليل عليه متجهة ظاهرة أكثر من غيره. ومعناه: إن وجد المفتي في مسألة أقوالاً، وصحح أحدهما بأي لفظ من ألفاظ الترجيح فإنه يعمل به؛ لأنه ترجيح صريح. ومن ألفاظ الترجيح: به نأخذ، أو عليه فتوى مشايخنا، أو هو المعتمد، أو هو الأشبه، أو هو الأوجه، أو به يعتمد أو عليه الاعتماد أو عليه العمل اليوم، أو هو الظاهر، أو هو الأظهر، أو هو المختار، أو به جرى العرف اليوم، أو هو المتعارف، أو به أخذ علماؤنا، وغيرها، فجميع هذه الألفاظ متساوية. واختلفوا في الصحيح والأصح أيهما أقوى، فقيل: الأصح أكد من الصحيح؛ لأنه باسم التفضيل، وقيل: الصحيح أكد من الأصح؛ لأن خلاف الصحيح خطأ، فلا يجوز العمل به، وخلاف الأصح صحيح، فيمكن العمل به. والأولى: أن الأصح أرجح من الصحيح إن صدر القولان من شخصين، فيكون ذكره للأصح ترجيحاً على الصحيح، وإن كان من شخصين فأكثر، فالأولى عدم الترجيح باللفظ، وإنما النظر للكتاب الذي ذكرت فيه والعالم القائل له، فيرجح بهما لا باللفظ؛ لأنهم يريدون الترجيح ولا يهتمون للفظ الذي استخدم في الترجيح.
And preceding the statements in al-Khaniyya and Multaqa al-Abhur is a virtue, and in others, rely on what they delayed its proof because it is the edited, the preferred in knowledge, as is the custom in al-Hidayah and similar. Likewise, if they have provided proof for one and neglected proof for the other. He began by mentioning forms of implicit tarjih: it is by knowing the methods of the scholars of his madhhab in writing their books, for each author has a method of tarjih between statements, which the mufti learns by frequent study of books, commentaries, and marginalia, in addition to looking at what has been written on the drawing of the mufti. Among these forms: 1. Presenting the preferred statement; some authors committed to presenting the preferred statement in mention over the inferior statements, e.g., Qadi Khan (d. 592H) said in his Fatawa: 'When the sayings of later scholars became numerous, I limited to one or two statements and presented what is most apparent and began with what is most famous.' b. Ibrahim al-Halabi (d. 961H) in Multaqa al-Abhur said: 'I stated the difference among our imams and presented their most preferred statements and delayed others.' 2. Delaying the proof of the preferred statement; the general run of books that committed to mentioning proofs, like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, their known custom is that they mention the proof of the preferred statement last and answer the proofs of other statements, so the proof mentioned last indicates the preference of its conclusion according to the author. 3. Mentioning the proof of the preferred statement; this is when proof is mentioned for only one statement and neglected for the other, so the preferred is the one whose proof is mentioned. It appears that the books concerned with giving evidence do not prefer by evidence except the statement of the Imam, even if the fatwa is contrary to his statement, then they prefer the other statement by the principles of application from necessity, custom, etc. al-Shilbi said: 'The principle is that practice is on the statement of Abu Hanifa; therefore, the shaykhs generally prefer his evidence over the evidence of those who disagree with him from his companions, and they answer the evidence of the dissenter, and this is a sign of practice on his statement, even if they do not explicitly state the fatwa on it; for tarjih is like explicit correction.' The meaning of 'ashbah' (more similar): more similar to texts in transmission, and the preferred in knowledge and proof, so the fatwa is upon it. The meaning of 'awjah' (more appropriate): having an aspect where the evidence is apparent more than others. And its meaning: if the mufti finds statements in a matter and one of them is corrected by any wording of tarjih, then he acts on it because it is explicit tarjih. Among the wordings of tarjih: 'we take by it', 'the fatwa of our shaykhs is upon it', 'it is the relied-upon', 'it is the more similar', 'it is the more appropriate', 'by it reliance is placed', 'reliance is on it', 'practice today is on it', 'it is the apparent', 'it is the more apparent', 'it is the chosen', 'by it the custom today operates', 'it is the customary', 'our scholars took by it', etc., all these wordings are equal. And they differed on 'sahih' (correct) and 'asahh' (more correct) which is stronger. It was said: 'asahh' is stronger than 'sahih' because it is a comparative. And it was said: 'sahih' is stronger than 'asahh' because the opposite of 'sahih' is error, so it is not permissible to act on it, while the opposite of 'asahh' is correct, so it is possible to act on it. The preferable view: 'asahh' is more preponderant than 'sahih' if the two statements come from two persons, then mentioning 'asahh' is a tarjih over 'sahih'; but if they are from two or more persons, then it is better not to prefer by the wording, rather consider the book in which it is mentioned and the scholar who said it, so prefer by those, not by the wording, because they intend tarjih and do not pay attention to the wording used in tarjih.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage presents essential rules for a Hanafi mufti on how to identify the preferred opinion (rajih) from the books of the madhhab. The author, Ibn Abidin, explains three methods of implicit tarjih (al-tarjih al-iltizami) that muftis must recognize: First, some authors commit to presenting the preferred opinion first in their books, as Qadi Khan did in al-Khaniyya and Ibrahim al-Halabi in Multaqa al-Abhur. Second, in books like al-Hidayah and al-Mabsut, the preferred opinion's proof is given last, after refuting other proofs, so the final proof indicates the author's preference. Third, if only one opinion is supported with proof, that opinion is the preferred one. The passage then clarifies that when a mufti finds a corrected opinion using terms like 'ashbah' or 'awjah', he must act on it. The term 'ashbah' means more similar to the transmitted texts (riwaya), while 'awjah' means more appropriate in terms of evidence (diraya). The passage also resolves the dispute on 'sahih' and 'asahh': the stronger view is that 'asahh' outweighs 'sahih' when from two persons, but when multiple persons are involved, the mufti should rely on the book and the scholar, not merely the wording.

Key Terms
الترجيح الالتزامي (al-tarjih al-iltizami): Implicit tarjih inferred from the author's method of presenting opinions and proofs
الأشبه (al-ashbah): More similar to transmitted texts (riwaya); indicates preference
الأوجه (al-awjah): More appropriate due to stronger evidence (diraya); indicates preference
الصحيح (al-sahih): Correct opinion, but its opposite is error (khatta)
الأصح (al-asahh): More correct; comparative form indicating higher degree of correctness

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which method of implicit tarjih is used in al-Hidayah?
A) Presenting the preferred opinion first
B) Delaying the proof of the preferred opinion
C) Mentioning proof only for the preferred opinion
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Implicit tarjih and the proper use of tarjih terminology are essential tools for a Hanafi mufti to identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) opinion.

Strength of the Expression 'به يفتى' in Tarjih
Commentary on why 'به يفتى' is the strongest tarjih expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the expression 'به يفتى' is the strongest tarjih expression, and explain why tarjih should be based on the authority of the scholar and book, not merely on the wording.

Core Idea
The strongest tarjih expression is 'به يفتى' because it implies both preference and practice, but true tarjih depends on the scholar and source.

In this passage, Ibn Abidin clarifies the relative strength of the expression 'به يفتى' among tarjih expressions. He warns against relying solely on the wording and emphasizes that the actual weight comes from the authority of the scholar and the reliability of the book. This lesson will help you understand how to properly apply tarjih in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the literal meaning
Identify the Arabic phrase 'به يفتى' and its translation 'with it fatwa is given'. Understand that it is a tarjih expression.
2
Understand its strength
Note that the passage says it is stronger than other expressions because it combines preference (tarjih) and required practice (amal).
3
Heed the caution
Ibn Abidin warns not to rely on wording alone; preference is actually determined by the speaker's ijtihad level and the book's reliability. Qadi Khan's corrections are given precedence due to his high fiqh.
4
Apply in fatwa context
When encountering conflicting tarjih expressions, first verify the authority of the scholar and the authenticity of the book before considering the phrase used. This ensures correct fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كذا به يفتى عليه
(۱) معناه أن لفظ به يفتى وعليه الفتوى، أقوى مِنْ غيرها من ألفاظ الترجيح؛ لأنها تضمن الترجيح والعمل. والأولى عدم الترجيح بالألفاظ، وإنَّما يرجح بالقائل والكتاب المذكور فيه لفظ الترجيح، فكلما ارتفعت درجة القائل في الاجتهاد كان قوله أقوى من غيره، وكذلك كلّما كان الكتاب أكثر اعتماداً كان ما فيه من الترجيح مُقدَّم على ترجيح غيره، قال ابن قطلوبغا في التصحيح ص١٣٤ : «ما يصححه قاضي خان مقدم على تصحيح غيره؛ لأنَّه فقيه النفس». وهذا هو الظاهر من استخدام ألفاظ الترجيح في الكتب، حيث تجد أن المفتي لو اهتم باللفظ ولم ينتبه للقائل والكتاب لن يستطيع التوصل للراجح؛ لوجود التساهل في إطلاق ألفاظ الترجيح المتنوعة على ما يرجحون، وأنّهم لا يقصدون التفضيل بين الألفاظ، وإِنَّما يُعبّر كلٌّ منهم برجحان ما اختار من قول بأي بلفظ مِن ألفاظ الترجيح، والله أعلم.
Thus, with it fatwa is given upon it. (1) Its meaning: The expression 'with it fatwa is given' and 'upon it is the fatwa' is stronger than other expressions of preference (tarjih), because it includes both preference and practice. And it is better not to give preference based on the expressions themselves; rather preference is given based on the speaker and the book in which the expression of preference is mentioned. So, the higher the degree of the speaker in ijtihad, the stronger his statement than others, and likewise, the more reliable a book is, the more its preference is given precedence over the preference of others. Ibn Qutlubugha said in al-Tashih p.134: 'What Qadi Khan corrects is given precedence over the correction of others because he is a faqih by nature.' And this is apparent from the usage of preference expressions in books, for you find that if the mufti pays attention to the expression and not to the speaker and the book, he will not be able to reach the preferable opinion due to the leniency in applying various preference expressions to what they prefer, and they do not intend a ranking of expressions, but rather each one expresses the preference of the opinion he chooses with any expression of preference. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rasm rule regarding the strength of the phrase 'به يفتى' (with it fatwa is given). The author explains that this phrase is stronger than other expressions of tarjih because it implies both that the ruling is preferable and that it is to be acted upon. However, he cautions that preference should not be determined merely by the wording of the expression; rather, the mufti must consider the authority of the scholar who made the correction and the reliability of the book in which it is recorded. He quotes Ibn Qutlubugha to illustrate that Qadi Khan's corrections are given precedence due to his high level of fiqh understanding. The key takeaway is that the actual tarjih is based on the source and the mujtahid, not on the linguistic form of the expression.

Key Terms
به يفتى (bihi yufatā): An expression meaning 'with it fatwa is given', indicating that a ruling is both preferred and to be acted upon.
عليه الفتوى (alayhi al-fatwā): An expression meaning 'upon it is the fatwa', another tarjih expression but slightly weaker than 'به يفتى' according to this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is used by Qadi Khan.
B) Because it is found in the matn.
C) Because it combines both preference (tarjih) and required practice (amal).
D) Because it is the most frequent expression in the books.

Key Takeaway
The strength of 'به يفتى' lies not in its wording but in the authority backing it.

Criteria for Preferring Conflicting Corrected Opinions
Detailed list of factors for a mufti to choose between conflicting corrections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi hierarchy of preferences to resolve conflicting corrected opinions when issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
When two corrected opinions conflict, the mufti must apply a structured hierarchy—from the same scholar's later view to explicit over implicit, matn over others, and istihsan over qiyas.

In Hanafi iftaa, a mufti often encounters conflicting corrected opinions (tashih). This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti provides a comprehensive set of criteria to resolve such conflicts. These criteria are not arbitrary but follow a logical hierarchy that respects the school's authority structure and practical considerations. By mastering these criteria, you will be able to issue well-grounded fatwas that align with the school's methodology.

Guided Path
1
Determine if the corrections come from the same or different scholars
First, identify whether both corrections are attributed to one mujtahid (e.g., Al-Quduri) or two different scholars. The same scholar's later view takes precedence if the date is known.
If from one scholar and date unknown, move to the other criteria.
2
Apply the hierarchical list when corrections come from two different scholars
The passage lists preferences in order: explicit over implicit, stronger wording, mentioned in matn, from Zahir al-Riwaya, saying of Imam Abu Hanifa over Sahibayn, majority of mashayikh, istihsan over qiyas, suitability for time, stronger evidence, benefit for poor (in zakat), benefit for waqf, preventing hudud, and finally preferring haram over halal.
This sequence is not exhaustive but provides a clear guide.
3
Check for any overriding considerations
Some criteria may conflict (e.g., one opinion is in matn but another is from Imam Abu Hanifa). The hierarchy helps but the mufti must also consider the specific context and strengths of evidence.
Ibn Abidin notes that all this applies when both opinions are equally authentic.
4
When no explicit preference appears, use conscience with caution
If no criterion gives a clear advantage, the mufti may choose based on internal inclination, avoiding caprice and seeking Allah's guidance.
This is a last resort, not a default.
5
Ensure the chosen opinion is properly documented in the fatwa
The mufti should record which preference led to the choice, especially in advanced cases. This maintains transparency and aligns with the school's practice.
Later sources often cite specific tarjihs from this list.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) معناه: إن وجد في مسألة أكثر من قول مصحح، ولم يظهر للمفتي شيء من المرجحات، فهو بالخيار، ويأخذ أحدهما بشهادة قلبه مجتنباً عن التشهي وطالباً للصواب مِنَ الله تعالى، وإن وجد أحد المرجحات الآتية لأحد القولين فيعمل بما رجح على النحو الآتي: ١ . إذا كان الترجيحان من رجل واحد، عمل بالمتأخر منهما إن عرف التاريخ، وإن لم يعرف التاريخ رجح المفتي أحدهما بمرجحات سيأتي ذكرها. ٢ . إذا كان الترجيحان من رجلين مُختلفين، رَبَّحَ المفتي أحدهما بمرجحات، وهي: أ. إذا كان أحد التصحيحين صريحاً والآخر التزاماً، عمل بالصريح. ب. إذا كان أحد التصحيحين بلفظ أقوى بالنسبة إلى تصحيح آخر، رجّح ما لفظه أقوى. ج. إذا كان أحدهما مذكوراً في المتون والآخر مذكوراً في غيرها، فالراجح ما في المتون. د . إذا كان أحدهما ظاهر الرواية والآخر غيره، فالراجح ما هو ظاهر الرواية. هـ. إذا كان أحدهما قول الإمام والآخر قول صاحبيه، فالراجح قول الإمام. و. إذا كان أحدهما مختار أكثر المشايخ والآخر مختار قليل منهم، فالراجح ما اختاره الأكثر . س. إذا كان أحدهما قياساً والآخر استحساناً، فالراجح الاستحسان. ح. إذا كان أحدهما أوفق بالزمان كان راجحاً على غيره. ط. إذا كان أحد القولين أقوى في الدليل عند مفت أهل للنظر في الدليل، فهو أولى من غيره ي. إذا كان أحد القولين أنفع للفقراء فهو أولى من غيره في باب الزكاة. ق. إذا كان أحد القولين أنفع للوقف فهو أولى من غيره. ل . إذا كان أحد القولين أدرأ للحدّ فهو أولى من غيره. ن. إذا كان التعارض بين الحل والحرمة فالراجح هو المحرم، ينظر: أصول الإفتاء ص٣٦- ٣٧، وغيرهما. (۱) في ج: «به أصلاً». (۲) معناه: هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأنَّ كلَّ واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة، فإذا كان في أحدهما زيادة قوّة مِنْ جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى مِنَ العمل بالآخر. وكذا إذا لم يُصرَّح بتصحيح واحد مِنَ القولين، فيُقَدَّم ما فيه مرجّح من هذه المرجّحات: ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرواية... الخ. ينظر : شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص .٤٠
(2) Its meaning: If in a case there is more than one corrected statement, and no preference (tarjih) appears to the mufti, then he has the choice, and he takes one of them with the testimony of his heart, avoiding caprice and seeking correctness from Allah Almighty. And if one of the following preferences appears for one of the two statements, then he acts according to what is preferred in the following manner: 1. If the two preferences come from one person, he acts by the later one if the date is known, and if the date is not known, the mufti prefers one of them with preferences to be mentioned later. 2. If the two preferences come from two different persons, the mufti prefers one of them based on preferences, namely: a. If one correction is explicit and the other implicit, he acts by the explicit. b. If one correction uses a stronger expression relative to another correction, he gives precedence to what is stronger in expression. c. If one is mentioned in the matn and the other in other books, the preferred is what is in the matn. d. If one is from zahir al-riwaya and the other not, the preferred is what is from zahir al-riwaya. e. If one is the saying of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the other is the saying of his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the preferred is the saying of the Imam. f. If one is chosen by the majority of mashayikh and the other by a few, the preferred is what the majority chose. g. If one is based on qiyas and the other on istihsan, the preferred is istihsan. h. If one is more suitable for the time, it is preferred over others. i. If one saying is stronger in evidence for a mufti who is capable of examining evidence, it is more preferable. j. If one saying is more beneficial for the poor, it is more preferable in the chapter of zakat. k. If one saying is more beneficial for the waqf, it is more preferable. l. If one saying is more preventive against hudud punishment, it is more preferable. n. If there is conflict between halal and haram, the preferred is the haram. See: Usul al-Ifta p.36-37, etc. (1) In copy (ج): 'به أصلاً'. (2) Its meaning: All this is when corrections conflict, because each of the two statements is equal in authenticity; so if one of them has an additional strength from another direction, acting upon it is more appropriate. Likewise, if there is no explicit correction for either statement, the one with a preference from these preferences is given precedence, such as being in the matn, or the saying of the Imam, or zahir al-riwaya, etc. See: Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p.40.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive list of criteria a Hanafi mufti uses when faced with conflicting corrected opinions. The author first addresses the situation where the mufti has no clear preference: he may choose based on his conscience, seeking Allah's guidance. When there are identified preferences, he prioritizes based on a hierarchy: the same scholar's later view, then explicit over implicit, stronger wording, mention in matn, being from Zahir al-Riwaya, Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion over the Sahibayn, majority of scholars, istihsan over qiyas, suitability for the time, strength of evidence, benefit to the poor (in zakat), benefit to the waqf, prevention of hudud, and finally, preferring haram over halal when there is a contradiction. The commentary emphasizes that these criteria apply only when both opinions are equally authentic, or when no explicit correction is available. This detailed methodology ensures the mufti's choice is grounded in the school's principles.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tashih): A correction or authentication of a legal ruling by a mujtahid, indicating that this opinion is the preferred one.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): Transmissions that are well-known and established in the school, from the core works of Muhammad al-Shaybani.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that allows departing from qiyas for a stronger reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) The one later in time

Key Takeaway
When corrected opinions conflict, the mufti must navigate a clear hierarchy—from same scholar's later view to explicit/implicit, matn, Zahir al-Riwaya, Imam's word, majority, istihsan, benefit, and finally haram over halal.

The Twelve Tarjih Rules of the Mufti
Enumerating twelve tarjih rules for conflicting rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and apply the twelve tarjih criteria for preferring one Hanafi ruling over another when tashih is absent.

Core Idea
When two Hanafi rulings are equally authentic, twelve tarjih rules guide the mufti to the stronger position.

This passage from Ibn 'Abidin's 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti presents the mufti's toolkit for resolving conflicting rulings within the Hanafi school. When no explicit tashih (preferred ruling) is available, these twelve criteria—ranging from source authority to practical benefit—determine which opinion should be adopted. Mastering this list is essential for any serious student of iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Identify source authority rules
Group rules dealing with the textual source: (ج) mutun over others, (د) Zahir al-Riwayah over others, (ه) Imam over Sahibayn. These establish a clear hierarchy of textual authority.
Note that 'mutun' refers to core abridged texts like al-Quduri, while Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the six books of Imam Muhammad.
2
Recognize consensus-based rules
Rule (و) prefers the choice of the majority of mashayikh over the minority. This reflects the importance of scholarly consensus (ijma' in practice).
This rule can override the previous ones if the majority chose a different opinion.
3
Distinguish methodological rules
Rule (ز) prefers istihsan over qiyas. This is a foundational Hanafi principle that juristic preference can override analogical reasoning.
Istihsan is not arbitrary but based on a stronger evidence or custom.
4
Apply context-sensitive rules
Rules (ح) time consonance, (ط) stronger evidence, (ي) benefit for poor (zakat), (ق) benefit for waqf, (ل) averting hadd. These consider contemporary circumstances and practical consequences.
Rule (ط) applies only to a mufti qualified for ijtihad; others may not use it.
5
Determine the default rule
Rule (ن) prefers prohibition over permissibility when the conflict is between halal and haram. This is a conservative default for doubtful matters.
This applies only when the two positions are equally sahih and other rules do not tip the balance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا تعارض التصحيح أو لم يكن [أصلاً به] تصريح فالذي له مرجح مما علمته فهذا الأوضح (۲) ج. إذا كان أحدهما مذكوراً في المتون والآخر مذكوراً في غيرها، فالراجح ما في المتون. د . إذا كان أحدهما ظاهر الرواية والآخر غيره، فالراجح ما هو ظاهر الرواية. هـ. إذا كان أحدهما قول الإمام والآخر قول صاحبيه، فالراجح قول الإمام. و. إذا كان أحدهما مختار أكثر المشايخ والآخر مختار قليل منهم، فالراجح ما اختاره الأكثر . س. إذا كان أحدهما قياساً والآخر استحساناً، فالراجح الاستحسان. ح. إذا كان أحدهما أوفق بالزمان كان راجحاً على غيره. ط. إذا كان أحد القولين أقوى في الدليل عند مفت أهل للنظر في الدليل، فهو أولى من غيره ي. إذا كان أحد القولين أنفع للفقراء فهو أولى من غيره في باب الزكاة. ق. إذا كان أحد القولين أنفع للوقف فهو أولى من غيره. ل . إذا كان أحد القولين أدرأ للحدّ فهو أولى من غيره. ن. إذا كان التعارض بين الحل والحرمة فالراجح هو المحرم. معناه: هذا كله إذا تعارض التصحيح؛ لأنَّ كلَّ واحد من القولين مساو للآخر في الصحة، فإذا كان في أحدهما زيادة قوَّة مِنْ جهة أخرى، يكون العمل به أولى مِنَ العمل بالآخر. وكذا إذا لم يُصرَّح بتصحيح واحد مِنَ القولين، فيُقَدَّم ما فيه مرجّح من هذه المرجّحات: ككونه في المتون، أو قول الإمام أو ظاهر الرواية... الخ. ينظر : شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص .٤٠
When correction (tashih) conflicts, or there is no explicit [originally] statement, then whichever has a preponderance from what you have learned is the clearer. (2) C. If one of them is mentioned in the matn and the other elsewhere, the preponderant is what is in the matn. D. If one is from Zahir al-Riwayah and the other not, the preponderant is the one from Zahir al-Riwayah. E. If one is the saying of the Imam and the other the saying of his two companions, the preponderant is the Imam's saying. F. If one is the choice of the majority of the mashayikh and the other the choice of a few of them, the preponderant is what the majority chose. S. If one is qiyas and the other is istihsan, the preponderant is istihsan. H. If one is more consonant with the time, it is preponderant over the other. T. If one of the two sayings is stronger in evidence according to a mufti qualified to consider evidence, it is more worthy than the other. Y. If one of the two sayings is more beneficial for the poor, it is more worthy than the other in the chapter of zakat. Q. If one of the two sayings is more beneficial for the waqf, it is more worthy than the other. L. If one of the two sayings is more repellant of the hadd penalty, it is more worthy than the other. N. If the conflict is between permissibility and prohibition, the preponderant is the prohibited. Meaning: All this is when the correction conflicts; because each of the two sayings is equal to the other in authenticity. So if there is additional strength in one from another aspect, acting upon it is more worthy than acting upon the other. Likewise, if there is no explicit correction of one of the two sayings, then what has a preponderance from these preponderating factors is given precedence: such as being in the matn, or the saying of the Imam, or Zahir al-Riwayah, etc. See: Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 40.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a list of twelve tarjih rules for a mufti when faced with conflicting authoritative positions. The author states that the rules apply when the two positions are equally sahih (authentic) from the madhhab, or when no explicit tashih (preferred ruling) is given. The rules are: (1) Preference for rulings found in the mutun (core texts) over those in commentaries. (2) Preference for Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad) over other transmissions (Nawadir). (3) Preference for the saying of Imam Abu Hanifa over the sayings of his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn). (4) Preference for the opinion chosen by the majority of scholars. (5) Preference for istihsan over qiyas. (6) Preference for the ruling more consonant with the time. (7) Preference for the stronger evidence according to a mufti capable of ijtihad. (8) Preference for the more beneficial for the poor in zakat. (9) Preference for the more beneficial for the waqf. (10) Preference for the ruling that averts the hadd penalty. (11) Preference for prohibition over permissibility. These rules ensure consistency and methodological rigor in fatwa. They are not derived from specific proofs but are established rasm (procedure) of the mufti.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat).
المتون (al-Mutun): The core abridged texts of the madhhab, such as al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah, etc.
التصحيح (al-Tashih): The act of preferring one ruling over another within the madhhab, often done by later scholars or indicated in the texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is istihsan preferred over qiyas?
A) Always, without exception.
B) Only when the qiyas is weak.
C) When the conflict is between qiyas and istihsan.
D) Only in mu'amalat.

Key Takeaway
The twelve tarjih rules are the mufti's systematic method for preferring one sahih Hanafi ruling over another when no explicit tashih exists.

Mafhum al-Mukhalafa in Fiqh Texts vs Shari'ah Texts
Explaining the rule of mafhum al-mukhalafa in fiqh texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between mafhum al-mukhalafa in fiqh texts and Shari'ah texts to determine when an implication is authoritative in fatwa derivation.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is authoritative in fiqh books but not in Qur'an and Sunnah—fiqh texts are precise codes, scriptures are eloquent.

This lesson addresses a critical distinction in Hanafi usul al-iftaa: the authority of mafhum al-mukhalafa (inference from the opposite) differs between Shari'ah texts (Qur'an and Sunnah) and fiqh texts (compilations of rulings). While the Shafi'i school generally accepts it in all texts, the Hanafi school restricts it to juristic works. The reason lies in the nature of the language: scripture contains rhetorical flourishes, whereas fiqh books are deliberately precise. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplying implications when deriving fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the Hanafi rule: mafhum al-mukhalafa is accepted in fiqh texts but not in Shari'ah texts.
This rule is specific to ifta and differs from the Shafi'i position.
2
Understand the rationale
Explain why: Shari'ah texts include rhetorical devices (emphasis, rebuke, denunciation) that are not intended as legal restrictions. Fiqh texts are purely legal codifications.
Quranic examples illustrate this: 'small price' (Q.2:41) and 'doubled and multiplied' (Q.3:130).
3
Examine the examples
Analyze the given Quranic verses to see how adjectives are used for denunciation, not as conditions.
These show that mafhum would lead to incorrect rulings if applied.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
Recognize that the Shafi'i school generally accepts mafhum al-mukhalafa in all texts, leading to different derivations.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: rulings differ when qualifications appear in scripture.
5
Apply to a fiqh text
Given a qualification in a fiqh book (e.g., 'if water is less than two qullahs'), infer the opposite for the unmentioned case.
This is the operative rule for a mufti consulting madhhab literature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعمل بمفهوم روايات أتى ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا والعرفُ في الشرع له اعتبار لذا عليه الحكم قد يدار (۱) معناه : يعمل بمفهوم المخالفة في عبارات الكتب الفقهيّة إن لم تكن مخالفة لما ثبت صريحاً؛ قال عمر ابن نجيم في النهر الفائق :۱: ۳۷ مفاهيم الكتب حجّة بخلاف أكثر مفاهيم النصوص»: أي من القرآن والسنة، فمفهوم المخالفة معتبر عند الشافعية، وغير معتبر عند مِنَ الحنفية، بمعنى أنَّ النصّ لا يدل على نقيض الحكم لغير المنطوق فيبقى المفهوم مسكوتاً عنه، فإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه حكم المنطوق عمل به، وإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه مناقض لحكم المنطوق عمل به. وجه الفرق بين النصوص الشرعية والعبارات الفقهية : أنَّ نصوص القرآن والسنة تحتوي على عبارات بليغة حكيمة، فربّما تذكر فيها ألفاظ للتأكيد والتوبيخ والتشنيع والوعظ والتذكير ولا تكون قيداً لما سبق: كقوله : {وَلا تَشْتَرُوا بِآيَاتِي ثَمَناً قَلِيلاً} [البقرة: ٤١]، فإنَّما أضيف لفظ القليل للتشنيع على العمل، ولا يدلّ على أن الاشتراء بالثمن الكثير جائز، وكذلك قوله لا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبا أَضْعَافاً مُضَاعَفَةٌ} [آل عمران: ۱۳۰] ، فإنَّه يدل على أن الربا جائز إذا لم يكن ضعفاً للأصل. أما كتب الفقه، فإنَّ مقصودها تدوين الأحكام على طريقة قانونية وليس فيها شيء مِنَ التأكيد والتشنيع وغير ذلك، فلا بُدَّ مِنْ اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة فيها. ينظر: أصول الإفتاء ص ٤٢ - ٤٣، وغيره.
And work with the implication (mafhum) of narrations that come, as long as they do not contradict something explicitly established. And custom in the Sacred Law has consideration, therefore ruling may be based on it. (1) Meaning: One acts upon the mafhum al-mukhalafa in the expressions of fiqh books as long as they do not contradict what is explicitly established. Umar Ibn Nujaym said in al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (1:37): 'The mafahim of books are authoritative, contrary to most mafahim of the texts' i.e. of the Qur'an and Sunnah. So mafhum al-mukhalafa is considered by the Shafi'is, and not considered by the Hanafis, in the sense that the text does not indicate the opposite ruling for the unstated, so the mafhum remains unspoken. If evidence indicates that its ruling is the same as the stated, one acts upon it; if evidence indicates that its ruling is contrary to the stated, one acts upon it. The difference between the Shari'ah texts and fiqh expressions: The texts of the Qur'an and Sunnah contain eloquent, wise expressions; sometimes words are mentioned for emphasis, rebuke, denunciation, admonition and reminder, and are not restrictions on what preceded: like His saying {And do not purchase with My verses a small price} [al-Baqarah 41], for the word 'small' was added to denounce the action, and it does not indicate that purchasing with a large price is permitted. And likewise His saying {Do not consume usury doubled and multiplied} [Aal 'Imran 130], for it indicates that usury is permitted if it is not compounded. As for fiqh books, their purpose is to codify rulings in a legal manner, and there is nothing in them of emphasis, denunciation, etc., so it is necessary to consider mafhum al-mukhalafa in them. See: Usul al-Ifta' pp. 42-43, etc.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage explains the rule for a mufti regarding mafhum al-mukhalafa (inference from the opposite). It distinguishes between Shari'ah texts (Qur'an and Sunnah) and fiqh texts (jurist-authored books). In Shari'ah texts, mafhum al-mukhalafa is not generally considered by Hanafis because the language may include hyperbole, emphasis, or rhetorical flourishes that are not meant as strict legal conditions. For example, the prohibition of selling Divine verses for a 'small price' does not imply that a large price is permissible; the adjective is for denunciation. Similarly, the prohibition of 'doubled and multiplied' usury does not permit simple usury. In contrast, fiqh books are written in a precise, legalistic style; their wording is deliberate and every qualifier is meaningful. Therefore, mafhum al-mukhalafa is authoritative in fiqh texts. The author quotes Umar ibn Nujaym to support this distinction. The mufti should apply this rule when deriving rulings from the madhhab's literature.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (Mafhum al-Mukhalafa): Inferring the opposite ruling for an unmentioned case based on a qualification in the text (e.g., if the text says 'if it is small', it implies the opposite for large).
مفاهيم الكتب (Mafahim al-Kutub): The implications (mafahim) found in the expressions of fiqh books, which are considered authoritative in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the verse is abrogated.
B) Because the phrase 'doubled and multiplied' is for emphasis and denunciation, not a legal restriction.
C) Because mafhum al-mukhalafa is never considered in the Qur'an.
D) Because it contradicts a consensus.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi iftaa, mafhum al-mukhalafa is considered in fiqh books but not in the Qur'an and Sunnah, due to the different nature of their language.

Custom and Change of Fatwa Over Time
Explaining how custom and changing times affect fatwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the principle that fatwa may change with changing custom, and apply it to distinguish between a change within the Hanafi madhhab and an abandonment of the madhhab.

Core Idea
A fatwa may change with time and custom, still staying within the Hanafi madhhab, because the founder would have ruled accordingly in the new context.

This lesson addresses a crucial principle for muftis: fatwa can evolve as customs and circumstances change, without breaking from the school. Ibn 'Abidin explains that the founding imams based rulings on their own time; when that time changes, the ruling may change accordingly. This is not a departure from the madhhab but a living application of its principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
Focus on the central claim: many rulings by the founder have changed with the times due to corruption or necessity.
The rule is that change of fatwa is permissible when custom or necessity changes.
2
Understand the rationale
Note the reasoning: if the founder were alive in the later time, he would have issued the new ruling. The change is hypothetically attributed to the founder himself.
3
Recognize the conditions
Only scholars with 'sound consideration' (al-nazar al-sahih) may exercise this. The change must be based on genuine change of custom or necessity, not personal preference.
The mufti must be qualified and the circumstances must truly have changed.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a modern case: a mufti asked about a contract that was previously prohibited due to custom but is now common. Use the principle to determine if a new fatwa is valid within the madhhab.
The test: would the founder rule differently today?
5
Distinguish from abandonment
The change remains within the madhhab because it derives from the same principles. Abandonment would be when a new rule contradicts a definitive nass without basis.
The maxim 'لا عبرة للعادة مع النص' limits custom's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲) معناه: كما قال ابن عابدين في شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٤٥: «إِنَّ كثيراً مِنَ الأَحكام التي نصَّ عليها المجتهد صاحب المذهب بناءً على ما كان في عرفه وزمانه قد تغيرت بتغير الأزمان بسبب فساد أهل الزمان أو عموم الضرورة... وكل ذلك غير خارج عن المذهب؛ لأنَّ صاحب المذهب لو كان في هذا الزمان لقال بها، ولو حدث هذا التغير في زمانه لم ينص على خلافها. وهذا الذي جَرّأ المجتهدين في المذهب وأهل النظر الصحيح مِنَ المتأخرين على مخالفة المنصوص عليه مِنْ صاحب المذهب في كتب ظاهر الرواية، بناءً على ما كان في زمنه...
(2) Its meaning: As Ibn 'Abidin said in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p. 45: 'Indeed many of the rulings which the mujtahid, the founder of the madhhab, laid down based on what was in his custom and time have changed with the change of times, due to corruption of the people of the time or general necessity... And all that is not outside the madhhab; because if the founder of the madhhab were in this time, he would have said them, and if this change had occurred in his time, he would not have stated the contrary. And this is what emboldened the mujtahids in the madhhab and those of sound consideration among the later scholars to oppose what is stated from the founder of the madhhab in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, based on what was in his time...'
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage addresses a crucial principle in ifta': fatwa can change with the change of time and custom, even if it means departing from explicit texts in the core books of the madhhab. Ibn 'Abidin explains that the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, etc.) based their rulings on the customs and circumstances of their own time. When those circumstances change—due to moral decay (fasad ahl al-zaman) or widespread necessity (umum al-darurah)—the ruling may change accordingly. This change is not a departure from the madhhab, because if the founder were alive in the later time, he himself would have issued the new ruling. Therefore, later scholars (mutakhkhirin) who are qualified can exercise ijtihad within the madhhab and issue fatwa based on new realities, even contradicting a Zahir al-Riwayah ruling. This principle is a 'rukhsa' (concession) that allows the madhhab to remain practical. The mufti must be careful: only those with 'sound consideration' (al-nazar al-sahih) may do this.

Key Terms
المجتهد صاحب المذهب (al-Mujtahid Sahib al-Madhhab): Refers to Imam Abu Hanifa (and by extension Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who founded the Hanafi school.
المنصوص عليه (al-Mansus 'alayh): The ruling explicitly stated in the authoritative texts (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because later scholars have greater knowledge than Abu Hanifa.
B) Because Abu Hanifa would have agreed with the new ruling if he lived in the later time.
C) Because Zahir al-Riwayah is not considered binding.
D) Because custom always overrides text.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa may change with changing custom and time, and this change is not a departure from the madhhab if it would have been the founder's view had he been present.

The Concept of Opposite (Mafhum al-Mukhalafah) in Fatwa
Explaining the limited application of mafhum al-mukhalafah in Hanafi fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mafhum al-mukhalafah and apply it correctly to fiqh books versus primary texts.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafah applies to fiqh books but not to Quran and Sunnah in the Hanafi school.

This lesson unpacks a key rasm al-mufti rule: the concept of opposite (mafhum al-mukhalafah). Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Abidin clarify that while Shafi'is apply this concept to all texts, Hanafis restrict it to fiqh codifications. Understanding this distinction is crucial for a mufti when deriving rulings from classical legal manuals versus the primary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
The text states: 'Act by the concept of transmitted reports unless it opposes a clear established text.' This is the general rule for mafhum al-mukhalafah.
The rule is qualified by the next step.
2
Understand the exception
Ibn Nujaym explains: 'Concepts of books are proof, unlike most concepts of the texts'—meaning Quran and Sunnah. So mafhum al-mukhalafah is valid in fiqh books but not in primary texts.
The exception is based on the nature of the texts.
3
Examine the Hanafi reasoning
Quran and Sunnah use rhetorical language (emphasis, reprimand, etc.). For example, 'Do not purchase with My verses a small price' uses 'small' for denunciation, not to permit a large price. Such phrases are not legal restrictions.
Fiqh books are purely legal codifications without such rhetoric.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i view
Shafi'is consider mafhum al-mukhalafah authoritative in all texts, including Quran and Sunnah. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Hanafis respond that primary texts require additional evidence to infer opposites.
5
Apply the rule
When reading a fiqh book, a mufti may infer the opposite ruling from a conditional or restrictive phrase. But from a Quranic verse, he cannot do so without separate evidence.
This affects fatwa in practice, e.g., interpreting conditions in contracts.

(۱) معناه : يعمل بمفهوم المخالفة في عبارات الكتب الفقهيّة إن لم تكن مخالفة لما ثبت صريحاً؛ قال عمر ابن نجيم في النهر الفائق :۱: ۳۷ مفاهيم الكتب حجّة بخلاف أكثر مفاهيم النصوص»: أي من القرآن والسنة، فمفهوم المخالفة معتبر عند الشافعية، وغير معتبر عند مِنَ الحنفية، بمعنى أنَّ النصّ لا يدل على نقيض الحكم لغير المنطوق فيبقى المفهوم مسكوتاً عنه، فإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه حكم المنطوق عمل به، وإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه مناقض لحكم المنطوق عمل به.
وجه الفرق بين النصوص الشرعية والعبارات الفقهية : أنَّ نصوص القرآن والسنة تحتوي على عبارات بليغة حكيمة، فربّما تذكر فيها ألفاظ للتأكيد والتوبيخ والتشنيع والوعظ والتذكير ولا تكون قيداً لما سبق: كقوله : {وَلا تَشْتَرُوا بِآيَاتِي ثَمَناً قَلِيلاً} [البقرة: ٤١]، فإنَّما أضيف لفظ القليل للتشنيع على العمل، ولا يدلّ على أن الاشتراء بالثمن الكثير جائز، وكذلك قوله لا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبا أَضْعَافاً مُضَاعَفَةٌ} [آل عمران: ۱۳۰] ، فإنَّه يدل على أن الربا جائز إذا لم يكن ضعفاً للأصل. أما كتب الفقه، فإنَّ مقصودها تدوين الأحكام على طريقة قانونية وليس فيها شيء مِنَ التأكيد والتشنيع وغير ذلك، فلا بُدَّ مِنْ اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة فيها. ينظر: أصول الإفتاء ص ٤٢ - ٤٣، وغيره.
(۲) معناه: كما قال ابن عابدين في شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٤٥: «إِنَّ كثيراً مِنَ الأَحكام التي نصَّ عليها المجتهد صاحب المذهب بناءً على ما كان في عرفه وزمانه قد تغيرت بتغير الأزمان بسبب فساد أهل الزمان أو عموم الضرورة... وكل ذلك غير خارج عن المذهب؛ لأنَّ صاحب المذهب لو كان في هذا الزمان لقال بها، ولو حدث هذا التغير في زمانه لم ينص على خلافها. وهذا الذي جَرّأ المجتهدين في المذهب وأهل النظر الصحيح مِنَ المتأخرين على مخالفة المنصوص عليه مِنْ صاحب المذهب في كتب ظاهر الرواية، بناءً على ما كان في زمنه... فللمفتي اتباع عرفه الحادث في الألفاظ العرفية، وكذا في الأحكام التي بناها المجتهد على ما كان في عُرف زَمانِه، وتغيّر عُرفه إلى عُرُفٍ آخر اقتداءً بهم، لكن بعد أن يكون المفتي ممن له رأي ونظر صحيح ومعرفة بقواعد الشرع، حتى يميز بين العُرف الذي يجوز بناء الأحكام عليه وبين غيره... و جمود المفتي أو القاضي على ظاهرِ المنقول مع تركِ العرفِ والقرائن الواضحة والجهل بأحوال النّاس، يلزم منه تضييع حقوق كثيرة وظلم خلق كثيرين». وهذا الكلام من ابن عابدين في غاية الدقة والروعة؛ لأنَّ هذا الجمود على النُّصوص الفقهية بدون فهم عللها ومراعاة الواقع أقصت الفقه عن حياة المسلمين في كثيرين من مناحي الحياه، والله المستعان.
وينتبه أن ابن عابدين أطلق مصطلح العرف ولم يقصد به العرف فحسب، بل قصد قواعد رسم المفتي من الضرورة والتيسير والمصلحة وتغير الزمان ويظهر هذا جلياً لمن يطالع رسالته: «نشر العرف في بناء بعض الأحكام على العرف». وإِنَّ أكثر قاعدة مِنَ الرسم تُراعى في الفتوى والتطبيق هي : النَّظر إلى عرف المجتمع، فيختلف الحكم من مكان إلى مكان وزمان إلى زمانٍ على ما حسب ما يقتضيه عرف الناس، قال الجويني في نهاية المطلب :۱۱ : ۳۸۲ : ومَن لم يمزج العرف في المعاملات بفقهها، لم يكن على حظ كامل فيها»، وقال أيضاً ٤١٦:١١: «والتعويل في التفاصيل على العرف، وأعرف النّاس به أعرفهم بفقه المعاملات»؛ لأنَّ العرف من الجانب التطبيقي للفقه، وليس من الجانب الاستنباطي للحكم ، ومَرَدُّه إلى أمرين:
١. فهم مراد المتكلم من كلامه، فنحن نستخدم ألفاظاً ونريد بها معاني معينة تعارفنا في إطلاقها عليها، وإن كان اللفظ عاماً يشمل غيرها، مثل: اللحم يشمل لحم سائر الحيوانات من الطيور والبقر والغنم وغيرها، ولكن تعارفنا عند إطلاقها على إرادة لحم البقر والغنم لا الطيور مثلاً، فإذا قال شخص: والله لا آكل لحماً، ثمّ أكل دجاجاً لا يحنث؛ لأنَّه لا يعتبر لحماً عرفاً، فاستفدنا من العرف معرفة مقصود المتكلّم من كلامه، وقس عليه. ٢ . معرفة صلاحية المحل لعلّة الحكم، فالحكم في نفسه ثابت من الشارع الحكيم، والعرف لا يغيّر الحكم، لكن الحكم مبني على علّة، وهذه العلة تحتاج إلى محل في تطبيقها، فالعرف
And act by the concept of transmitted reports unless it opposes a clear established text, and custom in the Law has consideration, so upon it the ruling may be based.
(1) Its meaning: One acts by the concept of opposite in the expressions of fiqh books if they are not contradictory to what is established explicitly. Ibn Nujaym said in al-Nahr al-Fa'iq: 'The concepts of books are proof, unlike most concepts of the texts' – i.e., from Quran and Sunnah. The concept of opposite is considered valid among Shafi'is, and not considered valid among Hanafis, meaning that the text does not indicate the opposite ruling for the unstated; the concept remains unspoken. If evidence indicates that its ruling is the same as the stated one, it is acted upon; if evidence indicates that its ruling contradicts the stated one, it is acted upon.
The difference between the original texts and fiqh expressions: The texts of Quran and Sunnah contain eloquent wise expressions; sometimes words are mentioned for emphasis, reprimand, denunciation, admonition, and reminder, and are not restrictions on what preceded: like His saying: {And do not purchase with My verses a small price} [2:41] – the word 'small' was added to denounce the act, and does not indicate that purchasing with a great price is permissible. Similarly, His saying: {Do not consume usury multiplied in multiples} [3:130] – it indicates that usury is permissible if it is not a multiple of the principal. As for fiqh books, their purpose is to codify rulings in a legal manner; they contain nothing of emphasis, denunciation, etc., so the concept of opposite must be considered there. See: Usul al-Ifta', pp. 42-43, etc.
(2) Its meaning: As Ibn Abidin said in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, p. 45: 'Indeed, many of the rulings that the mujtahid founder of the school stated based on what was in his custom and time have changed with changing times due to the corruption of the people of the time or general necessity... And all that is not outside the school; because if the founder were in this time, he would say them; and if this change had occurred in his time, he would not have stated contrary to them. This is what emboldened the mujtahids in the school and those of sound reflection among the later scholars to oppose what is stated by the founder in the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, based on what was in his time... So the mufti must follow his emerging custom in customary expressions, and likewise in the rulings that the mujtahid built on what was in the custom of his time, and his custom changed to another custom, following their example. But only after the mufti is one who has opinion, sound reflection, and knowledge of the principles of Shari'a, so that he can distinguish between custom upon which rulings may be built and others... And the rigidity of the mufti or judge on the apparent transmitted text while abandoning custom, clear circumstantial evidence, and ignorance of people's conditions, necessitates the loss of many rights and oppression of many creatures.' This statement from Ibn Abidin is extremely precise and wonderful; because this rigidity on fiqh texts without understanding their causes and considering reality has alienated fiqh from the lives of Muslims in many aspects of life, and Allah is the helper.
Note that Ibn Abidin used the term 'urf and did not intend by it only custom, but intended the rules of rasm al-mufti such as necessity, facilitation, maslaha, and change of time. This becomes clear to whoever examines his treatise: 'Nashr al-'Urf fi Bina' Ba'd al-Ahkam 'ala al-'Urf'. And indeed, the most applied rule of rasm in fatwa and practice is: consideration of the custom of society; so the ruling differs from place to place and time to time according to what people's custom demands. Al-Juwayni said in Nihayat al-Matlab: 'He who does not mix custom in transactions with their fiqh has no complete share in it.' And he also said: 'Reliance in details is on custom, and the most knowledgeable of people about it is the most knowledgeable of fiqh of transactions.' Because custom is from the applied aspect of fiqh, not from the aspect of deriving rulings. Its referent is two matters:
1. Understanding the intent of the speaker from his speech. We use words and intend specific meanings that we are accustomed to applying them to, even if the word is general covering others. For example: 'meat' includes the meat of all animals – birds, cows, sheep, etc. But we are accustomed to intending by its absolute use the meat of cows and sheep, not birds, for instance. So if a person says: 'By Allah, I will not eat meat' and then eats chicken, he does not break his oath; because it is not considered meat customarily. Thus, we benefit from custom in knowing the intent of the speaker. And measure other cases accordingly.
2. Knowing the suitability of the locus for the cause of the ruling. The ruling itself is established by the Wise Lawgiver; custom does not change the ruling. But the ruling is built on a cause, and this cause needs a locus in its application. So custom...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two key rules (rasm rules) for the mufti. The first rule concerns the concept of opposite (mafhum al-mukhalafah). The author explains that in fiqh books, unlike the Quran and Sunnah, the concept of opposite is considered valid because fiqh books are written in a legalistic, non-rhetorical style. The Hanafi position is that concepts of books (i.e., fiqh texts) are authoritative, but not concepts of original texts. The Shafi'i view differs, considering the concept of opposite in the primary texts too. The second and more extensive rule is about the role of custom ('urf). Ibn Abidin quotes his own work to argue that many rulings of the mujtahid imams were based on their contemporary customs; when customs change, the rulings may change accordingly, without leaving the madhhab. The mufti must be qualified to judge which customs are valid bases for rulings. Rigid adherence to transmitted texts without regard to custom and circumstantial evidence leads to injustice. The passage emphasizes that 'urf here is not just custom but encompasses the broader principles of necessity, facilitation, and maslaha. It provides two applications: (1) understanding the speaker's intent by customary usage (e.g., meat does not include chicken in an oath), and (2) determining the suitability of the context for the application of a legal cause. Custom does not change the ruling itself but affects its application.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The concept of opposite: deriving the opposite ruling for the unstated case from the wording of a text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true about mafhum al-mukhalafah?
A) It applies to Quran, Sunnah, and fiqh books equally.
B) It applies to fiqh books but not to Quran and Sunnah.
C) It applies to Quran and Sunnah but not to fiqh books.
D) It does not apply to any text in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts the concept of opposite (mafhum al-mukhalafah) to fiqh books, not to primary texts.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
The Role of Custom ('Urf) in Fatwa: When Rulings Change with Time
Outlining the authority of custom in fatwa and its role in changing rulings over time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim on custom to determine when a mufti may issue a ruling different from the earlier text due to changed circumstances.

Core Idea
Custom can justify changing fatwas, but only when the custom is sound and the mufti is qualified.

Ibn Abidin's discussion on 'urf is a cornerstone of Hanafi fatwa methodology. He explains that many rulings of the founding imams were based on their contemporary customs. Later muftis may depart from those textual rulings when customs change, provided they have the necessary expertise. This lesson explores the conditions and limits of this principle.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the maxim
The text opens with: 'Custom in the Law has consideration, so upon it the ruling may be based.' This is the foundational maxim.
The maxim is broad but qualified by subsequent conditions.
2
Understand the basis
Ibn Abidin states that many rulings were built on the custom of the time. If custom changes, the ruling can change accordingly.
This does not mean the earlier ruling was wrong; it was correct for its time.
3
Identify the qualification
Only a mufti with sound knowledge and ability to distinguish valid custom from invalid can apply this. Rigidity leads to injustice.
The mufti must understand the 'illah (cause) of the original ruling.
4
Apply to a case
Example: someone swears not to eat 'meat', then eats chicken. Custom determines that chicken is not meat in that society, so the oath is not broken.
This shows custom helps understand the speaker's intent.
5
Note the limits
Custom cannot contradict a clear nass or definitive principle. If it does, the text prevails.
The exception is part of the qawida's dabt.

واعمل بمفهوم روايات أتى ما لم يخالف لصريح ثبتا والعرفُ في الشرع له اعتبار لذا عليه الحكم قد يدار
(۱) معناه : يعمل بمفهوم المخالفة في عبارات الكتب الفقهيّة إن لم تكن مخالفة لما ثبت صريحاً؛ قال عمر ابن نجيم في النهر الفائق :۱: ۳۷ مفاهيم الكتب حجّة بخلاف أكثر مفاهيم النصوص»: أي من القرآن والسنة، فمفهوم المخالفة معتبر عند الشافعية، وغير معتبر عند مِنَ الحنفية، بمعنى أنَّ النصّ لا يدل على نقيض الحكم لغير المنطوق فيبقى المفهوم مسكوتاً عنه، فإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه حكم المنطوق عمل به، وإن دل دليل على أنَّ حكمه مناقض لحكم المنطوق عمل به.
وجه الفرق بين النصوص الشرعية والعبارات الفقهية : أنَّ نصوص القرآن والسنة تحتوي على عبارات بليغة حكيمة، فربّما تذكر فيها ألفاظ للتأكيد والتوبيخ والتشنيع والوعظ والتذكير ولا تكون قيداً لما سبق: كقوله : {وَلا تَشْتَرُوا بِآيَاتِي ثَمَناً قَلِيلاً} [البقرة: ٤١]، فإنَّما أضيف لفظ القليل للتشنيع على العمل، ولا يدلّ على أن الاشتراء بالثمن الكثير جائز، وكذلك قوله لا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبا أَضْعَافاً مُضَاعَفَةٌ} [آل عمران: ۱۳۰] ، فإنَّه يدل على أن الربا جائز إذا لم يكن ضعفاً للأصل. أما كتب الفقه، فإنَّ مقصودها تدوين الأحكام على طريقة قانونية وليس فيها شيء مِنَ التأكيد والتشنيع وغير ذلك، فلا بُدَّ مِنْ اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة فيها. ينظر: أصول الإفتاء ص ٤٢ - ٤٣، وغيره.
(۲) معناه: كما قال ابن عابدين في شرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٤٥: «إِنَّ كثيراً مِنَ الأَحكام التي نصَّ عليها المجتهد صاحب المذهب بناءً على ما كان في عرفه وزمانه قد تغيرت بتغير الأزمان بسبب فساد أهل الزمان أو عموم الضرورة... وكل ذلك غير خارج عن المذهب؛ لأنَّ صاحب المذهب لو كان في هذا الزمان لقال بها، ولو حدث هذا التغير في زمانه لم ينص على خلافها. وهذا الذي جَرّأ المجتهدين في المذهب وأهل النظر الصحيح مِنَ المتأخرين على مخالفة المنصوص عليه مِنْ صاحب المذهب في كتب ظاهر الرواية، بناءً على ما كان في زمنه... فللمفتي اتباع عرفه الحادث في الألفاظ العرفية، وكذا في الأحكام التي بناها المجتهد على ما كان في عُرف زَمانِه، وتغيّر عُرفه إلى عُرُفٍ آخر اقتداءً بهم، لكن بعد أن يكون المفتي ممن له رأي ونظر صحيح ومعرفة بقواعد الشرع، حتى يميز بين العُرف الذي يجوز بناء الأحكام عليه وبين غيره... و جمود المفتي أو القاضي على ظاهرِ المنقول مع تركِ العرفِ والقرائن الواضحة والجهل بأحوال النّاس، يلزم منه تضييع حقوق كثيرة وظلم خلق كثيرين». وهذا الكلام من ابن عابدين في غاية الدقة والروعة؛ لأنَّ هذا الجمود على النُّصوص الفقهية بدون فهم عللها ومراعاة الواقع أقصت الفقه عن حياة المسلمين في كثيرين من مناحي الحياه، والله المستعان.
وينتبه أن ابن عابدين أطلق مصطلح العرف ولم يقصد به العرف فحسب، بل قصد قواعد رسم المفتي من الضرورة والتيسير والمصلحة وتغير الزمان ويظهر هذا جلياً لمن يطالع رسالته: «نشر العرف في بناء بعض الأحكام على العرف». وإِنَّ أكثر قاعدة مِنَ الرسم تُراعى في الفتوى والتطبيق هي : النَّظر إلى عرف المجتمع، فيختلف الحكم من مكان إلى مكان وزمان إلى زمانٍ على ما حسب ما يقتضيه عرف الناس، قال الجويني في نهاية المطلب :۱۱ : ۳۸۲ : ومَن لم يمزج العرف في المعاملات بفقهها، لم يكن على حظ كامل فيها»، وقال أيضاً ٤١٦:١١: «والتعويل في التفاصيل على العرف، وأعرف النّاس به أعرفهم بفقه المعاملات»؛ لأنَّ العرف من الجانب التطبيقي للفقه، وليس من الجانب الاستنباطي للحكم ، ومَرَدُّه إلى أمرين:
١. فهم مراد المتكلم من كلامه، فنحن نستخدم ألفاظاً ونريد بها معاني معينة تعارفنا في إطلاقها عليها، وإن كان اللفظ عاماً يشمل غيرها، مثل: اللحم يشمل لحم سائر الحيوانات من الطيور والبقر والغنم وغيرها، ولكن تعارفنا عند إطلاقها على إرادة لحم البقر والغنم لا الطيور مثلاً، فإذا قال شخص: والله لا آكل لحماً، ثمّ أكل دجاجاً لا يحنث؛ لأنَّه لا يعتبر لحماً عرفاً، فاستفدنا من العرف معرفة مقصود المتكلّم من كلامه، وقس عليه. ٢ . معرفة صلاحية المحل لعلّة الحكم، فالحكم في نفسه ثابت من الشارع الحكيم، والعرف لا يغيّر الحكم، لكن الحكم مبني على علّة، وهذه العلة تحتاج إلى محل في تطبيقها، فالعرف
And act by the concept of transmitted reports unless it opposes a clear established text, and custom in the Law has consideration, so upon it the ruling may be based.
(1) Its meaning: One acts by the concept of opposite in the expressions of fiqh books if they are not contradictory to what is established explicitly. If evidence indicates that its ruling is the same as the stated one, it is acted upon; if evidence indicates that its ruling contradicts the stated one, it is acted upon.
The difference between the original texts and fiqh expressions: The texts of Quran and Sunnah contain eloquent wise expressions; sometimes words are mentioned for emphasis, reprimand, denunciation, admonition, and reminder, and are not restrictions on what preceded: like His saying: {And do not purchase with My verses a small price} [2:41] – the word 'small' was added to denounce the act, and does not indicate that purchasing with a great price is permissible. As for fiqh books, their purpose is to codify rulings in a legal manner; they contain nothing of emphasis, denunciation, etc., so the concept of opposite must be considered there. See: Usul al-Ifta', pp. 42-43, etc.
(2) Its meaning: As Ibn Abidin said in Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, p. 45: 'Indeed, many of the rulings that the mujtahid founder of the school stated based on what was in his custom and time have changed with changing times due to the corruption of the people of the time or general necessity... And he also said: 'Reliance in details is on custom, and the most knowledgeable of people about it is the most knowledgeable of fiqh of transactions.' 1. Understanding the intent of the speaker from his speech. We use words and intend specific meanings that we are accustomed to applying them to, even if the word is general covering others. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two key rules (rasm rules) for the mufti. The first rule concerns the concept of opposite (mafhum al-mukhalafah). The author explains that in fiqh books, unlike the Quran and Sunnah, the concept of opposite is considered valid because fiqh books are written in a legalistic, non-rhetorical style. The Hanafi position is that concepts of books (i.e., fiqh texts) are authoritative, but not concepts of original texts. The Shafi'i view differs, considering the concept of opposite in the primary texts too. The second and more extensive rule is about the role of custom ('urf). Ibn Abidin quotes his own work to argue that many rulings of the mujtahid imams were based on their contemporary customs; when customs change, the rulings may change accordingly, without leaving the madhhab. The mufti must be qualified to judge which customs are valid bases for rulings. Rigid adherence to transmitted texts without regard to custom and circumstantial evidence leads to injustice. The passage emphasizes that 'urf here is not just custom but encompasses the broader principles of necessity, facilitation, and maslaha. It provides two applications: (1) understanding the speaker's intent by customary usage (e.g., meat does not include chicken in an oath), and (2) determining the suitability of the context for the application of a legal cause. Custom does not change the ruling itself but affects its application.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Custom or established practice in a society that is considered in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin, which of the following is true about changing rulings based on custom?
A) Any custom can change any ruling, even if it contradicts the Quran.
B) Only the original founders can change rulings; later jurists cannot.
C) Rulings based on custom can change when custom changes, provided the new custom does not contradict a clear text.
D) Custom is not considered in Hanafi fatwa at all.

Key Takeaway
Custom is a legitimate basis for changing fatwas, but only when it does not contradict explicit texts and the mufti is qualified.

The Mufti and Custom in Fatwa
Explains the mufti's duty to follow custom and its two functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two functions of custom ('urf) in fatwa and apply the maxim 'Consideration of societal custom' to determine a ruling.

Core Idea
Custom does not change Sharia rulings; it only clarifies intent and application context.

A mufti cannot mechanically apply texts without understanding the living custom of his society. Ibn Abidin warns that rigidity leads to injustice and argues that custom, properly understood, is not a source that changes rulings but a tool to apply them correctly. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two functions of custom
From the text, isolate exactly what custom does and does not do. List the two functions: (1) understanding speaker's intent, (2) knowing the suitability of the locus for the legal cause.
Memorize these two – they are the entire basis of 'urf in Hanafi fatwa.
2
Distinguish custom from ruling change
The text repeatedly stresses that custom does NOT change the Sharia ruling itself. Note the example of testimony: the ruling (upright witnesses) is fixed, but what constitutes uprightness depends on custom.
This refutes the misconception that custom can abrogate.
3
Analyze the 'urf in the oath example
The text uses 'meat' as an example. Apply the first function: what does the speaker customarily mean? Connect this to the ruling on breaking an oath.
Custom determines if the action falls under the prohibition/undertaking.
4
Explain how custom relates to rasm al-mufti
Ibn Abidin says 'urf here includes necessity, facilitation, and change of time. Explain why these are part of the mufti's methodology.
Rasm al-mufti is a broader framework – custom is a key element.
5
Apply the maxim to a new scenario
Use the qawida 'النظر إلى عرف المجتمع' to a modern case, e.g., what constitutes 'food' in an oath for a diabetic patient on a specific diet.
The application must respect the two functions and not change the fixed ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فللمفتي اتباع عرفه الحادث في الألفاظ العرفية، وكذا في الأحكام التي بناها المجتهد على ما كان في عُرف زَمانِه، وتغيّر عُرفه إلى عُرُفٍ آخر اقتداءً بهم، لكن بعد أن يكون المفتي ممن له رأي ونظر صحيح ومعرفة بقواعد الشرع، حتى يميز بين العُرف الذي يجوز بناء الأحكام عليه وبين غيره... و جمود المفتي أو القاضي على ظاهرِ المنقول مع تركِ العرفِ والقرائن الواضحة والجهل بأحوال النّاس، يلزم منه تضييع حقوق كثيرة وظلم خلق كثيرين». وهذا الكلام من ابن عابدين في غاية الدقة والروعة؛ لأنَّ هذا الجمود على النُّصوص الفقهية بدون فهم عللها ومراعاة الواقع أقصت الفقه عن حياة المسلمين في كثيرين من مناحي الحياه، والله المستعان. وينتبه أن ابن عابدين أطلق مصطلح العرف ولم يقصد به العرف فحسب، بل قصد قواعد رسم المفتي من الضرورة والتيسير والمصلحة وتغير الزمان ويظهر هذا جلياً لمن يطالع رسالته: «نشر العرف في بناء بعض الأحكام على العرف». وإِنَّ أكثر قاعدة مِنَ الرسم تُراعى في الفتوى والتطبيق هي : النَّظر إلى عرف المجتمع، فيختلف الحكم من مكان إلى مكان وزمان إلى زمانٍ على ما حسب ما يقتضيه عرف الناس، قال الجويني في نهاية المطلب :۱۱ : ۳۸۲ : ومَن لم يمزج العرف في المعاملات بفقهها، لم يكن على حظ كامل فيها»، وقال أيضاً ٤١٦:١١: «والتعويل في التفاصيل على العرف، وأعرف النّاس به أعرفهم بفقه المعاملات»؛ لأنَّ العرف من الجانب التطبيقي للفقه، وليس من الجانب الاستنباطي للحكم ، ومَرَدُّه إلى أمرين:
١. فهم مراد المتكلم من كلامه، فنحن نستخدم ألفاظاً ونريد بها معاني معينة تعارفنا في إطلاقها عليها، وإن كان اللفظ عاماً يشمل غيرها، مثل: اللحم يشمل لحم سائر الحيوانات من الطيور والبقر والغنم وغيرها، ولكن تعارفنا عند إطلاقها على إرادة لحم البقر والغنم لا الطيور مثلاً، فإذا قال شخص: والله لا آكل لحماً، ثمّ أكل دجاجاً لا يحنث؛ لأنَّه لا يعتبر لحماً عرفاً، فاستفدنا من العرف معرفة مقصود المتكلّم من كلامه، وقس عليه. ٢ . معرفة صلاحية المحل لعلّة الحكم، فالحكم في نفسه ثابت من الشارع الحكيم، والعرف لا يغيّر الحكم، لكن الحكم مبني على علّة، وهذه العلة تحتاج إلى محل في تطبيقها، فالعرف يساعدنا على تطبيق ذلك، مثاله : أنَّ الحكم عدم قبول إلا شهادة العدل، كما شهد القرآن: ممن ترضون من الشهداء} [البقرة: ۲۸۲]، والعرف يُساعدنا في معرفة العدل، ففي زمن أبي حنيفة لم يحتج للتزكية في العدالة؛ لأنَّ النّاس عدول، وفي زمن الصاحبين تغيّرت أحوال الناس، فنحتاج لتحقق علّة الحكم من العدالة بالتزكية، فمن لم يكن عدلاً لا تقبل شهادته، هذا هو الحكم، ولكن كيف نتعرّف على العدالة، حيث أمكن ذلك بالعرف. وبالتالي لا يخرج العرف عن هذين المعنيين ،البتة، فلا يكون مغيّراً للحكم الشرعي أبداً، ولا تستنبط به الأحكام أيضاً، وإنَّما هو معرّف للحكم ببيان مقصود المتكلّم من كلامه، ومعرفة صلاحيّة المحل لعلّة الحكم. وتَبيُّن أنَّ المحل صالح للحكم أمر مهم جداً؛ إذ نحتاج قبل تطبيق كل حكم أن نتعرّف على علته أولاً ثمّ ننظر هل المحل مناسب لها أم لا؟ فإن لم يكن مناسباً لها فإنَّ الحكم لا يطبق هنا.
So it is for the mufti to follow his contemporary custom in verbal customs, and likewise in rulings that the mujtahid built upon what was in the custom of his time, and his custom changed to another custom, following them, but only after the mufti is one who has sound opinion and judgment and knowledge of the rules of Sharia, so that he can distinguish between custom on which rulings may be built and other than it... The rigidity of the mufti or judge upon the apparent transmitted texts while abandoning custom and clear indications and ignorance of people's conditions necessarily results in wasting many rights and oppressing many creatures. This statement from Ibn Abidin is extremely precise and wonderful; because this rigidity upon juristic texts without understanding their causes and considering reality has removed fiqh from the life of Muslims in many aspects of life, and Allah is the Helper. And it is noted that Ibn Abidin used the term custom ('urf) and did not intend by it only custom, rather he intended the rules of the mufti's drawing (rasm) from necessity, facilitation, public interest (maslaha), and change of time. This appears clearly to whoever reads his treatise: 'Nashr al-'Urf fi Bina' Ba'd al-Ahkam 'ala al-'Urf.' And the most comprehensive rule of the drawing that is observed in fatwa and application is: consideration of the custom of society, so the ruling differs from place to place and time to time according to what the people's custom requires. Al-Juwayni said in Nihayat al-Matlab (11:382): 'Whoever does not mix custom in transactions with their fiqh, he is not fully competent in it.' And he also said (11:416): 'Reliance in details is on custom, and the most knowledgeable of people about it is the most knowledgeable in the fiqh of transactions.' Because custom is from the applied side of fiqh, not from the deductive side of the ruling, and its reference is to two matters: 1. Understanding the speaker's intent from his speech: we use words and intend specific meanings we have come to know in their application, even if the word is general and includes others. For example, 'meat' includes the meat of all animals from birds, cows, sheep, etc., but our customary usage when uttering it is to intend the meat of cows and sheep, not birds. So if someone says, 'By Allah, I will not eat meat,' then he eats chicken, he does not break his oath because it is not considered meat customarily. Thus we benefit from custom to know the speaker's intent from his speech, and analogize to this. 2. Knowing the suitability of the locus for the cause of the ruling: the ruling itself is established from the Wise Lawgiver, and custom does not change the ruling, but the ruling is based on a cause, and this cause needs a locus for its application. So custom helps us to apply that. For example: the ruling is that only the testimony of the upright is accepted, as the Quran testifies: 'from those whom you approve as witnesses' [Al-Baqarah 282]. Custom helps us to know uprightness. In the time of Abu Hanifa, there was no need for verification of uprightness because people were upright. In the time of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), people's conditions changed, so we need to verify the cause of the ruling of uprightness through investigation. So whoever is not upright, his testimony is not accepted. This is the ruling, but how do we ascertain uprightness? That is made possible by custom. Thus custom does not deviate from these two meanings at all; it is not a changer of the Sharia ruling ever, nor are rulings deduced through it, rather it is a definer of the ruling by clarifying the speaker's intent from his speech and knowing the suitability of the locus for the cause of the ruling. And it becomes clear that the locus being suitable for the ruling is a very important matter; for before applying every ruling we need to know its cause first, then see whether the locus is appropriate for it or not. If it is not appropriate for it, then the ruling is not applied here.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule (principle for muftis) regarding the role of custom ('urf) in fatwa. Ibn Abidin begins by asserting that a mufti must follow the prevailing custom of his time, both in verbal expressions and in rulings that were originally based on a certain custom. However, this is conditional upon the mufti possessing sound judgment and knowledge of Sharia rules to distinguish valid custom from invalid custom. He then quotes a critique of rigidity: clinging to transmitted texts without understanding their causes and ignoring custom leads to injustice. Ibn Abidin's statement is praised for its precision; such rigidity has isolated fiqh from Muslim life. He clarifies that the term 'urf in his usage encompasses broader principles of rasm al-mufti: necessity (darurah), facilitation (taysir), public interest (maslahah), and change of time. The most comprehensive principle is considering societal custom, leading to different rulings in different places and times. Ibn Abidin quotes al-Juwayni to emphasize that custom in transactions is essential for competence in fiqh. Custom operates in two functions: (1) understanding the speaker's intent—custom clarifies what words mean in context, e.g., 'meat' customarily refers to red meat, not poultry, affecting oath rulings. (2) determining the suitability of the locus for the legal cause—the ruling itself is fixed, but its application requires a suitable locus; custom helps identify that locus. The example of testimony illustrates: the ruling requires upright witnesses; custom helps define uprightness, and it changed from Abu Hanifa's time (people were upright) to the Sahibayn's time (investigation needed). Thus custom does not change Sharia rulings but identifies their application. Finally, he stresses that before applying any ruling, one must ascertain its cause and check if the locus is suitable; if not, the ruling does not apply.

Key Terms
العرف (al-'urf): Customary practice of people in a particular time and place, used to determine the intended meaning of words and the suitability of a locus for a legal cause.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The set of principles and guidelines that a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas, including consideration of custom, necessity, facilitation, and change of time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To change Sharia rulings according to time and place.
B) To deduce new rulings from people's practices.
C) To help understand the speaker's intent and determine the suitability of a locus for a legal cause.
D) To override clear Quranic texts when they conflict with people's habits.

Key Takeaway
Custom in fatwa operates solely as a tool to understand intent and apply causes, never to abrogate or alter Sharia rulings.
