Working with Weak Opinions in Fatwa
States the prohibition of acting on weak opinions and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on using weak opinions in fatwa and identify the exceptions when it is permissible.

Core Idea
Weak opinions are prohibited in fatwa except for necessity or by a qualified mujtahid.

The Hanafi school has a clear hierarchy of opinions: the preponderant (rajih) is the norm, and the outweighed (marjuh) is not to be used. But life brings pressing needs. This lesson unpacks the baseline rule, its consensus backing, and the carefully defined exceptions that allow a mufti to navigate difficult cases without caprice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
Read the first sentence: opinions and reports whose weakness is explicit or known from the scholars of tarjih are prohibited for action and fatwa. This is the default.
The prohibition is general; it applies to all weak opinions.
2
Recognize the authority backing the rule
Ibn Qutlubugha is quoted: 'Judgment and fatwa with what is outweighed (marjuh) is contrary to consensus (ijma).' This elevates the rule to a matter of scholarly agreement.
Consensus strengthens the prohibition; it is not merely a preferred view.
3
Identify the first exception: necessity for a layperson
Al-Uthmani's quote clarifies: if a person is afflicted by a pressing necessity (darurah), it is permissible for him to act for himself with a weak opinion. This is personal concession, not a blanket fatwa.
The exception is limited to the individual in need; a mufti cannot give fatwa with it for others without a similar necessity.
4
Identify the second exception: qualified mujtahid's preference
A faqih who is qualified to weigh opinions (tarjih) can prefer a weak opinion if he finds a valid reason: maslahah, urf, hajah, taysir, or darurah. This is not caprice but considered ijtihad.
This exception only applies to scholars capable of tarjih, not to every mufti.
5
Note the third exception: need for an opposing madhhab opinion
The text adds that it is permissible to act with an opinion from a different madhhab if there is need and necessity. The Hanafi scholars have explicitly stated this in specific issues.
This allows talfiq (combining opinions) under duress, but only as a last resort.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱) معناه : إن ما يوجد في كتب الفقه من أقوال وروايات ضعيفة صرح أصحاب الترجيح بضعفها أو عُلِمَ ضعفها بعباراتهم ضمناً والتزاماً ، فلا يجوز العمل عليها والإفتاء بها، قال ابن قُطلوبغا: «إن الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع». ينظر : رد المحتار ٥: ٤٠٨، وغيره. ولكن صرّح عدة من الفقهاء بأنه قد يجوز العمل أو الإفتاء برواية ضعيفة أو قول مرجوح لضرورة اقتضت ذلك، قال العثماني في أصول الإفتاء ص ٤٢ : وحاصل كلامهم أنه لا يجوز الأخذ بأقواله الضعيفة بالتشهي ولكن إذا ابتلي الرجل بضرورة ملحة وسع له أن يعمل لنفسه بقول ضعيف أو رواية مرجوحة». وكذلك يستثنى من عدم جواز العمل بالضعيف، من كان فقيهاً مجتهداً، وهو أهل للترجيح بين الأقوال في المذهب، فيتمكن أن يرجح القول الضعيف لما اتفق له من مصلحة أو عرف أو حاجة أو تيسير أو ضرورة. ويجوز العمل بقول المذهب المخالف إن حصلت حاجة وضرورة لذلك، وقد نص علماء المذهب على ذلك في بعض المسائل. ينظر : أصول الإفتاء ص ٥٢ .
(1) Its meaning: What is found in fiqh books of opinions and weak reports, whose weakness has been explicitly stated by the scholars of tarjih (preference) or known implicitly from their expressions and commitment, then it is not permissible to act upon them or give fatwa with them. Ibn Qutlubugha said: 'Judgment and fatwa with what is outweighed (marjuh) is contrary to consensus.' See: Radd al-Muhtar 5:408, etc. However, several jurists have stated that it may be permissible to act or give fatwa with a weak report or outweighed opinion due to a necessity that requires that. Al-Uthmani said in Usul al-Ifta p.42: 'The conclusion of their words is that it is not permissible to take his weak opinions capriciously, but if a person is afflicted by a pressing necessity, it is permissible for him to act for himself with a weak opinion or outweighed report.' Likewise, excluded from the prohibition of acting with the weak is one who is a knowledgeable jurist (faqih, mujtahid) who is qualified to weigh between opinions in the madhhab; he can prefer the weak opinion when he deems a benefit, custom, need, facilitation, or necessity. And it is permissible to act with the opinion of the opposing madhhab if there is a need and necessity for that; the scholars of the madhhab have explicitly stated this in some issues. See: Usul al-Ifta p.52.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a rasm rule concerning the use of weak or outweighed opinions in fatwa. The baseline rule is clear: opinions and reports that have been identified as weak or outweighed by the scholars of preference (tarjih) cannot be used for action or fatwa. Ibn Qutlubugha even states that doing so is contrary to consensus (ijma). However, the text then refines this rule by stating several exceptions. The first exception is necessity: if a person faces a pressing necessity, it is permissible for him to act (for himself) with a weak opinion. The second exception involves a qualified mujtahid within the Hanafi school: such a person can prefer a weak opinion if he finds a valid reason like benefit (maslahah), custom (urf), need (hajah), facilitation (taysir), or necessity (darurah). This is not mere caprice but a considered preference. Finally, the text adds that it is also permissible to act with an opinion from an opposing madhhab if there is genuine need or necessity. This shows the flexibility of the Hanafi tradition in accommodating practical difficulties while adhering to the general principle of avoiding weak rulings in normal circumstances.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The outweighed opinion in a school, deemed weaker than the preponderant (rajih) opinion.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of weighing evidence to determine which opinion is stronger (rajih) and which is weaker (marjuh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Whenever he prefers it.
B) If he is a knowledgeable scholar.
C) If he faces a pressing necessity.
D) Only if the weak opinion is from an opposing madhhab.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits fatwa with weak opinions unless there is necessity or the mufti is a qualified mujtahid with valid reasoning.

The Role of Custom in Identifying Legal Causes
Explaining that custom identifies the cause and suitability of the place for a ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two functions of custom ('urf) in Hanafi fatwa methodology and apply them to the example of witness testimony.

Core Idea
Custom does not change the ruling; it only identifies the cause and its presence in the subject.

In this passage, Ibn Abidin clarifies a crucial principle for muftis: custom ('urf) does not create or alter legal rulings, but it helps us apply them correctly. Before applying any ruling, we must identify its cause ('illah) and confirm that the subject (mahall) is suitable for that cause. Custom guides us in both tasks. The classic example is the requirement that a witness be 'adl (just) — the ruling is fixed by the Quran, but who qualifies as 'adl changes over time, and custom tells us when verification is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its cause
Pinpoint the hukm (e.g., acceptance of a just witness) and its 'illah (justice/'adalah). The passage uses Quran 2:282 as the source.
2
Understand the role of custom
Custom does not change the hukm but helps identify the 'illah and its presence in the mahall. Note the two functions: clarifying meaning and assessing suitability.
3
Apply to the example
Trace how custom operated differently in the time of Abu Hanifa (no tazkiyah needed) vs. the time of the Sahibayn (tazkiyah needed). The hukm remained the same; only the identification of 'adl changed.
4
Extract the methodological rule
Formulate the principle: 'Al-urf mu'arraf la musharrif' — custom is an identifier, not a changer. This is a rasm al-mufti foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يساعدنا على تطبيق ذلك، مثاله : أنَّ الحكم عدم قبول إلا شهادة العدل، كما شهد القرآن: ممن ترضون من الشهداء} [البقرة: ۲۸۲]، والعرف يُساعدنا في معرفة العدل، ففي زمن أبي حنيفة لم يحتج للتزكية في العدالة؛ لأنَّ النّاس عدول، وفي زمن الصاحبين تغيّرت أحوال الناس، فنحتاج لتحقق علّة الحكم من العدالة بالتزكية، فمن لم يكن عدلاً لا تقبل شهادته، هذا هو الحكم، ولكن كيف نتعرّف على العدالة، حيث أمكن ذلك بالعرف. وبالتالي لا يخرج العرف عن هذين المعنيين ،البتة، فلا يكون مغيّراً للحكم الشرعي أبداً، ولا تستنبط به الأحكام أيضاً، وإنَّما هو معرّف للحكم ببيان مقصود المتكلّم من كلامه، ومعرفة صلاحيّة المحل لعلّة الحكم.
وتَبيُّن أنَّ المحل صالح للحكم أمر مهم جداً؛ إذ نحتاج قبل تطبيق كل حكم أن نتعرّف على علته أولاً ثمّ ننظر هل المحل مناسب لها أم لا؟ فإن لم يكن مناسباً لها فإنَّ الحكم لا يطبق هنا.
It helps us to apply that, for example: the ruling is that the testimony of only the just person is accepted, as the Quran states: 'From those whom you approve among the witnesses' [al-Baqarah 2:282]. Custom helps us in knowing the just person. In the time of Abu Hanifa, there was no need for verification of justice because people were just. In the time of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the conditions of people changed, so we need to verify the cause of the ruling regarding justice through verification. So whoever is not just, his testimony is not accepted. This is the ruling. But how do we identify justice? That is possible through custom. Thus, custom does not depart from these two meanings at all. It never changes the legal ruling, nor are rulings derived from it. Rather, it is a definer of the ruling by clarifying the intended meaning of the speaker from his speech and knowing the suitability of the place (subject) for the cause of the ruling. And it is very important to ascertain that the place is suitable for the ruling; for before applying any ruling, we need to first identify its cause, then see whether the place is appropriate for it or not. If it is not appropriate for it, then the ruling is not applied here.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the methodological rule regarding the function of custom ('urf) in the process of fatwa and qada. The author establishes that custom is not a source that changes the divine ruling (hukm shar'i) nor does it derive new rulings. Rather, its role is limited to two functions: first, clarifying the intended meaning of the speaker (e.g., of the Lawgiver or of parties in contracts), and second, determining the suitability (salahiyyah) of the subject (mahall) for the application of the ruling's cause ('illah). The author illustrates this with the example of the requirement for the witness to be 'adl (just). The ruling is fixed by the Quran: only a just witness is accepted. However, the definition of 'adl changes with time and custom. In the time of Imam Abu Hanifa, people were generally just, so no verification was needed. Later, in the time of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, social conditions changed and verification (tazkiyah) became necessary. Custom here does not alter the ruling that only the just witness is accepted; it merely helps to identify who is just. The author emphasizes that before applying any ruling, one must first identify the cause (illah) and then verify if the subject (mahall) is suitable for that cause. If the subject lacks the required attribute, the ruling does not apply. This is a critical rasm al-mufti principle that guards against misapplication of rulings due to changing circumstances.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Custom that helps in identifying the intended meaning of the speaker and the suitability of the subject for the cause of the ruling.
علة الحكم (illat al-hukm): The legal cause or reason for a ruling, which must be present for the ruling to apply.
محل الحكم (mahall al-hukm): The subject or locus where the ruling is applied; its suitability for the 'illah must be verified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the function of custom ('urf) in relation to legal rulings?
A) It derives new rulings
B) It changes the ruling to suit the times
C) It identifies the intended meaning and the suitability of the subject for the cause
D) It is a source of legislation when the texts are silent

Key Takeaway
Custom identifies the presence of the cause and the meaning, but never changes the ruling itself.

The Muqallid Judge's Obligation to Follow the Stronger View
Ruling on judge's requirement to follow rajih view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that a muqallid judge must judge by the rajih view and identify the exception when the judge is not restricted to a specific madhhab.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge must judge by the rajih view; judgment by a weak opinion is void unless the ruler left him unrestricted on a debatable issue.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti outlines the binding rule for judges who are muqallids. It clarifies that a judge appointed with a condition to follow a specific madhhab cannot rely on weak opinions. However, if no restriction is placed, his judgment on ijtihadi matters stands even if it contradicts his madhhab. Understanding this rule is crucial for both judges and muftis in validating judicial decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
What is the judge required to follow? The passage states that the judge only judges by the preponderant (rajih) view in the madhhab of his Imam.
The rule is absolute for a muqallid judge.
2
Note the consequence of violating the rule
If he judges by a weak narration or contrary to the madhhab, his judgment is not executed.
Invalidity of judgment is the consequence.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios based on the appointing condition
The rule applies when the judge is restricted by the ruler to a specific madhhab. If no restriction is placed, the judgment may be executed.
Condition matters: restriction vs. no restriction.
4
Understand the exception
If the judge is not restricted and the issue is subject to ijtihad, his judgment contrary to his madhhab is executed.
Exception: ijtihadi issues, no restriction.
5
Recognize the limitation of a known maxim
The idea that a weak opinion is strengthened by a judge's ruling only applies to a mujtahid judge, not a muqallid.
Prevents misapplication of the maxim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخاتمة: ونصَّ الفقهاء على أنّ القاضي لا يقضي إلا بالراجح في مذهب إمامه ولا يجوز له أن يحكم برواية ضعيفة أو بما خالف المذهب، فإن قضى برواية ضعيفة أو بقول غير الإمام لم ينفذ قضاؤه، ولكن هذا مختص بالقاضي الذي قلّده الإمام بشرط أن يحكم بمذهب أبي حنيفة؛ لأنَّه معزول في القضاء بغير مذهبه، فأما إذا لم يقيده الإمام المقلّد بمذهب بعينه فقضى بما خالف المذهب نفذ قضاؤه ما دامت المسألة مجتهداً فيها. قال ابن قطلوبغا: «وليس للقاضي المقلد أن يحكم بالضعيف لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل ولو حكم لا ينفذ; لأنَّ قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق; لأنَّ الحق هو الصحيح وما وقع مِنْ أنَّ القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به: قضاء المجتهد كما بين في موضعه . ينظر : رد المحتار ٥: ٤٠٨ ، وشرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٥٢، وغيرهما. وقال ابن الغرس: «وأما المقلّد المحض فلا يقضي إلا بما عليه العمل والفتوى». وقال ابن نجيم: «أما القاضي المقلد فليس له الحكم إلا بالصحيح المفتى به في مذهبه ولا ينفذ قضاؤه بالقول الضعيف». ينظر : رد المحتار ٥: ٤٠٨، وغيره.
Conclusion: The jurists have explicitly stated that the judge only judges by the preponderant (rajih) view in the madhhab of his Imam, and it is not permissible for him to judge by a weak narration or by what contradicts the madhhab. If he judges by a weak narration or by a saying of other than the Imam, his judgment is not executed. But this is specific to the judge whom the Imam (ruler) appointed with the condition that he judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, because he is dismissed from judging by other than his madhhab. As for if the appointing Imam did not restrict him to a particular madhhab, and he judged contrary to the madhhab, his judgment is executed as long as the issue is subject to ijtihad. Ibn Qutlubugha said: 'It is not for the muqallid judge to judge by the weak, because he is not from the people of tarjih, so he should not deviate from the correct unless for an unworthy purpose, and if he judges it is not executed, because his judgment is a judgment without truth, for the truth is what is correct. And what has been said that the weak opinion is strengthened by the judgment is meant by the judgment of a mujtahid, as explained in its place. See Radd al-Muhtar 5:408, and Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p.52, etc.' Ibn al-Ghars said: 'As for the pure muqallid, he judges only by what is acted upon and issued as fatwa.' Ibn Nujaym said: 'As for the muqallid judge, he only has the right to judge by the correct view that is issued as fatwa in his madhhab, and his judgment by a weak view is not executed.' See Radd al-Muhtar 5:408, etc.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on the judge's role. It establishes that a judge who is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) is bound to judge only by the preponderant (rajih) view within his madhhab. If he judges by a weak opinion, the judgment is invalid and not executed. However, this applies only when the appointing authority has restricted him to a specific madhhab. If no restriction is placed, and the issue is debatable among mujtahids, his judgment is valid even if it contradicts his own madhhab. The passage quotes Ibn Qutlubugha who clarifies that the concept of a weak opinion gaining strength through a judge's ruling applies only to a mujtahid judge, not a muqallid. Ibn al-Ghars and Ibn Nujaym affirm that a muqallid judge must follow the relied-upon fatwa in his madhhab. This is a critical rasm rule for the judiciary in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
المقلد المحض (al-muqallid al-mahd): A judge who is a pure follower (muqallid) without the ability to weigh evidence or perform ijtihad.
القول الضعيف (al-qawl al-da'if): A weak opinion within the madhhab that is not relied upon for fatwa or judicial decision.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant or stronger view within a madhhab, based on evidence and authority.
التقاضي بالضعيف (al-taqāḍī bi-al-ḍa'īf): Judging by a weak opinion, which is prohibited for a muqallid judge.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge must adhere to the rajih view; only when unrestricted and on ijtihadi matters can he depart from his madhhab and his judgment remains valid.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
The Muqallid Judge: Only the Rajih Opinion
Stating the ruling on a muqallid judge's use of weak opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for validity of a muqallid judge's judgment and apply the rule that weak opinions do not become enforceable through his ruling.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge may only judge by the preponderant opinion of his madhhab; weak opinions remain weak regardless of his ruling.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti lays down a foundational rule for judges who are not mujtahids. It clarifies the limits of a muqallid judge's authority: he must adhere to the preponderant (rajih) opinion within his school and cannot rely on weak transmissions. However, there is a crucial exception when the appointing authority does not restrict him to a specific madhhab. Understanding this distinction is essential for both judges and muftis in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its core prohibition
The text begins by stating that a judge (al-qadi) must judge only by the preponderant (al-rajih) opinion in the madhhab of his imam. It explicitly prohibits judging by a weak transmission (riwaya da'ifa) or by an opinion that contradicts the madhhab. The consequence: such a judgment is not executed (la yanfudh).
The prohibition applies to any muqallid judge, not just Hanafis.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios based on appointment conditions
Ibn Abidin then introduces a conditional: the above rule applies specifically when the appointing authority (imam al-muqallid) has appointed the judge with the condition that he judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. In that case, the judge is considered 'dismissed' (ma'zul) from judging by other madhhabs, so his judgment outside Hanafi is void. If no such restriction exists, and the judge rules by a different madhhab opinion that is a matter of ijtihad, his judgment is valid.
This distinction is critical for understanding the scope of the rule.
3
Examine the rationale from Ibn Qutlubugha
Ibn Qutlubugha explains that a muqallid judge is not among the people of tarjih (preponderance). He should not deviate from the correct opinion except for an unseemly purpose. The idea that a weak opinion becomes strong by being judged (by a mujtahid) does not apply to the muqallid.
Tarjih requires ijtihad, which a muqallid lacks.
4
Apply the supporting quotes from later Hanafi authorities
Ibn al-Ghars and Ibn Nujaym confirm that a pure muqallid (muqallid mahd) must judge only by what is acted upon (ma 'alayhi al-'amal) and issued as fatwa (al-mufta bihi). The weak opinion is not a valid basis for judgment.
These quotes reinforce the rule that the mufta bihi opinion is the only valid source for a muqallid judge.
5
Synthesize the practical takeaway
In practice, when a muqallid judge issues a judgment based on a weak narration, the judgment is void and not enforceable. The judge's ruling does not alter the weakness of the opinion. Only a mujtahid's ruling can potentially strengthen a weak opinion, and even that is specific to the case.
This rule upholds the integrity of the madhhab's authoritative positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصَّ الفقهاء على أنّ القاضي لا يقضي إلا بالراجح في مذهب إمامه ولا يجوز له أن يحكم برواية ضعيفة أو بما خالف المذهب، فإن قضى برواية ضعيفة أو بقول غير الإمام لم ينفذ قضاؤه، ولكن هذا مختص بالقاضي الذي قلّده الإمام بشرط أن يحكم بمذهب أبي حنيفة؛ لأنَّه معزول في القضاء بغير مذهبه، فأما إذا لم يقيده الإمام المقلّد بمذهب بعينه فقضى بما خالف المذهب نفذ قضاؤه ما دامت المسألة مجتهداً فيها. قال ابن قطلوبغا: «وليس للقاضي المقلد أن يحكم بالضعيف لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل ولو حكم لا ينفذ; لأنَّ قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق; لأنَّ الحق هو الصحيح وما وقع مِنْ أنَّ القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به: قضاء المجتهد كما بين في موضعه . ينظر : رد المحتار ٥: ٤٠٨ ، وشرح عقود رسم المفتي ص ٥٢، وغيرهما. وقال ابن الغرس: «وأما المقلّد المحض فلا يقضي إلا بما عليه العمل والفتوى». وقال ابن نجيم: «أما القاضي المقلد فليس له الحكم إلا بالصحيح المفتى به في مذهبه ولا ينفذ قضاؤه بالقول الضعيف». ينظر : رد المحتار ٥: ٤٠٨، وغيره.
The jurists have stated that the judge does not judge except by the preponderant (opinion) in the madhhab of his imam, and it is not permissible for him to rule by a weak transmission or by what contradicts the madhhab. If he judges by a weak transmission or by a saying of other than the imam, his judgment is not executed. But this is specific to the judge whom the imam has appointed as a muqallid, on condition that he judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, because he is dismissed from judging by other than his madhhab. As for when the appointing imam does not restrict him to a particular madhhab, and he judges by what contradicts the madhhab, his judgment is executed as long as the issue is one of ijtihad. Ibn Qutlubugha said: 'It is not for the muqallid judge to judge by the weak, because he is not among the people of tarjih (preponderance), so he should not deviate from the correct except for an unseemly purpose. If he judges, it is not executed, because his judgment is a judgment by other than the truth, for the truth is the correct. And what has been mentioned that the weak opinion becomes strong by being judged by, what is meant by that is the judgment of the mujtahid, as clarified in its place. See Radd al-Muhtar 5:408 and Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti p.52 and others.' Ibn al-Ghars said: 'As for the pure muqallid, he does not judge except by that which is acted upon and issued as fatwa.' Ibn Nujaym said: 'As for the muqallid judge, he is not to rule except by the correct (opinion) that is issued as fatwa in his madhhab, and his judgment by the weak opinion is not executed.' See Radd al-Muhtar 5:408 and others.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a rasm rule from the conclusion of Ibn Abidin's work. It lays down the foundational principle for muqallid judges regarding which opinions they may rely upon in their judgments. The jurists (الفقهاء) are unanimous that a judge who is a muqallid (follower of a madhhab) must only judge by the preponderant (راجح) opinion within his imam's madhhab. He is not permitted to rule based on a weak transmission (رواية ضعيفة) or any opinion that contradicts the established madhhab. If he does so, his judgment is not executed (لا ينفذ). However, Ibn Abidin introduces an important distinction: this restriction applies only to a judge who has been appointed (قلده الإمام) by the political authority specifically on the condition that he judge by the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. Such a judge is considered 'dismissed' (معزول) from judging by any other madhhab, so his verdict outside the Hanafi madhhab is void. The exception is when the appointing authority did not restrict the judge to a particular madhhab; in that case, if the judge rules by an opinion that contradicts the Hanafi madhhab, his judgment is valid as long as the issue is one of ijtihad (i.e., there is room for scholarly disagreement). Ibn Abidin then supports this with quotes from later Hanafi authorities: Ibn Qutlubugha emphasizes that a muqallid judge is not qualified to weigh evidences (ليس من أهل الترجيح), so he must stick to the correct opinion. The notion that a weak opinion becomes strong by being upheld in a judgment is only applicable to a mujtahid judge, not a muqallid. Ibn al-Ghars and Ibn Nujaym reiterate that a muqallid judge can only act upon the opinion that is relied upon for practice and fatwa (ما عليه العمل والفتوى). This passage is crucial for understanding the limits of judicial authority in the Hanafi tradition and the hierarchy of opinions.

Key Terms
القاضي المقلد (al-qadi al-muqallid): A judge who follows a specific madhhab (here Hanafi) and is not qualified for independent ijtihad.
الراجح (al-rajih): The preponderant opinion within the madhhab, identified by later scholars as the one that is acted upon and given fatwa.
الرواية الضعيفة (al-riwaya al-da'ifa): A transmission from the founding imams (abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) that is considered weak or less authentic, not relied upon for practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is valid but makruh.
B) It is not executed (la yanfudh).
C) It becomes strong and enforceable.
D) It is valid only if the litigants agree.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge's authority is limited to the preponderant opinion; he cannot elevate weak opinions through his judgment.

The Indispensable Role of Rasm al-Mufti in Hanafi Ifta
Conclusion of a study on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six findings presented in the study and explain why the science of Rasm al-Mufti is essential for tarjih and the application of fiqh to real life.

Core Idea
Rasm al-Mufti bridges fiqh texts and reality—without it, fatwa is blind.

This lesson examines a modern academic study that highlights the critical importance of the Hanafi science of Rasm al-Mufti. The study, by Professor Salah Abu al-Haj, presents six key findings about the unique poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by Ibn Abidin and the science it represents. As you read, consider why this science has been both neglected and indispensable, and how its absence has contributed to the theoretical turn in contemporary fiqh.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the work and its significance
Locate the finding that describes 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' as the only poetic composition in its field and the broadest collection of Usul al-Ifta rules.
This establishes the unique status of Ibn Abidin's contribution.
2
2. Understand the definition of Rasm al-Mufti
Extract the study's description of Rasm al-Mufti as 'the science of applied fiqh' that connects written rulings to lived reality.
Focus on the phrase 'al-halqah ma bayna al-masa'il al-fiqhiyyah wa al-waqi''.
3
3. Trace the historical transmission shift
Note how the study explains that early scholars transmitted this science orally, while later scholars wrote about it due to increased disagreement.
This explains the relative scarcity of written works in earlier times.
4
4. Recognize the consequences of neglect
Identify the study's claim that neglect of Rasm al-Mufti has led to fiqh becoming a theoretical science in modern domains.
The study lists economic, social, political, military, and judicial spheres.
5
5. Summarize the indispensable functions
Synthesize the final finding: tarjih, understanding madhhab disagreement, and applying fiqh to reality all require Rasm al-Mufti.
This is the core argument for why this science demands greater attention.

للأستاذ الدكتور صلاح أبو الحاج.
وفي نهاية البحث توصلت لهذه النتائج ولخصتها في النقاط الآتية: ١ . عقود رسم المفتي لخاتمة المحققين ابن عابدين هي المنظومة الوحيدة في علم رسم المفتي عند الحنفية، وهي أوسع ما جمع من مسائل وقواعد علم أصول الإفتاء، ولم يتسنّ لأحدٍ أن يجمع مسائل علم الرسم ويرتبها كما فعل ابن عابدين حيث جمعها في هذه المنظومة وشرحها، وجمع ما تفرّق في الكتب من أسس هذا العلم.
٢ . صحة ثبوت المنظومة لابن عابدين واسمها هو: عقود رسم المفتي ٣ . علم الرسم هو علم تطبيق الفقه، وهو أحد مكونات الملكة الفقهيّة التي يقدر بها المرء على فهم الفقه ومعايشته وتعليمه والإفتاء به، وهو يُمثل الحلقة ما بين المسائل الفقهيّة المدوّنة في الكتب وما بين الواقع المعاش للنّاس في كافة مناحي الحياة، وقواعده هي الأصول التي يرجع إليها المجتهد في المذهب في التخريج والترجيح والإفتاء.
٤. قلة الكتابة في علم الرسم أنَّه كان عند سلفنا الصالح يتلقاه الطالبُ من أستاذه بالمصاحبة بدون أن يقرأ فيه شيئاً، فيحصل له بالتجربة والملازمة للشيخ، أما بعد توسّع العلوم، وكثرة الاختلاف أكثر مما كان عليه المتقدمين، صار المتأخرين يصرحون به كثيراً في مؤلفاتهم.
ه. إنَّ هذا التّراجعَ الذي حَصَلَ لعلم الفقه في هذا الزمان حتى أصبح علماً نظرياً في حياتنا الاقتصادية والاجتماعية والسياسية والعسكرية والقضائيّة عائد لأمور منها إهمال علم رسم المفتي. ٦ . رسم المفتي ينبغي أن ينال اهتماماً كبيراً من المشتغلين في الفقه، فلا سبيل لنا للترجيح بين الأقوال الفقهيّة إلا به، ولا فهم الخلاف الحاصل بين علماء المذهب إلا من خلاله، ولا إعمال الفقه في الواقع بدونه.
By Professor Dr. Salah Abu al-Haj. At the end of the research, I arrived at these results and summarized them in the following points: 1. The poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti' by the seal of the verifiers Ibn Abidin is the only poem in the science of Rasm al-Mufti among the Hanafis, and it is the broadest collection of issues and rules of the science of Usul al-Ifta, and no one has been able to collect the issues of the science of al-Rasm and arrange them as Ibn Abidin did, as he collected them in this poem and its commentary, and gathered what was scattered in books of the foundations of this science. 2. The poem's attribution to Ibn Abidin is established, and its name is 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. 3. The science of al-Rasm is the science of applied fiqh, and it is one of the components of the juristic faculty by which one is able to understand fiqh, live it, teach it, and issue fatwas with it. It represents the link between the fiqh issues recorded in books and the lived reality of people in all aspects of life. Its rules are the principles to which the mujtahid in the madhhab refers for takhrij, tarjih, and ifta. 4. The scarcity of writing in the science of al-Rasm is because among our righteous predecessors, the student would receive it from his teacher through accompaniment without reading anything about it, so he would acquire it through experience and constant association with the shaykh. But after the expansion of the sciences and the increase of disagreement more than was the case with the earlier scholars, the later scholars began to state it explicitly in their writings. E. Indeed, this regression that has occurred in the science of fiqh in this time until it became a theoretical science in our economic, social, political, military, and judicial spheres is due to several factors, including neglect of the science of Rasm al-Mufti. 6. Rasm al-Mufti must receive great attention from those engaged in fiqh, for we have no way to give tarjih between juristic opinions except through it, nor to understand the disagreement among the scholars of the madhhab except through it, nor to apply fiqh to reality without it.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a conclusion from a modern academic study on Ibn Abidin's poem 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti'. It presents six key findings regarding the significance and nature of the science of Rasm al-Mufti. The study emphasizes that this science, unique to the Hanafi school as formally codified by Ibn Abidin, serves as the bridge between abstract fiqh rules and their application in real life. It notes that early scholars transmitted this science orally through companionship, but later scholars began writing about it due to increased differences. The study argues that the decline of fiqh as a practical science in modern times is partly due to neglect of Rasm al-Mufti, and that this science is indispensable for tarjih (preferring one opinion over another) and for understanding intra-madhhab disagreement. The passage does not present specific legal rulings but rather underscores the methodological importance of the discipline.

Key Terms
عقود رسم المفتي (Uqud Rasm al-Mufti): The only poetic composition in the science of Rasm al-Mufti among the Hanafis, authored by Ibn Abidin, collecting rules and issues of Usul al-Ifta.
رسم المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): The science of applied fiqh that links written fiqh rules to real-life situations, essential for issuing fatwas and tarjih.
أصول الإفتاء (Usul al-Ifta): The foundational principles for issuing fatwas, including rules of tarjih, taqlid, and dealing with conflicting opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the study, why did later Hanafi scholars begin writing explicitly about Rasm al-Mufti?
A) Because earlier scholars were unable to transmit it orally.
B) Because the expansion of sciences and increase of disagreement made written transmission necessary.
C) Because Ibn Abidin forced them to write commentaries.
D) Because the science was newly invented in their time.

Key Takeaway
Rasm al-Mufti is the bridge between fiqh theory and practice; its study is essential for any mufti seeking to issue sound and relevant fatwas.
